001686 "'What, the red-headed man?'
001687 
001688 "'Yes.'
001689 
001690 "'Oh,' said he, 'his name was William Morris. He was a solicitor
001691 and was using my room as a temporary convenience until his new
001692 premises were ready. He moved out yesterday.'
001693 
001694 "'Where could I find him?'
001695 
001696 "'Oh, at his new offices. He did tell me the address. Yes, 17
001697 King Edward Street, near St. Paul's.'
001698 
001699 "I started off, Mr. Holmes, but when I got to that address it was
001700 a manufactory of artificial knee-caps, and no one in it had ever
001701 heard of either Mr. William Morris or Mr. Duncan Ross."
001702 
001703 "And what did you do then?" asked Holmes.
001704 
001705 "I went home to Saxe-Coburg Square, and I took the advice of my
001706 assistant. But he could not help me in any way. He could only say
001707 that if I waited I should hear by post. But that was not quite
001708 good enough, Mr. Holmes. I did not wish to lose such a place
001709 without a struggle, so, as I had heard that you were good enough
001710 to give advice to poor folk who were in need of it, I came right
001711 away to you."
001712 
001713 "And you did very wisely," said Holmes. "Your case is an
001714 exceedingly remarkable one, and I shall be happy to look into it.
001715 From what you have told me I think that it is possible that
001716 graver issues hang from it than might at first sight appear."
001717 
001718 "Grave enough!" said Mr. Jabez Wilson. "Why, I have lost four
001719 pound a week."
001720 
001721 "As far as you are personally concerned," remarked Holmes, "I do
001722 not see that you have any grievance against this extraordinary
001723 league. On the contrary, you are, as I understand, richer by some
001724 30 pounds, to say nothing of the minute knowledge which you have
001725 gained on every subject which comes under the letter A. You have
001726 lost nothing by them."
001727 
001728 "No, sir. But I want to find out about them, and who they are,
001729 and what their object was in playing this prank--if it was a
001730 prank--upon me. It was a pretty expensive joke for them, for it
001731 cost them two and thirty pounds."
001732 
001733 "We shall endeavour to clear up these points for you. And, first,
001734 one or two questions, Mr. Wilson. This assistant of yours who
001735 first called your attention to the advertisement--how long had he
001736 been with you?"
001737 
001738 "About a month then."
001739 
001740 "How did he come?"
001741 
001742 "In answer to an advertisement."
001743 
001744 "Was he the only applicant?"
001745 
001746 "No, I had a dozen."
001747 
001748 "Why did you pick him?"
001749 
001750 "Because he was handy and would come cheap."
001751 
001752 "At half-wages, in fact."
001753 
001754 "Yes."
001755 
001756 "What is he like, this Vincent Spaulding?"
001757 
001758 "Small, stout-built, very quick in his ways, no hair on his face,
001759 though he's not short of thirty. Has a white splash of acid upon
001760 his forehead."
001761 
001762 Holmes sat up in his chair in considerable excitement. "I thought
001763 as much," said he. "Have you ever observed that his ears are
001764 pierced for earrings?"
001765 
001766 "Yes, sir. He told me that a gipsy had done it for him when he
001767 was a lad."
001768 
001769 "Hum!" said Holmes, sinking back in deep thought. "He is still
001770 with you?"
001771 
001772 "Oh, yes, sir; I have only just left him."
001773 
001774 "And has your business been attended to in your absence?"
001775 
001776 "Nothing to complain of, sir. There's never very much to do of a
001777 morning."
001778 
001779 "That will do, Mr. Wilson. I shall be happy to give you an
001780 opinion upon the subject in the course of a day or two. To-day is
001781 Saturday, and I hope that by Monday we may come to a conclusion."
001782 
001783 "Well, Watson," said Holmes when our visitor had left us, "what
001784 do you make of it all?"
001785 
001786 "I make nothing of it," I answered frankly. "It is a most
001787 mysterious business."
001788 
001789 "As a rule," said Holmes, "the more bizarre a thing is the less
001790 mysterious it proves to be. It is your commonplace, featureless
001791 crimes which are really puzzling, just as a commonplace face is
001792 the most difficult to identify. But I must be prompt over this
001793 matter."
001794 
001795 "What are you going to do, then?" I asked.
001796 
001797 "To smoke," he answered. "It is quite a three pipe problem, and I
001798 beg that you won't speak to me for fifty minutes." He curled
001799 himself up in his chair, with his thin knees drawn up to his
001800 hawk-like nose, and there he sat with his eyes closed and his
001801 black clay pipe thrusting out like the bill of some strange bird.
001802 I had come to the conclusion that he had dropped asleep, and
001803 indeed was nodding myself, when he suddenly sprang out of his
001804 chair with the gesture of a man who has made up his mind and put
001805 his pipe down upon the mantelpiece.
001806 
001807 "Sarasate plays at the St. James's Hall this afternoon," he
001808 remarked. "What do you think, Watson? Could your patients spare
001809 you for a few hours?"
001810 
001811 "I have nothing to do to-day. My practice is never very
001812 absorbing."
001813 
001814 "Then put on your hat and come. I am going through the City
001815 first, and we can have some lunch on the way. I observe that
001816 there is a good deal of German music on the programme, which is
001817 rather more to my taste than Italian or French. It is
001818 introspective, and I want to introspect. Come along!"
001819 
001820 We travelled by the Underground as far as Aldersgate; and a short
001821 walk took us to Saxe-Coburg Square, the scene of the singular
001822 story which we had listened to in the morning. It was a poky,
001823 little, shabby-genteel place, where four lines of dingy
001824 two-storied brick houses looked out into a small railed-in
001825 enclosure, where a lawn of weedy grass and a few clumps of faded
001826 laurel-bushes made a hard fight against a smoke-laden and
001827 uncongenial atmosphere. Three gilt balls and a brown board with
001828 "JABEZ WILSON" in white letters, upon a corner house, announced
001829 the place where our red-headed client carried on his business.
001830 Sherlock Holmes stopped in front of it with his head on one side
001831 and looked it all over, with his eyes shining brightly between
001832 puckered lids. Then he walked slowly up the street, and then down
001833 again to the corner, still looking keenly at the houses. Finally
001834 he returned to the pawnbroker's, and, having thumped vigorously
001835 upon the pavement with his stick two or three times, he went up
001836 to the door and knocked. It was instantly opened by a
001837 bright-looking, clean-shaven young fellow, who asked him to step
001838 in.
001839 
001840 "Thank you," said Holmes, "I only wished to ask you how you would
001841 go from here to the Strand."
001842 
001843 "Third right, fourth left," answered the assistant promptly,
001844 closing the door.
001845 
001846 "Smart fellow, that," observed Holmes as we walked away. "He is,
001847 in my judgment, the fourth smartest man in London, and for daring
001848 I am not sure that he has not a claim to be third. I have known
001849 something of him before."
001850 
001851 "Evidently," said I, "Mr. Wilson's assistant counts for a good
001852 deal in this mystery of the Red-headed League. I am sure that you
001853 inquired your way merely in order that you might see him."
001854 
001855 "Not him."
001856 
001857 "What then?"
001858 
001859 "The knees of his trousers."
001860 
001861 "And what did you see?"
001862 
001863 "What I expected to see."
001864 
001865 "Why did you beat the pavement?"
001866 
001867 "My dear doctor, this is a time for observation, not for talk. We
001868 are spies in an enemy's country. We know something of Saxe-Coburg
001869 Square. Let us now explore the parts which lie behind it."
001870 
001871 The road in which we found ourselves as we turned round the
001872 corner from the retired Saxe-Coburg Square presented as great a
001873 contrast to it as the front of a picture does to the back. It was
001874 one of the main arteries which conveyed the traffic of the City
001875 to the north and west. The roadway was blocked with the immense
001876 stream of commerce flowing in a double tide inward and outward,
001877 while the footpaths were black with the hurrying swarm of
001878 pedestrians. It was difficult to realise as we looked at the line
001879 of fine shops and stately business premises that they really
001880 abutted on the other side upon the faded and stagnant square
001881 which we had just quitted.
001882 
001883 "Let me see," said Holmes, standing at the corner and glancing
001884 along the line, "I should like just to remember the order of the
001885 houses here. It is a hobby of mine to have an exact knowledge of
001886 London. There is Mortimer's, the tobacconist, the little
001887 newspaper shop, the Coburg branch of the City and Suburban Bank,
001888 the Vegetarian Restaurant, and McFarlane's carriage-building
001889 depot. That carries us right on to the other block. And now,
001890 Doctor, we've done our work, so it's time we had some play. A
001891 sandwich and a cup of coffee, and then off to violin-land, where
001892 all is sweetness and delicacy and harmony, and there are no
001893 red-headed clients to vex us with their conundrums."
001894 
001895 My friend was an enthusiastic musician, being himself not only a
001896 very capable performer but a composer of no ordinary merit. All
001897 the afternoon he sat in the stalls wrapped in the most perfect
001898 happiness, gently waving his long, thin fingers in time to the
001899 music, while his gently smiling face and his languid, dreamy eyes
001900 were as unlike those of Holmes the sleuth-hound, Holmes the
001901 relentless, keen-witted, ready-handed criminal agent, as it was
001902 possible to conceive. In his singular character the dual nature
001903 alternately asserted itself, and his extreme exactness and
001904 astuteness represented, as I have often thought, the reaction
001905 against the poetic and contemplative mood which occasionally
001906 predominated in him. The swing of his nature took him from
001907 extreme languor to devouring energy; and, as I knew well, he was
001908 never so truly formidable as when, for days on end, he had been
001909 lounging in his armchair amid his improvisations and his
001910 black-letter editions. Then it was that the lust of the chase
001911 would suddenly come upon him, and that his brilliant reasoning
001912 power would rise to the level of intuition, until those who were
001913 unacquainted with his methods would look askance at him as on a
001914 man whose knowledge was not that of other mortals. When I saw him
001915 that afternoon so enwrapped in the music at St. James's Hall I
001916 felt that an evil time might be coming upon those whom he had set
001917 himself to hunt down.
001918 
001919 "You want to go home, no doubt, Doctor," he remarked as we
001920 emerged.
001921 
001922 "Yes, it would be as well."
001923 
001924 "And I have some business to do which will take some hours. This
001925 business at Coburg Square is serious."
001926 
001927 "Why serious?"
001928 
001929 "A considerable crime is in contemplation. I have every reason to
001930 believe that we shall be in time to stop it. But to-day being
001931 Saturday rather complicates matters. I shall want your help
001932 to-night."
001933 
001934 "At what time?"
001935 
001936 "Ten will be early enough."
001937 
001938 "I shall be at Baker Street at ten."
001939 
001940 "Very well. And, I say, Doctor, there may be some little danger,
001941 so kindly put your army revolver in your pocket." He waved his
001942 hand, turned on his heel, and disappeared in an instant among the
001943 crowd.
001944 
001945 I trust that I am not more dense than my neighbours, but I was
001946 always oppressed with a sense of my own stupidity in my dealings
001947 with Sherlock Holmes. Here I had heard what he had heard, I had
001948 seen what he had seen, and yet from his words it was evident that
001949 he saw clearly not only what had happened but what was about to
001950 happen, while to me the whole business was still confused and
001951 grotesque. As I drove home to my house in Kensington I thought
001952 over it all, from the extraordinary story of the red-headed
001953 copier of the "Encyclopaedia" down to the visit to Saxe-Coburg
001954 Square, and the ominous words with which he had parted from me.
001955 What was this nocturnal expedition, and why should I go armed?
001956 Where were we going, and what were we to do? I had the hint from
001957 Holmes that this smooth-faced pawnbroker's assistant was a
001958 formidable man--a man who might play a deep game. I tried to
001959 puzzle it out, but gave it up in despair and set the matter aside
001960 until night should bring an explanation.
001961 
001962 It was a quarter-past nine when I started from home and made my
001963 way across the Park, and so through Oxford Street to Baker
001964 Street. Two hansoms were standing at the door, and as I entered
001965 the passage I heard the sound of voices from above. On entering
001966 his room I found Holmes in animated conversation with two men,
001967 one of whom I recognised as Peter Jones, the official police
001968 agent, while the other was a long, thin, sad-faced man, with a
001969 very shiny hat and oppressively respectable frock-coat.
001970 
001971 "Ha! Our party is complete," said Holmes, buttoning up his
001972 pea-jacket and taking his heavy hunting crop from the rack.
001973 "Watson, I think you know Mr. Jones, of Scotland Yard? Let me
001974 introduce you to Mr. Merryweather, who is to be our companion in
001975 to-night's adventure."
001976 
001977 "We're hunting in couples again, Doctor, you see," said Jones in
001978 his consequential way. "Our friend here is a wonderful man for
001979 starting a chase. All he wants is an old dog to help him to do
001980 the running down."
001981 
001982 "I hope a wild goose may not prove to be the end of our chase,"
001983 observed Mr. Merryweather gloomily.
001984 
001985 "You may place considerable confidence in Mr. Holmes, sir," said
001986 the police agent loftily. "He has his own little methods, which
001987 are, if he won't mind my saying so, just a little too theoretical
001988 and fantastic, but he has the makings of a detective in him. It
001989 is not too much to say that once or twice, as in that business of
001990 the Sholto murder and the Agra treasure, he has been more nearly
001991 correct than the official force."
001992 
001993 "Oh, if you say so, Mr. Jones, it is all right," said the
001994 stranger with deference. "Still, I confess that I miss my rubber.
001995 It is the first Saturday night for seven-and-twenty years that I
001996 have not had my rubber."
001997 
001998 "I think you will find," said Sherlock Holmes, "that you will
001999 play for a higher stake to-night than you have ever done yet, and
002000 that the play will be more exciting. For you, Mr. Merryweather,
002001 the stake will be some 30,000 pounds; and for you, Jones, it will
002002 be the man upon whom you wish to lay your hands."
002003 
002004 "John Clay, the murderer, thief, smasher, and forger. He's a
002005 young man, Mr. Merryweather, but he is at the head of his
002006 profession, and I would rather have my bracelets on him than on
002007 any criminal in London. He's a remarkable man, is young John
002008 Clay. His grandfather was a royal duke, and he himself has been
002009 to Eton and Oxford. His brain is as cunning as his fingers, and
002010 though we meet signs of him at every turn, we never know where to
002011 find the man himself. He'll crack a crib in Scotland one week,
002012 and be raising money to build an orphanage in Cornwall the next.
002013 I've been on his track for years and have never set eyes on him
002014 yet."
002015 
002016 "I hope that I may have the pleasure of introducing you to-night.
002017 I've had one or two little turns also with Mr. John Clay, and I
002018 agree with you that he is at the head of his profession. It is
002019 past ten, however, and quite time that we started. If you two
002020 will take the first hansom, Watson and I will follow in the
002021 second."
002022 
002023 Sherlock Holmes was not very communicative during the long drive
002024 and lay back in the cab humming the tunes which he had heard in
002025 the afternoon. We rattled through an endless labyrinth of gas-lit
002026 streets until we emerged into Farrington Street.
002027 
002028 "We are close there now," my friend remarked. "This fellow
002029 Merryweather is a bank director, and personally interested in the
002030 matter. I thought it as well to have Jones with us also. He is
002031 not a bad fellow, though an absolute imbecile in his profession.
002032 He has one positive virtue. He is as brave as a bulldog and as
002033 tenacious as a lobster if he gets his claws upon anyone. Here we
002034 are, and they are waiting for us."
002035 
002036 We had reached the same crowded thoroughfare in which we had
002037 found ourselves in the morning. Our cabs were dismissed, and,
002038 following the guidance of Mr. Merryweather, we passed down a
002039 narrow passage and through a side door, which he opened for us.
002040 Within there was a small corridor, which ended in a very massive
002041 iron gate. This also was opened, and led down a flight of winding
002042 stone steps, which terminated at another formidable gate. Mr.
002043 Merryweather stopped to light a lantern, and then conducted us
002044 down a dark, earth-smelling passage, and so, after opening a
002045 third door, into a huge vault or cellar, which was piled all
002046 round with crates and massive boxes.
002047 
002048 "You are not very vulnerable from above," Holmes remarked as he
002049 held up the lantern and gazed about him.
002050 
002051 "Nor from below," said Mr. Merryweather, striking his stick upon
002052 the flags which lined the floor. "Why, dear me, it sounds quite
002053 hollow!" he remarked, looking up in surprise.
002054 
002055 "I must really ask you to be a little more quiet!" said Holmes
002056 severely. "You have already imperilled the whole success of our
002057 expedition. Might I beg that you would have the goodness to sit
002058 down upon one of those boxes, and not to interfere?"
002059 
002060 The solemn Mr. Merryweather perched himself upon a crate, with a
002061 very injured expression upon his face, while Holmes fell upon his
002062 knees upon the floor and, with the lantern and a magnifying lens,
002063 began to examine minutely the cracks between the stones. A few
002064 seconds sufficed to satisfy him, for he sprang to his feet again
002065 and put his glass in his pocket.
002066 
002067 "We have at least an hour before us," he remarked, "for they can
002068 hardly take any steps until the good pawnbroker is safely in bed.
002069 Then they will not lose a minute, for the sooner they do their
002070 work the longer time they will have for their escape. We are at
002071 present, Doctor--as no doubt you have divined--in the cellar of
002072 the City branch of one of the principal London banks. Mr.
002073 Merryweather is the chairman of directors, and he will explain to
002074 you that there are reasons why the more daring criminals of
002075 London should take a considerable interest in this cellar at
002076 present."
002077 
002078 "It is our French gold," whispered the director. "We have had
002079 several warnings that an attempt might be made upon it."
002080 
002081 "Your French gold?"
002082 
002083 "Yes. We had occasion some months ago to strengthen our resources
002084 and borrowed for that purpose 30,000 napoleons from the Bank of
002085 France. It has become known that we have never had occasion to
002086 unpack the money, and that it is still lying in our cellar. The
002087 crate upon which I sit contains 2,000 napoleons packed between
002088 layers of lead foil. Our reserve of bullion is much larger at
002089 present than is usually kept in a single branch office, and the
002090 directors have had misgivings upon the subject."
002091 
002092 "Which were very well justified," observed Holmes. "And now it is
002093 time that we arranged our little plans. I expect that within an
002094 hour matters will come to a head. In the meantime Mr.
002095 Merryweather, we must put the screen over that dark lantern."
002096 
002097 "And sit in the dark?"
002098 
002099 "I am afraid so. I had brought a pack of cards in my pocket, and
002100 I thought that, as we were a partie carre, you might have your
002101 rubber after all. But I see that the enemy's preparations have
002102 gone so far that we cannot risk the presence of a light. And,
002103 first of all, we must choose our positions. These are daring men,
002104 and though we shall take them at a disadvantage, they may do us
002105 some harm unless we are careful. I shall stand behind this crate,
002106 and do you conceal yourselves behind those. Then, when I flash a
002107 light upon them, close in swiftly. If they fire, Watson, have no
002108 compunction about shooting them down."
002109 
002110 I placed my revolver, cocked, upon the top of the wooden case
002111 behind which I crouched. Holmes shot the slide across the front
002112 of his lantern and left us in pitch darkness--such an absolute
002113 darkness as I have never before experienced. The smell of hot
002114 metal remained to assure us that the light was still there, ready
002115 to flash out at a moment's notice. To me, with my nerves worked
002116 up to a pitch of expectancy, there was something depressing and
002117 subduing in the sudden gloom, and in the cold dank air of the
002118 vault.
002119 
002120 "They have but one retreat," whispered Holmes. "That is back
002121 through the house into Saxe-Coburg Square. I hope that you have
002122 done what I asked you, Jones?"
002123 
002124 "I have an inspector and two officers waiting at the front door."
002125 
002126 "Then we have stopped all the holes. And now we must be silent
002127 and wait."
002128 
002129 What a time it seemed! From comparing notes afterwards it was but
002130 an hour and a quarter, yet it appeared to me that the night must
002131 have almost gone and the dawn be breaking above us. My limbs
002132 were weary and stiff, for I feared to change my position; yet my
002133 nerves were worked up to the highest pitch of tension, and my
002134 hearing was so acute that I could not only hear the gentle
002135 breathing of my companions, but I could distinguish the deeper,
002136 heavier in-breath of the bulky Jones from the thin, sighing note
002137 of the bank director. From my position I could look over the case
002138 in the direction of the floor. Suddenly my eyes caught the glint
002139 of a light.
002140 
002141 At first it was but a lurid spark upon the stone pavement. Then
002142 it lengthened out until it became a yellow line, and then,
002143 without any warning or sound, a gash seemed to open and a hand
002144 appeared, a white, almost womanly hand, which felt about in the
002145 centre of the little area of light. For a minute or more the
002146 hand, with its writhing fingers, protruded out of the floor. Then
002147 it was withdrawn as suddenly as it appeared, and all was dark
002148 again save the single lurid spark which marked a chink between
002149 the stones.
002150 
002151 Its disappearance, however, was but momentary. With a rending,
002152 tearing sound, one of the broad, white stones turned over upon
002153 its side and left a square, gaping hole, through which streamed
002154 the light of a lantern. Over the edge there peeped a clean-cut,
002155 boyish face, which looked keenly about it, and then, with a hand
002156 on either side of the aperture, drew itself shoulder-high and
002157 waist-high, until one knee rested upon the edge. In another
002158 instant he stood at the side of the hole and was hauling after
002159 him a companion, lithe and small like himself, with a pale face
002160 and a shock of very red hair.
002161 
002162 "It's all clear," he whispered. "Have you the chisel and the
002163 bags? Great Scott! Jump, Archie, jump, and I'll swing for it!"
002164 
002165 Sherlock Holmes had sprung out and seized the intruder by the
002166 collar. The other dived down the hole, and I heard the sound of
002167 rending cloth as Jones clutched at his skirts. The light flashed
002168 upon the barrel of a revolver, but Holmes' hunting crop came
002169 down on the man's wrist, and the pistol clinked upon the stone
002170 floor.
002171 
002172 "It's no use, John Clay," said Holmes blandly. "You have no
002173 chance at all."
002174 
002175 "So I see," the other answered with the utmost coolness. "I fancy
002176 that my pal is all right, though I see you have got his
002177 coat-tails."
002178 
002179 "There are three men waiting for him at the door," said Holmes.
002180 
002181 "Oh, indeed! You seem to have done the thing very completely. I
002182 must compliment you."
002183 
002184 "And I you," Holmes answered. "Your red-headed idea was very new
002185 and effective."
002186 
002187 "You'll see your pal again presently," said Jones. "He's quicker
002188 at climbing down holes than I am. Just hold out while I fix the
002189 derbies."
002190 
002191 "I beg that you will not touch me with your filthy hands,"
002192 remarked our prisoner as the handcuffs clattered upon his wrists.
002193 "You may not be aware that I have royal blood in my veins. Have
002194 the goodness, also, when you address me always to say 'sir' and
002195 'please.'"
002196 
002197 "All right," said Jones with a stare and a snigger. "Well, would
002198 you please, sir, march upstairs, where we can get a cab to carry
002199 your Highness to the police-station?"
002200 
002201 "That is better," said John Clay serenely. He made a sweeping bow
002202 to the three of us and walked quietly off in the custody of the
002203 detective.
002204 
002205 "Really, Mr. Holmes," said Mr. Merryweather as we followed them
002206 from the cellar, "I do not know how the bank can thank you or
002207 repay you. There is no doubt that you have detected and defeated
002208 in the most complete manner one of the most determined attempts
002209 at bank robbery that have ever come within my experience."
002210 
002211 "I have had one or two little scores of my own to settle with Mr.
002212 John Clay," said Holmes. "I have been at some small expense over
002213 this matter, which I shall expect the bank to refund, but beyond
002214 that I am amply repaid by having had an experience which is in
002215 many ways unique, and by hearing the very remarkable narrative of
002216 the Red-headed League."
002217 
002218 
002219 "You see, Watson," he explained in the early hours of the morning
002220 as we sat over a glass of whisky and soda in Baker Street, "it
002221 was perfectly obvious from the first that the only possible
002222 object of this rather fantastic business of the advertisement of
002223 the League, and the copying of the 'Encyclopaedia,' must be to get
002224 this not over-bright pawnbroker out of the way for a number of
002225 hours every day. It was a curious way of managing it, but,
002226 really, it would be difficult to suggest a better. The method was
002227 no doubt suggested to Clay's ingenious mind by the colour of his
002228 accomplice's hair. The 4 pounds a week was a lure which must draw
002229 him, and what was it to them, who were playing for thousands?
002230 They put in the advertisement, one rogue has the temporary
002231 office, the other rogue incites the man to apply for it, and
002232 together they manage to secure his absence every morning in the
002233 week. From the time that I heard of the assistant having come for
002234 half wages, it was obvious to me that he had some strong motive
002235 for securing the situation."
002236 
002237 "But how could you guess what the motive was?"
002238 
002239 "Had there been women in the house, I should have suspected a
002240 mere vulgar intrigue. That, however, was out of the question. The
002241 man's business was a small one, and there was nothing in his
002242 house which could account for such elaborate preparations, and
002243 such an expenditure as they were at. It must, then, be something
002244 out of the house. What could it be? I thought of the assistant's
002245 fondness for photography, and his trick of vanishing into the
002246 cellar. The cellar! There was the end of this tangled clue. Then
002247 I made inquiries as to this mysterious assistant and found that I
002248 had to deal with one of the coolest and most daring criminals in
002249 London. He was doing something in the cellar--something which
002250 took many hours a day for months on end. What could it be, once
002251 more? I could think of nothing save that he was running a tunnel
002252 to some other building.
002253 
002254 "So far I had got when we went to visit the scene of action. I
002255 surprised you by beating upon the pavement with my stick. I was
002256 ascertaining whether the cellar stretched out in front or behind.
002257 It was not in front. Then I rang the bell, and, as I hoped, the
002258 assistant answered it. We have had some skirmishes, but we had
002259 never set eyes upon each other before. I hardly looked at his
002260 face. His knees were what I wished to see. You must yourself have
002261 remarked how worn, wrinkled, and stained they were. They spoke of
002262 those hours of burrowing. The only remaining point was what they
002263 were burrowing for. I walked round the corner, saw the City and
002264 Suburban Bank abutted on our friend's premises, and felt that I
002265 had solved my problem. When you drove home after the concert I
002266 called upon Scotland Yard and upon the chairman of the bank
002267 directors, with the result that you have seen."
002268 
002269 "And how could you tell that they would make their attempt
002270 to-night?" I asked.
002271 
002272 "Well, when they closed their League offices that was a sign that
002273 they cared no longer about Mr. Jabez Wilson's presence--in other
002274 words, that they had completed their tunnel. But it was essential
002275 that they should use it soon, as it might be discovered, or the
002276 bullion might be removed. Saturday would suit them better than
002277 any other day, as it would give them two days for their escape.
002278 For all these reasons I expected them to come to-night."
002279 
002280 "You reasoned it out beautifully," I exclaimed in unfeigned
002281 admiration. "It is so long a chain, and yet every link rings
002282 true."
002283 
002284 "It saved me from ennui," he answered, yawning. "Alas! I already
002285 feel it closing in upon me. My life is spent in one long effort
002286 to escape from the commonplaces of existence. These little
002287 problems help me to do so."
002288 
002289 "And you are a benefactor of the race," said I.
002290 
002291 He shrugged his shoulders. "Well, perhaps, after all, it is of
002292 some little use," he remarked. "'L'homme c'est rien--l'oeuvre
002293 c'est tout,' as Gustave Flaubert wrote to George Sand."
002294 
002295 
002296 
002297 ADVENTURE III. A CASE OF IDENTITY
002298 
002299 "My dear fellow," said Sherlock Holmes as we sat on either side
002300 of the fire in his lodgings at Baker Street, "life is infinitely
002301 stranger than anything which the mind of man could invent. We
002302 would not dare to conceive the things which are really mere
002303 commonplaces of existence. If we could fly out of that window
002304 hand in hand, hover over this great city, gently remove the
002305 roofs, and peep in at the queer things which are going on, the
002306 strange coincidences, the plannings, the cross-purposes, the
002307 wonderful chains of events, working through generations, and
002308 leading to the most outr results, it would make all fiction with
002309 its conventionalities and foreseen conclusions most stale and
002310 unprofitable."
002311 
002312 "And yet I am not convinced of it," I answered. "The cases which
002313 come to light in the papers are, as a rule, bald enough, and
002314 vulgar enough. We have in our police reports realism pushed to
002315 its extreme limits, and yet the result is, it must be confessed,
002316 neither fascinating nor artistic."
002317 
002318 "A certain selection and discretion must be used in producing a
002319 realistic effect," remarked Holmes. "This is wanting in the
002320 police report, where more stress is laid, perhaps, upon the
002321 platitudes of the magistrate than upon the details, which to an
002322 observer contain the vital essence of the whole matter. Depend
002323 upon it, there is nothing so unnatural as the commonplace."
002324 
002325 I smiled and shook my head. "I can quite understand your thinking
002326 so," I said. "Of course, in your position of unofficial adviser
002327 and helper to everybody who is absolutely puzzled, throughout
002328 three continents, you are brought in contact with all that is
002329 strange and bizarre. But here"--I picked up the morning paper
002330 from the ground--"let us put it to a practical test. Here is the
002331 first heading upon which I come. 'A husband's cruelty to his
002332 wife.' There is half a column of print, but I know without
002333 reading it that it is all perfectly familiar to me. There is, of
002334 course, the other woman, the drink, the push, the blow, the
002335 bruise, the sympathetic sister or landlady. The crudest of
002336 writers could invent nothing more crude."
002337 
002338 "Indeed, your example is an unfortunate one for your argument,"
002339 said Holmes, taking the paper and glancing his eye down it. "This
002340 is the Dundas separation case, and, as it happens, I was engaged
002341 in clearing up some small points in connection with it. The
002342 husband was a teetotaler, there was no other woman, and the
002343 conduct complained of was that he had drifted into the habit of
002344 winding up every meal by taking out his false teeth and hurling
002345 them at his wife, which, you will allow, is not an action likely
002346 to occur to the imagination of the average story-teller. Take a
002347 pinch of snuff, Doctor, and acknowledge that I have scored over
002348 you in your example."
002349 
002350 He held out his snuffbox of old gold, with a great amethyst in
002351 the centre of the lid. Its splendour was in such contrast to his
002352 homely ways and simple life that I could not help commenting upon
002353 it.
002354 
002355 "Ah," said he, "I forgot that I had not seen you for some weeks.
002356 It is a little souvenir from the King of Bohemia in return for my
002357 assistance in the case of the Irene Adler papers."
002358 
002359 "And the ring?" I asked, glancing at a remarkable brilliant which
002360 sparkled upon his finger.
002361 
002362 "It was from the reigning family of Holland, though the matter in
002363 which I served them was of such delicacy that I cannot confide it
002364 even to you, who have been good enough to chronicle one or two of
002365 my little problems."
002366 
002367 "And have you any on hand just now?" I asked with interest.
002368 
002369 "Some ten or twelve, but none which present any feature of
002370 interest. They are important, you understand, without being
002371 interesting. Indeed, I have found that it is usually in
002372 unimportant matters that there is a field for the observation,
002373 and for the quick analysis of cause and effect which gives the
002374 charm to an investigation. The larger crimes are apt to be the
002375 simpler, for the bigger the crime the more obvious, as a rule, is
002376 the motive. In these cases, save for one rather intricate matter
002377 which has been referred to me from Marseilles, there is nothing
002378 which presents any features of interest. It is possible, however,
002379 that I may have something better before very many minutes are
002380 over, for this is one of my clients, or I am much mistaken."
002381 
002382 He had risen from his chair and was standing between the parted
002383 blinds gazing down into the dull neutral-tinted London street.
002384 Looking over his shoulder, I saw that on the pavement opposite
002385 there stood a large woman with a heavy fur boa round her neck,
002386 and a large curling red feather in a broad-brimmed hat which was
002387 tilted in a coquettish Duchess of Devonshire fashion over her
002388 ear. From under this great panoply she peeped up in a nervous,
002389 hesitating fashion at our windows, while her body oscillated
002390 backward and forward, and her fingers fidgeted with her glove
002391 buttons. Suddenly, with a plunge, as of the swimmer who leaves
002392 the bank, she hurried across the road, and we heard the sharp
002393 clang of the bell.
002394 
002395 "I have seen those symptoms before," said Holmes, throwing his
002396 cigarette into the fire. "Oscillation upon the pavement always
002397 means an affaire de coeur. She would like advice, but is not sure
002398 that the matter is not too delicate for communication. And yet
002399 even here we may discriminate. When a woman has been seriously
002400 wronged by a man she no longer oscillates, and the usual symptom
002401 is a broken bell wire. Here we may take it that there is a love
002402 matter, but that the maiden is not so much angry as perplexed, or
002403 grieved. But here she comes in person to resolve our doubts."
002404 
002405 As he spoke there was a tap at the door, and the boy in buttons
002406 entered to announce Miss Mary Sutherland, while the lady herself
002407 loomed behind his small black figure like a full-sailed
002408 merchant-man behind a tiny pilot boat. Sherlock Holmes welcomed
002409 her with the easy courtesy for which he was remarkable, and,
002410 having closed the door and bowed her into an armchair, he looked
002411 her over in the minute and yet abstracted fashion which was
002412 peculiar to him.
002413 
002414 "Do you not find," he said, "that with your short sight it is a
002415 little trying to do so much typewriting?"
002416 
002417 "I did at first," she answered, "but now I know where the letters
002418 are without looking." Then, suddenly realising the full purport
002419 of his words, she gave a violent start and looked up, with fear
002420 and astonishment upon her broad, good-humoured face. "You've
002421 heard about me, Mr. Holmes," she cried, "else how could you know
002422 all that?"
002423 
002424 "Never mind," said Holmes, laughing; "it is my business to know
002425 things. Perhaps I have trained myself to see what others
002426 overlook. If not, why should you come to consult me?"
002427 
002428 "I came to you, sir, because I heard of you from Mrs. Etherege,
002429 whose husband you found so easy when the police and everyone had
002430 given him up for dead. Oh, Mr. Holmes, I wish you would do as
002431 much for me. I'm not rich, but still I have a hundred a year in
002432 my own right, besides the little that I make by the machine, and
002433 I would give it all to know what has become of Mr. Hosmer Angel."
002434 
002435 "Why did you come away to consult me in such a hurry?" asked
002436 Sherlock Holmes, with his finger-tips together and his eyes to
002437 the ceiling.
002438 
002439 Again a startled look came over the somewhat vacuous face of Miss
002440 Mary Sutherland. "Yes, I did bang out of the house," she said,
002441 "for it made me angry to see the easy way in which Mr.
002442 Windibank--that is, my father--took it all. He would not go to
002443 the police, and he would not go to you, and so at last, as he
002444 would do nothing and kept on saying that there was no harm done,
002445 it made me mad, and I just on with my things and came right away
002446 to you."
002447 
002448 "Your father," said Holmes, "your stepfather, surely, since the
002449 name is different."
002450 
002451 "Yes, my stepfather. I call him father, though it sounds funny,
002452 too, for he is only five years and two months older than myself."
002453 
002454 "And your mother is alive?"
002455 
002456 "Oh, yes, mother is alive and well. I wasn't best pleased, Mr.
002457 Holmes, when she married again so soon after father's death, and
002458 a man who was nearly fifteen years younger than herself. Father
002459 was a plumber in the Tottenham Court Road, and he left a tidy
002460 business behind him, which mother carried on with Mr. Hardy, the
002461 foreman; but when Mr. Windibank came he made her sell the
002462 business, for he was very superior, being a traveller in wines.
002463 They got 4700 pounds for the goodwill and interest, which wasn't
002464 near as much as father could have got if he had been alive."
002465 
002466 I had expected to see Sherlock Holmes impatient under this
002467 rambling and inconsequential narrative, but, on the contrary, he
002468 had listened with the greatest concentration of attention.
002469 
002470 "Your own little income," he asked, "does it come out of the
002471 business?"
002472 
002473 "Oh, no, sir. It is quite separate and was left me by my uncle
002474 Ned in Auckland. It is in New Zealand stock, paying 4 1/2 per
002475 cent. Two thousand five hundred pounds was the amount, but I can
002476 only touch the interest."
002477 
002478 "You interest me extremely," said Holmes. "And since you draw so
002479 large a sum as a hundred a year, with what you earn into the
002480 bargain, you no doubt travel a little and indulge yourself in
002481 every way. I believe that a single lady can get on very nicely
002482 upon an income of about 60 pounds."
002483 
002484 "I could do with much less than that, Mr. Holmes, but you
002485 understand that as long as I live at home I don't wish to be a
002486 burden to them, and so they have the use of the money just while
002487 I am staying with them. Of course, that is only just for the
002488 time. Mr. Windibank draws my interest every quarter and pays it
002489 over to mother, and I find that I can do pretty well with what I
002490 earn at typewriting. It brings me twopence a sheet, and I can
002491 often do from fifteen to twenty sheets in a day."
002492 
002493 "You have made your position very clear to me," said Holmes.
002494 "This is my friend, Dr. Watson, before whom you can speak as
002495 freely as before myself. Kindly tell us now all about your
002496 connection with Mr. Hosmer Angel."
002497 
002498 A flush stole over Miss Sutherland's face, and she picked
002499 nervously at the fringe of her jacket. "I met him first at the
002500 gasfitters' ball," she said. "They used to send father tickets
002501 when he was alive, and then afterwards they remembered us, and
002502 sent them to mother. Mr. Windibank did not wish us to go. He
002503 never did wish us to go anywhere. He would get quite mad if I
002504 wanted so much as to join a Sunday-school treat. But this time I
002505 was set on going, and I would go; for what right had he to
002506 prevent? He said the folk were not fit for us to know, when all
002507 father's friends were to be there. And he said that I had nothing
002508 fit to wear, when I had my purple plush that I had never so much
002509 as taken out of the drawer. At last, when nothing else would do,
002510 he went off to France upon the business of the firm, but we went,
002511 mother and I, with Mr. Hardy, who used to be our foreman, and it
002512 was there I met Mr. Hosmer Angel."
002513 
002514 "I suppose," said Holmes, "that when Mr. Windibank came back from
002515 France he was very annoyed at your having gone to the ball."
002516 
002517 "Oh, well, he was very good about it. He laughed, I remember, and
002518 shrugged his shoulders, and said there was no use denying
002519 anything to a woman, for she would have her way."
002520 
002521 "I see. Then at the gasfitters' ball you met, as I understand, a
002522 gentleman called Mr. Hosmer Angel."
002523 
002524 "Yes, sir. I met him that night, and he called next day to ask if
002525 we had got home all safe, and after that we met him--that is to
002526 say, Mr. Holmes, I met him twice for walks, but after that father
002527 came back again, and Mr. Hosmer Angel could not come to the house
002528 any more."
002529 
002530 "No?"
002531 
002532 "Well, you know father didn't like anything of the sort. He
002533 wouldn't have any visitors if he could help it, and he used to
002534 say that a woman should be happy in her own family circle. But
002535 then, as I used to say to mother, a woman wants her own circle to
002536 begin with, and I had not got mine yet."
002537 
002538 "But how about Mr. Hosmer Angel? Did he make no attempt to see
002539 you?"
002540 
002541 "Well, father was going off to France again in a week, and Hosmer
002542 wrote and said that it would be safer and better not to see each
002543 other until he had gone. We could write in the meantime, and he
002544 used to write every day. I took the letters in in the morning, so
002545 there was no need for father to know."
002546 
002547 "Were you engaged to the gentleman at this time?"
002548 
002549 "Oh, yes, Mr. Holmes. We were engaged after the first walk that
002550 we took. Hosmer--Mr. Angel--was a cashier in an office in
002551 Leadenhall Street--and--"
002552 
002553 "What office?"
002554 
002555 "That's the worst of it, Mr. Holmes, I don't know."
002556 
002557 "Where did he live, then?"
002558 
002559 "He slept on the premises."
002560 
002561 "And you don't know his address?"
002562 
002563 "No--except that it was Leadenhall Street."
002564 
002565 "Where did you address your letters, then?"
002566 
002567 "To the Leadenhall Street Post Office, to be left till called
002568 for. He said that if they were sent to the office he would be
002569 chaffed by all the other clerks about having letters from a lady,
002570 so I offered to typewrite them, like he did his, but he wouldn't
002571 have that, for he said that when I wrote them they seemed to come
002572 from me, but when they were typewritten he always felt that the
002573 machine had come between us. That will just show you how fond he
002574 was of me, Mr. Holmes, and the little things that he would think
002575 of."
002576 
002577 "It was most suggestive," said Holmes. "It has long been an axiom
002578 of mine that the little things are infinitely the most important.
002579 Can you remember any other little things about Mr. Hosmer Angel?"
002580 
002581 "He was a very shy man, Mr. Holmes. He would rather walk with me
002582 in the evening than in the daylight, for he said that he hated to
002583 be conspicuous. Very retiring and gentlemanly he was. Even his
002584 voice was gentle. He'd had the quinsy and swollen glands when he
002585 was young, he told me, and it had left him with a weak throat,
002586 and a hesitating, whispering fashion of speech. He was always
002587 well dressed, very neat and plain, but his eyes were weak, just
002588 as mine are, and he wore tinted glasses against the glare."
002589 
002590 "Well, and what happened when Mr. Windibank, your stepfather,
002591 returned to France?"
002592 
002593 "Mr. Hosmer Angel came to the house again and proposed that we
002594 should marry before father came back. He was in dreadful earnest
002595 and made me swear, with my hands on the Testament, that whatever
002596 happened I would always be true to him. Mother said he was quite
002597 right to make me swear, and that it was a sign of his passion.
002598 Mother was all in his favour from the first and was even fonder
002599 of him than I was. Then, when they talked of marrying within the
002600 week, I began to ask about father; but they both said never to
002601 mind about father, but just to tell him afterwards, and mother
002602 said she would make it all right with him. I didn't quite like
002603 that, Mr. Holmes. It seemed funny that I should ask his leave, as
002604 he was only a few years older than me; but I didn't want to do
002605 anything on the sly, so I wrote to father at Bordeaux, where the
002606 company has its French offices, but the letter came back to me on
002607 the very morning of the wedding."
002608 
002609 "It missed him, then?"
002610 
002611 "Yes, sir; for he had started to England just before it arrived."
002612 
002613 "Ha! that was unfortunate. Your wedding was arranged, then, for
002614 the Friday. Was it to be in church?"
002615 
002616 "Yes, sir, but very quietly. It was to be at St. Saviour's, near
002617 King's Cross, and we were to have breakfast afterwards at the St.
002618 Pancras Hotel. Hosmer came for us in a hansom, but as there were
002619 two of us he put us both into it and stepped himself into a
002620 four-wheeler, which happened to be the only other cab in the
002621 street. We got to the church first, and when the four-wheeler
002622 drove up we waited for him to step out, but he never did, and
002623 when the cabman got down from the box and looked there was no one
002624 there! The cabman said that he could not imagine what had become
002625 of him, for he had seen him get in with his own eyes. That was
002626 last Friday, Mr. Holmes, and I have never seen or heard anything
002627 since then to throw any light upon what became of him."
002628 
002629 "It seems to me that you have been very shamefully treated," said
002630 Holmes.
002631 
002632 "Oh, no, sir! He was too good and kind to leave me so. Why, all
002633 the morning he was saying to me that, whatever happened, I was to
002634 be true; and that even if something quite unforeseen occurred to
002635 separate us, I was always to remember that I was pledged to him,
002636 and that he would claim his pledge sooner or later. It seemed
002637 strange talk for a wedding-morning, but what has happened since
002638 gives a meaning to it."
002639 
002640 "Most certainly it does. Your own opinion is, then, that some
002641 unforeseen catastrophe has occurred to him?"
002642 
002643 "Yes, sir. I believe that he foresaw some danger, or else he
002644 would not have talked so. And then I think that what he foresaw
002645 happened."
002646 
002647 "But you have no notion as to what it could have been?"
002648 
002649 "None."
002650 
002651 "One more question. How did your mother take the matter?"
002652 
002653 "She was angry, and said that I was never to speak of the matter
002654 again."
002655 
002656 "And your father? Did you tell him?"
002657 
002658 "Yes; and he seemed to think, with me, that something had
002659 happened, and that I should hear of Hosmer again. As he said,
002660 what interest could anyone have in bringing me to the doors of
002661 the church, and then leaving me? Now, if he had borrowed my
002662 money, or if he had married me and got my money settled on him,
002663 there might be some reason, but Hosmer was very independent about
002664 money and never would look at a shilling of mine. And yet, what
002665 could have happened? And why could he not write? Oh, it drives me
002666 half-mad to think of it, and I can't sleep a wink at night." She
002667 pulled a little handkerchief out of her muff and began to sob
002668 heavily into it.
002669 
002670 "I shall glance into the case for you," said Holmes, rising, "and
002671 I have no doubt that we shall reach some definite result. Let the
002672 weight of the matter rest upon me now, and do not let your mind
002673 dwell upon it further. Above all, try to let Mr. Hosmer Angel
002674 vanish from your memory, as he has done from your life."
002675 
002676 "Then you don't think I'll see him again?"
002677 
002678 "I fear not."
002679 
002680 "Then what has happened to him?"
002681 
002682 "You will leave that question in my hands. I should like an
002683 accurate description of him and any letters of his which you can
002684 spare."
002685 
002686 "I advertised for him in last Saturday's Chronicle," said she.
002687 "Here is the slip and here are four letters from him."
002688 
002689 "Thank you. And your address?"
002690 
002691 "No. 31 Lyon Place, Camberwell."
002692 
002693 "Mr. Angel's address you never had, I understand. Where is your
002694 father's place of business?"
002695 
002696 "He travels for Westhouse & Marbank, the great claret importers
002697 of Fenchurch Street."
002698 
002699 "Thank you. You have made your statement very clearly. You will
002700 leave the papers here, and remember the advice which I have given
002701 you. Let the whole incident be a sealed book, and do not allow it
002702 to affect your life."
002703 
002704 "You are very kind, Mr. Holmes, but I cannot do that. I shall be
002705 true to Hosmer. He shall find me ready when he comes back."
002706 
002707 For all the preposterous hat and the vacuous face, there was
002708 something noble in the simple faith of our visitor which
002709 compelled our respect. She laid her little bundle of papers upon
002710 the table and went her way, with a promise to come again whenever
002711 she might be summoned.
002712 
002713 Sherlock Holmes sat silent for a few minutes with his fingertips
002714 still pressed together, his legs stretched out in front of him,
002715 and his gaze directed upward to the ceiling. Then he took down
002716 from the rack the old and oily clay pipe, which was to him as a
002717 counsellor, and, having lit it, he leaned back in his chair, with
002718 the thick blue cloud-wreaths spinning up from him, and a look of
002719 infinite languor in his face.
002720 
002721 "Quite an interesting study, that maiden," he observed. "I found
002722 her more interesting than her little problem, which, by the way,
002723 is rather a trite one. You will find parallel cases, if you
002724 consult my index, in Andover in '77, and there was something of
002725 the sort at The Hague last year. Old as is the idea, however,
002726 there were one or two details which were new to me. But the
002727 maiden herself was most instructive."
002728 
002729 "You appeared to read a good deal upon her which was quite
002730 invisible to me," I remarked.
002731 
002732 "Not invisible but unnoticed, Watson. You did not know where to
002733 look, and so you missed all that was important. I can never bring
002734 you to realise the importance of sleeves, the suggestiveness of
002735 thumb-nails, or the great issues that may hang from a boot-lace.
002736 Now, what did you gather from that woman's appearance? Describe
002737 it."
002738 
002739 "Well, she had a slate-coloured, broad-brimmed straw hat, with a
002740 feather of a brickish red. Her jacket was black, with black beads
002741 sewn upon it, and a fringe of little black jet ornaments. Her
002742 dress was brown, rather darker than coffee colour, with a little
002743 purple plush at the neck and sleeves. Her gloves were greyish and
002744 were worn through at the right forefinger. Her boots I didn't
002745 observe. She had small round, hanging gold earrings, and a
002746 general air of being fairly well-to-do in a vulgar, comfortable,
002747 easy-going way."
002748 
002749 Sherlock Holmes clapped his hands softly together and chuckled.
002750 
002751 "'Pon my word, Watson, you are coming along wonderfully. You have
002752 really done very well indeed. It is true that you have missed
002753 everything of importance, but you have hit upon the method, and
002754 you have a quick eye for colour. Never trust to general
002755 impressions, my boy, but concentrate yourself upon details. My
002756 first glance is always at a woman's sleeve. In a man it is
002757 perhaps better first to take the knee of the trouser. As you
002758 observe, this woman had plush upon her sleeves, which is a most
002759 useful material for showing traces. The double line a little
002760 above the wrist, where the typewritist presses against the table,
002761 was beautifully defined. The sewing-machine, of the hand type,
002762 leaves a similar mark, but only on the left arm, and on the side
002763 of it farthest from the thumb, instead of being right across the
002764 broadest part, as this was. I then glanced at her face, and,
002765 observing the dint of a pince-nez at either side of her nose, I
002766 ventured a remark upon short sight and typewriting, which seemed
002767 to surprise her."
002768 
002769 "It surprised me."
002770 
002771 "But, surely, it was obvious. I was then much surprised and
002772 interested on glancing down to observe that, though the boots
002773 which she was wearing were not unlike each other, they were
002774 really odd ones; the one having a slightly decorated toe-cap, and
002775 the other a plain one. One was buttoned only in the two lower
002776 buttons out of five, and the other at the first, third, and
002777 fifth. Now, when you see that a young lady, otherwise neatly
002778 dressed, has come away from home with odd boots, half-buttoned,
002779 it is no great deduction to say that she came away in a hurry."
002780 
002781 "And what else?" I asked, keenly interested, as I always was, by
002782 my friend's incisive reasoning.
002783 
002784 "I noted, in passing, that she had written a note before leaving
002785 home but after being fully dressed. You observed that her right
002786 glove was torn at the forefinger, but you did not apparently see
002787 that both glove and finger were stained with violet ink. She had
002788 written in a hurry and dipped her pen too deep. It must have been
002789 this morning, or the mark would not remain clear upon the finger.
002790 All this is amusing, though rather elementary, but I must go back
002791 to business, Watson. Would you mind reading me the advertised
002792 description of Mr. Hosmer Angel?"
002793 
002794 I held the little printed slip to the light.
002795 
002796 "Missing," it said, "on the morning of the fourteenth, a gentleman
002797 named Hosmer Angel. About five ft. seven in. in height;
002798 strongly built, sallow complexion, black hair, a little bald in
002799 the centre, bushy, black side-whiskers and moustache; tinted
002800 glasses, slight infirmity of speech. Was dressed, when last seen,
002801 in black frock-coat faced with silk, black waistcoat, gold Albert
002802 chain, and grey Harris tweed trousers, with brown gaiters over
002803 elastic-sided boots. Known to have been employed in an office in
002804 Leadenhall Street. Anybody bringing--"
002805 
002806 "That will do," said Holmes. "As to the letters," he continued,
002807 glancing over them, "they are very commonplace. Absolutely no
002808 clue in them to Mr. Angel, save that he quotes Balzac once. There
002809 is one remarkable point, however, which will no doubt strike
002810 you."
002811 
002812 "They are typewritten," I remarked.
002813 
002814 "Not only that, but the signature is typewritten. Look at the
002815 neat little 'Hosmer Angel' at the bottom. There is a date, you
002816 see, but no superscription except Leadenhall Street, which is
002817 rather vague. The point about the signature is very suggestive--in
002818 fact, we may call it conclusive."
002819 
002820 "Of what?"
002821 
002822 "My dear fellow, is it possible you do not see how strongly it
002823 bears upon the case?"
002824 
002825 "I cannot say that I do unless it were that he wished to be able
002826 to deny his signature if an action for breach of promise were
002827 instituted."
002828 
002829 "No, that was not the point. However, I shall write two letters,
002830 which should settle the matter. One is to a firm in the City, the
002831 other is to the young lady's stepfather, Mr. Windibank, asking
002832 him whether he could meet us here at six o'clock tomorrow
002833 evening. It is just as well that we should do business with the
002834 male relatives. And now, Doctor, we can do nothing until the
002835 answers to those letters come, so we may put our little problem
002836 upon the shelf for the interim."
002837 
002838 I had had so many reasons to believe in my friend's subtle powers
002839 of reasoning and extraordinary energy in action that I felt that
002840 he must have some solid grounds for the assured and easy
002841 demeanour with which he treated the singular mystery which he had
002842 been called upon to fathom. Once only had I known him to fail, in
002843 the case of the King of Bohemia and of the Irene Adler
002844 photograph; but when I looked back to the weird business of the
002845 Sign of Four, and the extraordinary circumstances connected with
002846 the Study in Scarlet, I felt that it would be a strange tangle
002847 indeed which he could not unravel.
002848 
002849 I left him then, still puffing at his black clay pipe, with the
002850 conviction that when I came again on the next evening I would
002851 find that he held in his hands all the clues which would lead up
002852 to the identity of the disappearing bridegroom of Miss Mary
002853 Sutherland.
002854 
002855 A professional case of great gravity was engaging my own
002856 attention at the time, and the whole of next day I was busy at
002857 the bedside of the sufferer. It was not until close upon six
002858 o'clock that I found myself free and was able to spring into a
002859 hansom and drive to Baker Street, half afraid that I might be too
002860 late to assist at the dnouement of the little mystery. I found
002861 Sherlock Holmes alone, however, half asleep, with his long, thin
002862 form curled up in the recesses of his armchair. A formidable
002863 array of bottles and test-tubes, with the pungent cleanly smell
002864 of hydrochloric acid, told me that he had spent his day in the
002865 chemical work which was so dear to him.
002866 
002867 "Well, have you solved it?" I asked as I entered.
002868 
002869 "Yes. It was the bisulphate of baryta."
002870 
002871 "No, no, the mystery!" I cried.
002872 
002873 "Oh, that! I thought of the salt that I have been working upon.
002874 There was never any mystery in the matter, though, as I said
002875 yesterday, some of the details are of interest. The only drawback
002876 is that there is no law, I fear, that can touch the scoundrel."
002877 
002878 "Who was he, then, and what was his object in deserting Miss
002879 Sutherland?"
002880 
002881 The question was hardly out of my mouth, and Holmes had not yet
002882 opened his lips to reply, when we heard a heavy footfall in the
002883 passage and a tap at the door.
002884 
002885 "This is the girl's stepfather, Mr. James Windibank," said
002886 Holmes. "He has written to me to say that he would be here at
002887 six. Come in!"
002888 
002889 The man who entered was a sturdy, middle-sized fellow, some
002890 thirty years of age, clean-shaven, and sallow-skinned, with a
002891 bland, insinuating manner, and a pair of wonderfully sharp and
002892 penetrating grey eyes. He shot a questioning glance at each of
002893 us, placed his shiny top-hat upon the sideboard, and with a
002894 slight bow sidled down into the nearest chair.
002895 
002896 "Good-evening, Mr. James Windibank," said Holmes. "I think that
002897 this typewritten letter is from you, in which you made an
002898 appointment with me for six o'clock?"
002899 
002900 "Yes, sir. I am afraid that I am a little late, but I am not
002901 quite my own master, you know. I am sorry that Miss Sutherland
002902 has troubled you about this little matter, for I think it is far
002903 better not to wash linen of the sort in public. It was quite
002904 against my wishes that she came, but she is a very excitable,
002905 impulsive girl, as you may have noticed, and she is not easily
002906 controlled when she has made up her mind on a point. Of course, I
002907 did not mind you so much, as you are not connected with the
002908 official police, but it is not pleasant to have a family
002909 misfortune like this noised abroad. Besides, it is a useless
002910 expense, for how could you possibly find this Hosmer Angel?"
002911 
002912 "On the contrary," said Holmes quietly; "I have every reason to
002913 believe that I will succeed in discovering Mr. Hosmer Angel."
002914 
002915 Mr. Windibank gave a violent start and dropped his gloves. "I am
002916 delighted to hear it," he said.
002917 
002918 "It is a curious thing," remarked Holmes, "that a typewriter has
002919 really quite as much individuality as a man's handwriting. Unless
002920 they are quite new, no two of them write exactly alike. Some
002921 letters get more worn than others, and some wear only on one
002922 side. Now, you remark in this note of yours, Mr. Windibank, that
002923 in every case there is some little slurring over of the 'e,' and
002924 a slight defect in the tail of the 'r.' There are fourteen other
002925 characteristics, but those are the more obvious."
002926 
002927 "We do all our correspondence with this machine at the office,
002928 and no doubt it is a little worn," our visitor answered, glancing
002929 keenly at Holmes with his bright little eyes.
002930 
002931 "And now I will show you what is really a very interesting study,
002932 Mr. Windibank," Holmes continued. "I think of writing another
002933 little monograph some of these days on the typewriter and its
002934 relation to crime. It is a subject to which I have devoted some
002935 little attention. I have here four letters which purport to come
002936 from the missing man. They are all typewritten. In each case, not
002937 only are the 'e's' slurred and the 'r's' tailless, but you will
002938 observe, if you care to use my magnifying lens, that the fourteen
002939 other characteristics to which I have alluded are there as well."
002940 
002941 Mr. Windibank sprang out of his chair and picked up his hat. "I
002942 cannot waste time over this sort of fantastic talk, Mr. Holmes,"
002943 he said. "If you can catch the man, catch him, and let me know
002944 when you have done it."
002945 
002946 "Certainly," said Holmes, stepping over and turning the key in
002947 the door. "I let you know, then, that I have caught him!"
002948 
002949 "What! where?" shouted Mr. Windibank, turning white to his lips
002950 and glancing about him like a rat in a trap.
002951 
002952 "Oh, it won't do--really it won't," said Holmes suavely. "There
002953 is no possible getting out of it, Mr. Windibank. It is quite too
002954 transparent, and it was a very bad compliment when you said that
002955 it was impossible for me to solve so simple a question. That's
002956 right! Sit down and let us talk it over."
002957 
002958 Our visitor collapsed into a chair, with a ghastly face and a
002959 glitter of moisture on his brow. "It--it's not actionable," he
002960 stammered.
002961 
002962 "I am very much afraid that it is not. But between ourselves,
002963 Windibank, it was as cruel and selfish and heartless a trick in a
002964 petty way as ever came before me. Now, let me just run over the
002965 course of events, and you will contradict me if I go wrong."
002966 
002967 The man sat huddled up in his chair, with his head sunk upon his
002968 breast, like one who is utterly crushed. Holmes stuck his feet up
002969 on the corner of the mantelpiece and, leaning back with his hands
002970 in his pockets, began talking, rather to himself, as it seemed,
002971 than to us.
002972 
002973 "The man married a woman very much older than himself for her
002974 money," said he, "and he enjoyed the use of the money of the
002975 daughter as long as she lived with them. It was a considerable
002976 sum, for people in their position, and the loss of it would have
002977 made a serious difference. It was worth an effort to preserve it.
002978 The daughter was of a good, amiable disposition, but affectionate
002979 and warm-hearted in her ways, so that it was evident that with
002980 her fair personal advantages, and her little income, she would
002981 not be allowed to remain single long. Now her marriage would
002982 mean, of course, the loss of a hundred a year, so what does her
002983 stepfather do to prevent it? He takes the obvious course of
002984 keeping her at home and forbidding her to seek the company of
002985 people of her own age. But soon he found that that would not
002986 answer forever. She became restive, insisted upon her rights, and
002987 finally announced her positive intention of going to a certain
002988 ball. What does her clever stepfather do then? He conceives an
002989 idea more creditable to his head than to his heart. With the
002990 connivance and assistance of his wife he disguised himself,
002991 covered those keen eyes with tinted glasses, masked the face with
002992 a moustache and a pair of bushy whiskers, sunk that clear voice
002993 into an insinuating whisper, and doubly secure on account of the
002994 girl's short sight, he appears as Mr. Hosmer Angel, and keeps off
002995 other lovers by making love himself."
002996 
002997 "It was only a joke at first," groaned our visitor. "We never
002998 thought that she would have been so carried away."
002999 
003000 "Very likely not. However that may be, the young lady was very
003001 decidedly carried away, and, having quite made up her mind that
003002 her stepfather was in France, the suspicion of treachery never
003003 for an instant entered her mind. She was flattered by the
003004 gentleman's attentions, and the effect was increased by the
003005 loudly expressed admiration of her mother. Then Mr. Angel began
003006 to call, for it was obvious that the matter should be pushed as
003007 far as it would go if a real effect were to be produced. There
003008 were meetings, and an engagement, which would finally secure the
003009 girl's affections from turning towards anyone else. But the
003010 deception could not be kept up forever. These pretended journeys
003011 to France were rather cumbrous. The thing to do was clearly to
003012 bring the business to an end in such a dramatic manner that it
003013 would leave a permanent impression upon the young lady's mind and
003014 prevent her from looking upon any other suitor for some time to
003015 come. Hence those vows of fidelity exacted upon a Testament, and
003016 hence also the allusions to a possibility of something happening
003017 on the very morning of the wedding. James Windibank wished Miss
003018 Sutherland to be so bound to Hosmer Angel, and so uncertain as to
003019 his fate, that for ten years to come, at any rate, she would not
003020 listen to another man. As far as the church door he brought her,
003021 and then, as he could go no farther, he conveniently vanished
003022 away by the old trick of stepping in at one door of a
003023 four-wheeler and out at the other. I think that was the chain of
003024 events, Mr. Windibank!"
003025 
003026 Our visitor had recovered something of his assurance while Holmes
003027 had been talking, and he rose from his chair now with a cold
003028 sneer upon his pale face.
003029 
003030 "It may be so, or it may not, Mr. Holmes," said he, "but if you
003031 are so very sharp you ought to be sharp enough to know that it is
003032 you who are breaking the law now, and not me. I have done nothing
003033 actionable from the first, but as long as you keep that door
003034 locked you lay yourself open to an action for assault and illegal
003035 constraint."
003036 
003037 "The law cannot, as you say, touch you," said Holmes, unlocking
003038 and throwing open the door, "yet there never was a man who
003039 deserved punishment more. If the young lady has a brother or a
003040 friend, he ought to lay a whip across your shoulders. By Jove!"
003041 he continued, flushing up at the sight of the bitter sneer upon
003042 the man's face, "it is not part of my duties to my client, but
003043 here's a hunting crop handy, and I think I shall just treat
003044 myself to--" He took two swift steps to the whip, but before he
003045 could grasp it there was a wild clatter of steps upon the stairs,
003046 the heavy hall door banged, and from the window we could see Mr.
003047 James Windibank running at the top of his speed down the road.
003048 
003049 "There's a cold-blooded scoundrel!" said Holmes, laughing, as he
003050 threw himself down into his chair once more. "That fellow will
003051 rise from crime to crime until he does something very bad, and
003052 ends on a gallows. The case has, in some respects, been not
003053 entirely devoid of interest."
003054 
003055 "I cannot now entirely see all the steps of your reasoning," I
003056 remarked.
003057 
003058 "Well, of course it was obvious from the first that this Mr.
003059 Hosmer Angel must have some strong object for his curious
003060 conduct, and it was equally clear that the only man who really
003061 profited by the incident, as far as we could see, was the
003062 stepfather. Then the fact that the two men were never together,
003063 but that the one always appeared when the other was away, was
003064 suggestive. So were the tinted spectacles and the curious voice,
003065 which both hinted at a disguise, as did the bushy whiskers. My
003066 suspicions were all confirmed by his peculiar action in
003067 typewriting his signature, which, of course, inferred that his
003068 handwriting was so familiar to her that she would recognise even
003069 the smallest sample of it. You see all these isolated facts,
003070 together with many minor ones, all pointed in the same
003071 direction."
003072 
003073 "And how did you verify them?"
003074 
003075 "Having once spotted my man, it was easy to get corroboration. I
003076 knew the firm for which this man worked. Having taken the printed
003077 description. I eliminated everything from it which could be the
003078 result of a disguise--the whiskers, the glasses, the voice, and I
003079 sent it to the firm, with a request that they would inform me
003080 whether it answered to the description of any of their
003081 travellers. I had already noticed the peculiarities of the
003082 typewriter, and I wrote to the man himself at his business
003083 address asking him if he would come here. As I expected, his
003084 reply was typewritten and revealed the same trivial but
003085 characteristic defects. The same post brought me a letter from
003086 Westhouse & Marbank, of Fenchurch Street, to say that the
003087 description tallied in every respect with that of their employ,
003088 James Windibank. Voil tout!"
003089 
003090 "And Miss Sutherland?"
003091 
003092 "If I tell her she will not believe me. You may remember the old
003093 Persian saying, 'There is danger for him who taketh the tiger
003094 cub, and danger also for whoso snatches a delusion from a woman.'
003095 There is as much sense in Hafiz as in Horace, and as much
003096 knowledge of the world."
003097 
003098 
003099 
003100 ADVENTURE IV. THE BOSCOMBE VALLEY MYSTERY
003101 
003102 We were seated at breakfast one morning, my wife and I, when the
003103 maid brought in a telegram. It was from Sherlock Holmes and ran
003104 in this way:
003105 
003106 "Have you a couple of days to spare? Have just been wired for from
003107 the west of England in connection with Boscombe Valley tragedy.
003108 Shall be glad if you will come with me. Air and scenery perfect.
003109 Leave Paddington by the 11:15."
003110 
003111 "What do you say, dear?" said my wife, looking across at me.
003112 "Will you go?"
003113 
003114 "I really don't know what to say. I have a fairly long list at
003115 present."
003116 
003117 "Oh, Anstruther would do your work for you. You have been looking
003118 a little pale lately. I think that the change would do you good,
003119 and you are always so interested in Mr. Sherlock Holmes' cases."
003120 
003121 "I should be ungrateful if I were not, seeing what I gained
003122 through one of them," I answered. "But if I am to go, I must pack
003123 at once, for I have only half an hour."
003124 
003125 My experience of camp life in Afghanistan had at least had the
003126 effect of making me a prompt and ready traveller. My wants were
003127 few and simple, so that in less than the time stated I was in a
003128 cab with my valise, rattling away to Paddington Station. Sherlock
003129 Holmes was pacing up and down the platform, his tall, gaunt
003130 figure made even gaunter and taller by his long grey
003131 travelling-cloak and close-fitting cloth cap.
003132 
003133 "It is really very good of you to come, Watson," said he. "It
003134 makes a considerable difference to me, having someone with me on
003135 whom I can thoroughly rely. Local aid is always either worthless
003136 or else biassed. If you will keep the two corner seats I shall
003137 get the tickets."
003138 
003139 We had the carriage to ourselves save for an immense litter of
003140 papers which Holmes had brought with him. Among these he rummaged
003141 and read, with intervals of note-taking and of meditation, until
003142 we were past Reading. Then he suddenly rolled them all into a
003143 gigantic ball and tossed them up onto the rack.
003144 
003145 "Have you heard anything of the case?" he asked.
003146 
003147 "Not a word. I have not seen a paper for some days."
003148 
003149 "The London press has not had very full accounts. I have just
003150 been looking through all the recent papers in order to master the
003151 particulars. It seems, from what I gather, to be one of those
003152 simple cases which are so extremely difficult."
003153 
003154 "That sounds a little paradoxical."
003155 
003156 "But it is profoundly true. Singularity is almost invariably a
003157 clue. The more featureless and commonplace a crime is, the more
003158 difficult it is to bring it home. In this case, however, they
003159 have established a very serious case against the son of the
003160 murdered man."
003161 
003162 "It is a murder, then?"
003163 
003164 "Well, it is conjectured to be so. I shall take nothing for
003165 granted until I have the opportunity of looking personally into
003166 it. I will explain the state of things to you, as far as I have
003167 been able to understand it, in a very few words.
003168 
003169 "Boscombe Valley is a country district not very far from Ross, in
003170 Herefordshire. The largest landed proprietor in that part is a
003171 Mr. John Turner, who made his money in Australia and returned
003172 some years ago to the old country. One of the farms which he
003173 held, that of Hatherley, was let to Mr. Charles McCarthy, who was
003174 also an ex-Australian. The men had known each other in the
003175 colonies, so that it was not unnatural that when they came to
003176 settle down they should do so as near each other as possible.
003177 Turner was apparently the richer man, so McCarthy became his
003178 tenant but still remained, it seems, upon terms of perfect
003179 equality, as they were frequently together. McCarthy had one son,
003180 a lad of eighteen, and Turner had an only daughter of the same
003181 age, but neither of them had wives living. They appear to have
003182 avoided the society of the neighbouring English families and to
003183 have led retired lives, though both the McCarthys were fond of
003184 sport and were frequently seen at the race-meetings of the
003185 neighbourhood. McCarthy kept two servants--a man and a girl.
003186 Turner had a considerable household, some half-dozen at the
003187 least. That is as much as I have been able to gather about the
003188 families. Now for the facts.
003189 
003190 "On June 3rd, that is, on Monday last, McCarthy left his house at
003191 Hatherley about three in the afternoon and walked down to the
