004725 web to weave, while theirs is already woven. The first
004726 consideration is to remove the pressing danger which threatens
004727 you. The second is to clear up the mystery and to punish the
004728 guilty parties."
004729 
004730 "I thank you," said the young man, rising and pulling on his
004731 overcoat. "You have given me fresh life and hope. I shall
004732 certainly do as you advise."
004733 
004734 "Do not lose an instant. And, above all, take care of yourself in
004735 the meanwhile, for I do not think that there can be a doubt that
004736 you are threatened by a very real and imminent danger. How do you
004737 go back?"
004738 
004739 "By train from Waterloo."
004740 
004741 "It is not yet nine. The streets will be crowded, so I trust that
004742 you may be in safety. And yet you cannot guard yourself too
004743 closely."
004744 
004745 "I am armed."
004746 
004747 "That is well. To-morrow I shall set to work upon your case."
004748 
004749 "I shall see you at Horsham, then?"
004750 
004751 "No, your secret lies in London. It is there that I shall seek
004752 it."
004753 
004754 "Then I shall call upon you in a day, or in two days, with news
004755 as to the box and the papers. I shall take your advice in every
004756 particular." He shook hands with us and took his leave. Outside
004757 the wind still screamed and the rain splashed and pattered
004758 against the windows. This strange, wild story seemed to have come
004759 to us from amid the mad elements--blown in upon us like a sheet
004760 of sea-weed in a gale--and now to have been reabsorbed by them
004761 once more.
004762 
004763 Sherlock Holmes sat for some time in silence, with his head sunk
004764 forward and his eyes bent upon the red glow of the fire. Then he
004765 lit his pipe, and leaning back in his chair he watched the blue
004766 smoke-rings as they chased each other up to the ceiling.
004767 
004768 "I think, Watson," he remarked at last, "that of all our cases we
004769 have had none more fantastic than this."
004770 
004771 "Save, perhaps, the Sign of Four."
004772 
004773 "Well, yes. Save, perhaps, that. And yet this John Openshaw seems
004774 to me to be walking amid even greater perils than did the
004775 Sholtos."
004776 
004777 "But have you," I asked, "formed any definite conception as to
004778 what these perils are?"
004779 
004780 "There can be no question as to their nature," he answered.
004781 
004782 "Then what are they? Who is this K. K. K., and why does he pursue
004783 this unhappy family?"
004784 
004785 Sherlock Holmes closed his eyes and placed his elbows upon the
004786 arms of his chair, with his finger-tips together. "The ideal
004787 reasoner," he remarked, "would, when he had once been shown a
004788 single fact in all its bearings, deduce from it not only all the
004789 chain of events which led up to it but also all the results which
004790 would follow from it. As Cuvier could correctly describe a whole
004791 animal by the contemplation of a single bone, so the observer who
004792 has thoroughly understood one link in a series of incidents
004793 should be able to accurately state all the other ones, both
004794 before and after. We have not yet grasped the results which the
004795 reason alone can attain to. Problems may be solved in the study
004796 which have baffled all those who have sought a solution by the
004797 aid of their senses. To carry the art, however, to its highest
004798 pitch, it is necessary that the reasoner should be able to
004799 utilise all the facts which have come to his knowledge; and this
004800 in itself implies, as you will readily see, a possession of all
004801 knowledge, which, even in these days of free education and
004802 encyclopaedias, is a somewhat rare accomplishment. It is not so
004803 impossible, however, that a man should possess all knowledge
004804 which is likely to be useful to him in his work, and this I have
004805 endeavoured in my case to do. If I remember rightly, you on one
004806 occasion, in the early days of our friendship, defined my limits
004807 in a very precise fashion."
004808 
004809 "Yes," I answered, laughing. "It was a singular document.
004810 Philosophy, astronomy, and politics were marked at zero, I
004811 remember. Botany variable, geology profound as regards the
004812 mud-stains from any region within fifty miles of town, chemistry
004813 eccentric, anatomy unsystematic, sensational literature and crime
004814 records unique, violin-player, boxer, swordsman, lawyer, and
004815 self-poisoner by cocaine and tobacco. Those, I think, were the
004816 main points of my analysis."
004817 
004818 Holmes grinned at the last item. "Well," he said, "I say now, as
004819 I said then, that a man should keep his little brain-attic
004820 stocked with all the furniture that he is likely to use, and the
004821 rest he can put away in the lumber-room of his library, where he
004822 can get it if he wants it. Now, for such a case as the one which
004823 has been submitted to us to-night, we need certainly to muster
004824 all our resources. Kindly hand me down the letter K of the
004825 'American Encyclopaedia' which stands upon the shelf beside you.
004826 Thank you. Now let us consider the situation and see what may be
004827 deduced from it. In the first place, we may start with a strong
004828 presumption that Colonel Openshaw had some very strong reason for
004829 leaving America. Men at his time of life do not change all their
004830 habits and exchange willingly the charming climate of Florida for
004831 the lonely life of an English provincial town. His extreme love
004832 of solitude in England suggests the idea that he was in fear of
004833 someone or something, so we may assume as a working hypothesis
004834 that it was fear of someone or something which drove him from
004835 America. As to what it was he feared, we can only deduce that by
004836 considering the formidable letters which were received by himself
004837 and his successors. Did you remark the postmarks of those
004838 letters?"
004839 
004840 "The first was from Pondicherry, the second from Dundee, and the
004841 third from London."
004842 
004843 "From East London. What do you deduce from that?"
004844 
004845 "They are all seaports. That the writer was on board of a ship."
004846 
004847 "Excellent. We have already a clue. There can be no doubt that
004848 the probability--the strong probability--is that the writer was
004849 on board of a ship. And now let us consider another point. In the
004850 case of Pondicherry, seven weeks elapsed between the threat and
004851 its fulfilment, in Dundee it was only some three or four days.
004852 Does that suggest anything?"
004853 
004854 "A greater distance to travel."
004855 
004856 "But the letter had also a greater distance to come."
004857 
004858 "Then I do not see the point."
004859 
004860 "There is at least a presumption that the vessel in which the man
004861 or men are is a sailing-ship. It looks as if they always send
004862 their singular warning or token before them when starting upon
004863 their mission. You see how quickly the deed followed the sign
004864 when it came from Dundee. If they had come from Pondicherry in a
004865 steamer they would have arrived almost as soon as their letter.
004866 But, as a matter of fact, seven weeks elapsed. I think that those
004867 seven weeks represented the difference between the mail-boat which
004868 brought the letter and the sailing vessel which brought the
004869 writer."
004870 
004871 "It is possible."
004872 
004873 "More than that. It is probable. And now you see the deadly
004874 urgency of this new case, and why I urged young Openshaw to
004875 caution. The blow has always fallen at the end of the time which
004876 it would take the senders to travel the distance. But this one
004877 comes from London, and therefore we cannot count upon delay."
004878 
004879 "Good God!" I cried. "What can it mean, this relentless
004880 persecution?"
004881 
004882 "The papers which Openshaw carried are obviously of vital
004883 importance to the person or persons in the sailing-ship. I think
004884 that it is quite clear that there must be more than one of them.
004885 A single man could not have carried out two deaths in such a way
004886 as to deceive a coroner's jury. There must have been several in
004887 it, and they must have been men of resource and determination.
004888 Their papers they mean to have, be the holder of them who it may.
004889 In this way you see K. K. K. ceases to be the initials of an
004890 individual and becomes the badge of a society."
004891 
004892 "But of what society?"
004893 
004894 "Have you never--" said Sherlock Holmes, bending forward and
004895 sinking his voice--"have you never heard of the Ku Klux Klan?"
004896 
004897 "I never have."
004898 
004899 Holmes turned over the leaves of the book upon his knee. "Here it
004900 is," said he presently:
004901 
004902 "'Ku Klux Klan. A name derived from the fanciful resemblance to
004903 the sound produced by cocking a rifle. This terrible secret
004904 society was formed by some ex-Confederate soldiers in the
004905 Southern states after the Civil War, and it rapidly formed local
004906 branches in different parts of the country, notably in Tennessee,
004907 Louisiana, the Carolinas, Georgia, and Florida. Its power was
004908 used for political purposes, principally for the terrorising of
004909 the negro voters and the murdering and driving from the country
004910 of those who were opposed to its views. Its outrages were usually
004911 preceded by a warning sent to the marked man in some fantastic
004912 but generally recognised shape--a sprig of oak-leaves in some
004913 parts, melon seeds or orange pips in others. On receiving this
004914 the victim might either openly abjure his former ways, or might
004915 fly from the country. If he braved the matter out, death would
004916 unfailingly come upon him, and usually in some strange and
004917 unforeseen manner. So perfect was the organisation of the
004918 society, and so systematic its methods, that there is hardly a
004919 case upon record where any man succeeded in braving it with
004920 impunity, or in which any of its outrages were traced home to the
004921 perpetrators. For some years the organisation flourished in spite
004922 of the efforts of the United States government and of the better
004923 classes of the community in the South. Eventually, in the year
004924 1869, the movement rather suddenly collapsed, although there have
004925 been sporadic outbreaks of the same sort since that date.'
004926 
004927 "You will observe," said Holmes, laying down the volume, "that
004928 the sudden breaking up of the society was coincident with the
004929 disappearance of Openshaw from America with their papers. It may
004930 well have been cause and effect. It is no wonder that he and his
004931 family have some of the more implacable spirits upon their track.
004932 You can understand that this register and diary may implicate
004933 some of the first men in the South, and that there may be many
004934 who will not sleep easy at night until it is recovered."
004935 
004936 "Then the page we have seen--"
004937 
004938 "Is such as we might expect. It ran, if I remember right, 'sent
004939 the pips to A, B, and C'--that is, sent the society's warning to
004940 them. Then there are successive entries that A and B cleared, or
004941 left the country, and finally that C was visited, with, I fear, a
004942 sinister result for C. Well, I think, Doctor, that we may let
004943 some light into this dark place, and I believe that the only
004944 chance young Openshaw has in the meantime is to do what I have
004945 told him. There is nothing more to be said or to be done
004946 to-night, so hand me over my violin and let us try to forget for
004947 half an hour the miserable weather and the still more miserable
004948 ways of our fellow-men."
004949 
004950 
004951 It had cleared in the morning, and the sun was shining with a
004952 subdued brightness through the dim veil which hangs over the
004953 great city. Sherlock Holmes was already at breakfast when I came

004955 
004956 "You will excuse me for not waiting for you," said he; "I have, I

004961 
004962 "It will very much depend upon the results of my first inquiries.

004964 
004965 "You will not go there first?"

004967 "No, I shall commence with the City. Just ring the bell and the

004979 "My eye caught the name of Openshaw, and the heading 'Tragedy

004981 
004982 "Between nine and ten last night Police-Constable Cook, of the H
004983 Division, on duty near Waterloo Bridge, heard a cry for help and

004985 stormy, so that, in spite of the help of several passers-by, it
004986 was quite impossible to effect a rescue. The alarm, however, was
004987 given, and, by the aid of the water-police, the body was
004988 eventually recovered. It proved to be that of a young gentleman
004989 whose name, as it appears from an envelope which was found in his

004991 It is conjectured that he may have been hurrying down to catch
004992 the last train from Waterloo Station, and that in his haste and

004994 of one of the small landing-places for river steamboats. The body
004995 exhibited no traces of violence, and there can be no doubt that
004996 the deceased had been the victim of an unfortunate accident,

004999 
005000 We sat in silence for some minutes, Holmes more depressed and

005002 
005003 "That hurts my pride, Watson," he said at last. "It is a petty
005004 feeling, no doubt, but it hurts my pride. It becomes a personal
005005 matter with me now, and, if God sends me health, I shall set my

005017 
005018 "To the police?"
005019 
005020 "No; I shall be my own police. When I have spun the web they may
005021 take the flies, but not before."
005022 
005023 All day I was engaged in my professional work, and it was late in
005024 the evening before I returned to Baker Street. Sherlock Holmes
005025 had not come back yet. It was nearly ten o'clock before he
005026 entered, looking pale and worn. He walked up to the sideboard,

005028 washing it down with a long draught of water.
005029 
005030 "You are hungry," I remarked.
005031 
005032 "Starving. It had escaped my memory. I have had nothing since
005033 breakfast."
005034 
005035 "Nothing?"
005036 
005037 "Not a bite. I had no time to think of it."
005038 
005039 "And how have you succeeded?"
005040 
005041 "Well."
005042 
005043 "You have a clue?"
005044 
005045 "I have them in the hollow of my hand. Young Openshaw shall not

005047 trade-mark upon them. It is well thought of!"
005048 
005049 "What do you mean?"
005050 
005051 He took an orange from the cupboard, and tearing it to pieces he

005053 thrust them into an envelope. On the inside of the flap he wrote
005054 "S. H. for J. O." Then he sealed it and addressed it to "Captain

005056

005060 
005061 "And who is this Captain Calhoun?"
005062

005065 "How did you trace it, then?"
005066 
005067 He took a large sheet of paper from his pocket, all covered with

005069 
005070 "I have spent the whole day," said he, "over Lloyd's registers
005071 and files of the old papers, following the future career of every
005072 vessel which touched at Pondicherry in January and February in
005073 '83. There were thirty-six ships of fair tonnage which were

005075 instantly attracted my attention, since, although it was reported

005078 
005079 "Texas, I think."

005083

005090 
005091 "Yes?"

005099 
005100 "What will you do, then?"
005101 
005102 "Oh, I have my hand upon him. He and the two mates, are as I
005103 learn, the only native-born Americans in the ship. The others are
005104 Finns and Germans. I know, also, that they were all three away
005105 from the ship last night. I had it from the stevedore who has
005106 been loading their cargo. By the time that their sailing-ship
005107 reaches Savannah the mail-boat will have carried this letter, and
005108 the cable will have informed the police of Savannah that these
005109 three gentlemen are badly wanted here upon a charge of murder."
005110 
005111 There is ever a flaw, however, in the best laid of human plans,
005112 and the murderers of John Openshaw were never to receive the
005113 orange pips which would show them that another, as cunning and as
005114 resolute as themselves, was upon their track. Very long and very
005115 severe were the equinoctial gales that year. We waited long for
005116 news of the "Lone Star" of Savannah, but none ever reached us. We
005117 did at last hear that somewhere far out in the Atlantic a
005118 shattered stern-post of a boat was seen swinging in the trough
005119 of a wave, with the letters "L. S." carved upon it, and that is
005120 all which we shall ever know of the fate of the "Lone Star."
005121 
005122 
005123 
005124 ADVENTURE VI. THE MAN WITH THE TWISTED LIP
005125 
005126 Isa Whitney, brother of the late Elias Whitney, D.D., Principal
005127 of the Theological College of St. George's, was much addicted to
005128 opium. The habit grew upon him, as I understand, from some
005129 foolish freak when he was at college; for having read De
005130 Quincey's description of his dreams and sensations, he had
005131 drenched his tobacco with laudanum in an attempt to produce the
005132 same effects. He found, as so many more have done, that the
005133 practice is easier to attain than to get rid of, and for many
005134 years he continued to be a slave to the drug, an object of
005135 mingled horror and pity to his friends and relatives. I can see
005136 him now, with yellow, pasty face, drooping lids, and pin-point
005137 pupils, all huddled in a chair, the wreck and ruin of a noble
005138 man.
005139 
005140 One night--it was in June, '89--there came a ring to my bell,
005141 about the hour when a man gives his first yawn and glances at the
005142 clock. I sat up in my chair, and my wife laid her needle-work
005143 down in her lap and made a little face of disappointment.
005144 
005145 "A patient!" said she. "You'll have to go out."
005146 
005147 I groaned, for I was newly come back from a weary day.
005148 
005149 We heard the door open, a few hurried words, and then quick steps
005150 upon the linoleum. Our own door flew open, and a lady, clad in
005151 some dark-coloured stuff, with a black veil, entered the room.
005152 
005153 "You will excuse my calling so late," she began, and then,
005154 suddenly losing her self-control, she ran forward, threw her arms
005155 about my wife's neck, and sobbed upon her shoulder. "Oh, I'm in
005156 such trouble!" she cried; "I do so want a little help."
005157 
005158 "Why," said my wife, pulling up her veil, "it is Kate Whitney.
005159 How you startled me, Kate! I had not an idea who you were when
005160 you came in."
005161 
005162 "I didn't know what to do, so I came straight to you." That was
005163 always the way. Folk who were in grief came to my wife like birds
005164 to a light-house.
005165 
005166 "It was very sweet of you to come. Now, you must have some wine
005167 and water, and sit here comfortably and tell us all about it. Or
005168 should you rather that I sent James off to bed?"
005169 
005170 "Oh, no, no! I want the doctor's advice and help, too. It's about
005171 Isa. He has not been home for two days. I am so frightened about
005172 him!"
005173 
005174 It was not the first time that she had spoken to us of her
005175 husband's trouble, to me as a doctor, to my wife as an old friend
005176 and school companion. We soothed and comforted her by such words
005177 as we could find. Did she know where her husband was? Was it
005178 possible that we could bring him back to her?
005179 
005180 It seems that it was. She had the surest information that of late
005181 he had, when the fit was on him, made use of an opium den in the
005182 farthest east of the City. Hitherto his orgies had always been
005183 confined to one day, and he had come back, twitching and
005184 shattered, in the evening. But now the spell had been upon him
005185 eight-and-forty hours, and he lay there, doubtless among the
005186 dregs of the docks, breathing in the poison or sleeping off the
005187 effects. There he was to be found, she was sure of it, at the Bar
005188 of Gold, in Upper Swandam Lane. But what was she to do? How could
005189 she, a young and timid woman, make her way into such a place and
005190 pluck her husband out from among the ruffians who surrounded him?
005191 
005192 There was the case, and of course there was but one way out of
005193 it. Might I not escort her to this place? And then, as a second
005194 thought, why should she come at all? I was Isa Whitney's medical
005195 adviser, and as such I had influence over him. I could manage it
005196 better if I were alone. I promised her on my word that I would
005197 send him home in a cab within two hours if he were indeed at the
005198 address which she had given me. And so in ten minutes I had left
005199 my armchair and cheery sitting-room behind me, and was speeding
005200 eastward in a hansom on a strange errand, as it seemed to me at
005201 the time, though the future only could show how strange it was to
005202 be.
005203 
005204 But there was no great difficulty in the first stage of my
005205 adventure. Upper Swandam Lane is a vile alley lurking behind the
005206 high wharves which line the north side of the river to the east
005207 of London Bridge. Between a slop-shop and a gin-shop, approached
005208 by a steep flight of steps leading down to a black gap like the
005209 mouth of a cave, I found the den of which I was in search.
005210 Ordering my cab to wait, I passed down the steps, worn hollow in
005211 the centre by the ceaseless tread of drunken feet; and by the
005212 light of a flickering oil-lamp above the door I found the latch
005213 and made my way into a long, low room, thick and heavy with the
005214 brown opium smoke, and terraced with wooden berths, like the
005215 forecastle of an emigrant ship.
005216 
005217 Through the gloom one could dimly catch a glimpse of bodies lying
005218 in strange fantastic poses, bowed shoulders, bent knees, heads
005219 thrown back, and chins pointing upward, with here and there a
005220 dark, lack-lustre eye turned upon the newcomer. Out of the black
005221 shadows there glimmered little red circles of light, now bright,
005222 now faint, as the burning poison waxed or waned in the bowls of
005223 the metal pipes. The most lay silent, but some muttered to
005224 themselves, and others talked together in a strange, low,
005225 monotonous voice, their conversation coming in gushes, and then
005226 suddenly tailing off into silence, each mumbling out his own
005227 thoughts and paying little heed to the words of his neighbour. At
005228 the farther end was a small brazier of burning charcoal, beside
005229 which on a three-legged wooden stool there sat a tall, thin old
005230 man, with his jaw resting upon his two fists, and his elbows upon
005231 his knees, staring into the fire.
005232 
005233 As I entered, a sallow Malay attendant had hurried up with a pipe
005234 for me and a supply of the drug, beckoning me to an empty berth.
005235 
005236 "Thank you. I have not come to stay," said I. "There is a friend
005237 of mine here, Mr. Isa Whitney, and I wish to speak with him."
005238 
005239 There was a movement and an exclamation from my right, and
005240 peering through the gloom, I saw Whitney, pale, haggard, and
005241 unkempt, staring out at me.
005242 
005243 "My God! It's Watson," said he. He was in a pitiable state of
005244 reaction, with every nerve in a twitter. "I say, Watson, what
005245 o'clock is it?"
005246 
005247 "Nearly eleven."
005248 
005249 "Of what day?"
005250 
005251 "Of Friday, June 19th."
005252 
005253 "Good heavens! I thought it was Wednesday. It is Wednesday. What
005254 d'you want to frighten a chap for?" He sank his face onto his
005255 arms and began to sob in a high treble key.
005256 
005257 "I tell you that it is Friday, man. Your wife has been waiting
005258 this two days for you. You should be ashamed of yourself!"
005259 
005260 "So I am. But you've got mixed, Watson, for I have only been here
005261 a few hours, three pipes, four pipes--I forget how many. But I'll
005262 go home with you. I wouldn't frighten Kate--poor little Kate.
005263 Give me your hand! Have you a cab?"
005264 
005265 "Yes, I have one waiting."
005266 
005267 "Then I shall go in it. But I must owe something. Find what I
005268 owe, Watson. I am all off colour. I can do nothing for myself."
005269 
005270 I walked down the narrow passage between the double row of
005271 sleepers, holding my breath to keep out the vile, stupefying
005272 fumes of the drug, and looking about for the manager. As I passed
005273 the tall man who sat by the brazier I felt a sudden pluck at my
005274 skirt, and a low voice whispered, "Walk past me, and then look
005275 back at me." The words fell quite distinctly upon my ear. I
005276 glanced down. They could only have come from the old man at my
005277 side, and yet he sat now as absorbed as ever, very thin, very
005278 wrinkled, bent with age, an opium pipe dangling down from between
005279 his knees, as though it had dropped in sheer lassitude from his
005280 fingers. I took two steps forward and looked back. It took all my
005281 self-control to prevent me from breaking out into a cry of
005282 astonishment. He had turned his back so that none could see him
005283 but I. His form had filled out, his wrinkles were gone, the dull
005284 eyes had regained their fire, and there, sitting by the fire and
005285 grinning at my surprise, was none other than Sherlock Holmes. He
005286 made a slight motion to me to approach him, and instantly, as he
005287 turned his face half round to the company once more, subsided
005288 into a doddering, loose-lipped senility.
005289 
005290 "Holmes!" I whispered, "what on earth are you doing in this den?"
005291 
005292 "As low as you can," he answered; "I have excellent ears. If you
005293 would have the great kindness to get rid of that sottish friend
005294 of yours I should be exceedingly glad to have a little talk with
005295 you."
005296 
005297 "I have a cab outside."
005298 
005299 "Then pray send him home in it. You may safely trust him, for he
005300 appears to be too limp to get into any mischief. I should
005301 recommend you also to send a note by the cabman to your wife to
005302 say that you have thrown in your lot with me. If you will wait
005303 outside, I shall be with you in five minutes."
005304 
005305 It was difficult to refuse any of Sherlock Holmes' requests, for
005306 they were always so exceedingly definite, and put forward with
005307 such a quiet air of mastery. I felt, however, that when Whitney
005308 was once confined in the cab my mission was practically
005309 accomplished; and for the rest, I could not wish anything better
005310 than to be associated with my friend in one of those singular
005311 adventures which were the normal condition of his existence. In a
005312 few minutes I had written my note, paid Whitney's bill, led him
005313 out to the cab, and seen him driven through the darkness. In a
005314 very short time a decrepit figure had emerged from the opium den,
005315 and I was walking down the street with Sherlock Holmes. For two
005316 streets he shuffled along with a bent back and an uncertain foot.
005317 Then, glancing quickly round, he straightened himself out and
005318 burst into a hearty fit of laughter.
005319 
005320 "I suppose, Watson," said he, "that you imagine that I have added
005321 opium-smoking to cocaine injections, and all the other little
005322 weaknesses on which you have favoured me with your medical
005323 views."
005324 
005325 "I was certainly surprised to find you there."
005326 
005327 "But not more so than I to find you."
005328 
005329 "I came to find a friend."
005330 
005331 "And I to find an enemy."
005332 
005333 "An enemy?"
005334 
005335 "Yes; one of my natural enemies, or, shall I say, my natural
005336 prey. Briefly, Watson, I am in the midst of a very remarkable
005337 inquiry, and I have hoped to find a clue in the incoherent
005338 ramblings of these sots, as I have done before now. Had I been
005339 recognised in that den my life would not have been worth an
005340 hour's purchase; for I have used it before now for my own
005341 purposes, and the rascally Lascar who runs it has sworn to have
005342 vengeance upon me. There is a trap-door at the back of that
005343 building, near the corner of Paul's Wharf, which could tell some
005344 strange tales of what has passed through it upon the moonless
005345 nights."
005346 
005347 "What! You do not mean bodies?"
005348 
005349 "Ay, bodies, Watson. We should be rich men if we had 1000 pounds
005350 for every poor devil who has been done to death in that den. It
005351 is the vilest murder-trap on the whole riverside, and I fear that
005352 Neville St. Clair has entered it never to leave it more. But our
005353 trap should be here." He put his two forefingers between his
005354 teeth and whistled shrilly--a signal which was answered by a
005355 similar whistle from the distance, followed shortly by the rattle
005356 of wheels and the clink of horses' hoofs.
005357 
005358 "Now, Watson," said Holmes, as a tall dog-cart dashed up through
005359 the gloom, throwing out two golden tunnels of yellow light from
005360 its side lanterns. "You'll come with me, won't you?"
005361 
005362 "If I can be of use."
005363 
005364 "Oh, a trusty comrade is always of use; and a chronicler still
005365 more so. My room at The Cedars is a double-bedded one."
005366 
005367 "The Cedars?"
005368 
005369 "Yes; that is Mr. St. Clair's house. I am staying there while I
005370 conduct the inquiry."
005371 
005372 "Where is it, then?"
005373 
005374 "Near Lee, in Kent. We have a seven-mile drive before us."
005375 
005376 "But I am all in the dark."
005377 
005378 "Of course you are. You'll know all about it presently. Jump up
005379 here. All right, John; we shall not need you. Here's half a
005380 crown. Look out for me to-morrow, about eleven. Give her her
005381 head. So long, then!"
005382 
005383 He flicked the horse with his whip, and we dashed away through
005384 the endless succession of sombre and deserted streets, which
005385 widened gradually, until we were flying across a broad
005386 balustraded bridge, with the murky river flowing sluggishly
005387 beneath us. Beyond lay another dull wilderness of bricks and
005388 mortar, its silence broken only by the heavy, regular footfall of
005389 the policeman, or the songs and shouts of some belated party of
005390 revellers. A dull wrack was drifting slowly across the sky, and a
005391 star or two twinkled dimly here and there through the rifts of
005392 the clouds. Holmes drove in silence, with his head sunk upon his
005393 breast, and the air of a man who is lost in thought, while I sat
005394 beside him, curious to learn what this new quest might be which
005395 seemed to tax his powers so sorely, and yet afraid to break in
005396 upon the current of his thoughts. We had driven several miles,
005397 and were beginning to get to the fringe of the belt of suburban
005398 villas, when he shook himself, shrugged his shoulders, and lit up
005399 his pipe with the air of a man who has satisfied himself that he
005400 is acting for the best.
005401 
005402 "You have a grand gift of silence, Watson," said he. "It makes
005403 you quite invaluable as a companion. 'Pon my word, it is a great
005404 thing for me to have someone to talk to, for my own thoughts are
005405 not over-pleasant. I was wondering what I should say to this dear
005406 little woman to-night when she meets me at the door."
005407 
005408 "You forget that I know nothing about it."
005409 
005410 "I shall just have time to tell you the facts of the case before
005411 we get to Lee. It seems absurdly simple, and yet, somehow I can
005412 get nothing to go upon. There's plenty of thread, no doubt, but I
005413 can't get the end of it into my hand. Now, I'll state the case
005414 clearly and concisely to you, Watson, and maybe you can see a
005415 spark where all is dark to me."
005416 
005417 "Proceed, then."
005418 
005419 "Some years ago--to be definite, in May, 1884--there came to Lee
005420 a gentleman, Neville St. Clair by name, who appeared to have
005421 plenty of money. He took a large villa, laid out the grounds very
005422 nicely, and lived generally in good style. By degrees he made
005423 friends in the neighbourhood, and in 1887 he married the daughter
005424 of a local brewer, by whom he now has two children. He had no
005425 occupation, but was interested in several companies and went into
005426 town as a rule in the morning, returning by the 5:14 from Cannon
005427 Street every night. Mr. St. Clair is now thirty-seven years of
005428 age, is a man of temperate habits, a good husband, a very
005429 affectionate father, and a man who is popular with all who know
005430 him. I may add that his whole debts at the present moment, as far
005431 as we have been able to ascertain, amount to 88 pounds 10s., while
005432 he has 220 pounds standing to his credit in the Capital and
005433 Counties Bank. There is no reason, therefore, to think that money
005434 troubles have been weighing upon his mind.
005435 
005436 "Last Monday Mr. Neville St. Clair went into town rather earlier
005437 than usual, remarking before he started that he had two important
005438 commissions to perform, and that he would bring his little boy
005439 home a box of bricks. Now, by the merest chance, his wife
005440 received a telegram upon this same Monday, very shortly after his
005441 departure, to the effect that a small parcel of considerable
005442 value which she had been expecting was waiting for her at the
005443 offices of the Aberdeen Shipping Company. Now, if you are well up
005444 in your London, you will know that the office of the company is
005445 in Fresno Street, which branches out of Upper Swandam Lane, where
005446 you found me to-night. Mrs. St. Clair had her lunch, started for
005447 the City, did some shopping, proceeded to the company's office,
005448 got her packet, and found herself at exactly 4:35 walking through
005449 Swandam Lane on her way back to the station. Have you followed me
005450 so far?"
005451 
005452 "It is very clear."
005453 
005454 "If you remember, Monday was an exceedingly hot day, and Mrs. St.
005455 Clair walked slowly, glancing about in the hope of seeing a cab,
005456 as she did not like the neighbourhood in which she found herself.
005457 While she was walking in this way down Swandam Lane, she suddenly
005458 heard an ejaculation or cry, and was struck cold to see her
005459 husband looking down at her and, as it seemed to her, beckoning
005460 to her from a second-floor window. The window was open, and she
005461 distinctly saw his face, which she describes as being terribly
005462 agitated. He waved his hands frantically to her, and then
005463 vanished from the window so suddenly that it seemed to her that
005464 he had been plucked back by some irresistible force from behind.
005465 One singular point which struck her quick feminine eye was that
005466 although he wore some dark coat, such as he had started to town
005467 in, he had on neither collar nor necktie.
005468 
005469 "Convinced that something was amiss with him, she rushed down the
005470 steps--for the house was none other than the opium den in which
005471 you found me to-night--and running through the front room she
005472 attempted to ascend the stairs which led to the first floor. At
005473 the foot of the stairs, however, she met this Lascar scoundrel of
005474 whom I have spoken, who thrust her back and, aided by a Dane, who
005475 acts as assistant there, pushed her out into the street. Filled
005476 with the most maddening doubts and fears, she rushed down the
005477 lane and, by rare good-fortune, met in Fresno Street a number of
005478 constables with an inspector, all on their way to their beat. The
005479 inspector and two men accompanied her back, and in spite of the
005480 continued resistance of the proprietor, they made their way to
005481 the room in which Mr. St. Clair had last been seen. There was no
005482 sign of him there. In fact, in the whole of that floor there was
005483 no one to be found save a crippled wretch of hideous aspect, who,
005484 it seems, made his home there. Both he and the Lascar stoutly
005485 swore that no one else had been in the front room during the
005486 afternoon. So determined was their denial that the inspector was
005487 staggered, and had almost come to believe that Mrs. St. Clair had
005488 been deluded when, with a cry, she sprang at a small deal box
005489 which lay upon the table and tore the lid from it. Out there fell
005490 a cascade of children's bricks. It was the toy which he had
005491 promised to bring home.
005492 
005493 "This discovery, and the evident confusion which the cripple
005494 showed, made the inspector realise that the matter was serious.
005495 The rooms were carefully examined, and results all pointed to an
005496 abominable crime. The front room was plainly furnished as a
005497 sitting-room and led into a small bedroom, which looked out upon
005498 the back of one of the wharves. Between the wharf and the bedroom
005499 window is a narrow strip, which is dry at low tide but is covered
005500 at high tide with at least four and a half feet of water. The
005501 bedroom window was a broad one and opened from below. On
005502 examination traces of blood were to be seen upon the windowsill,
005503 and several scattered drops were visible upon the wooden floor of
005504 the bedroom. Thrust away behind a curtain in the front room were
005505 all the clothes of Mr. Neville St. Clair, with the exception of
005506 his coat. His boots, his socks, his hat, and his watch--all were
005507 there. There were no signs of violence upon any of these
005508 garments, and there were no other traces of Mr. Neville St.
005509 Clair. Out of the window he must apparently have gone for no
005510 other exit could be discovered, and the ominous bloodstains upon
005511 the sill gave little promise that he could save himself by
005512 swimming, for the tide was at its very highest at the moment of
005513 the tragedy.
005514 
005515 "And now as to the villains who seemed to be immediately
005516 implicated in the matter. The Lascar was known to be a man of the
005517 vilest antecedents, but as, by Mrs. St. Clair's story, he was
005518 known to have been at the foot of the stair within a very few
005519 seconds of her husband's appearance at the window, he could
005520 hardly have been more than an accessory to the crime. His defence
005521 was one of absolute ignorance, and he protested that he had no
005522 knowledge as to the doings of Hugh Boone, his lodger, and that he
005523 could not account in any way for the presence of the missing
005524 gentleman's clothes.
005525 
005526 "So much for the Lascar manager. Now for the sinister cripple who
005527 lives upon the second floor of the opium den, and who was
005528 certainly the last human being whose eyes rested upon Neville St.
005529 Clair. His name is Hugh Boone, and his hideous face is one which
005530 is familiar to every man who goes much to the City. He is a
005531 professional beggar, though in order to avoid the police
005532 regulations he pretends to a small trade in wax vestas. Some
005533 little distance down Threadneedle Street, upon the left-hand
005534 side, there is, as you may have remarked, a small angle in the
005535 wall. Here it is that this creature takes his daily seat,
005536 cross-legged with his tiny stock of matches on his lap, and as he
005537 is a piteous spectacle a small rain of charity descends into the
005538 greasy leather cap which lies upon the pavement beside him. I
005539 have watched the fellow more than once before ever I thought of
005540 making his professional acquaintance, and I have been surprised
005541 at the harvest which he has reaped in a short time. His
005542 appearance, you see, is so remarkable that no one can pass him
005543 without observing him. A shock of orange hair, a pale face
005544 disfigured by a horrible scar, which, by its contraction, has
005545 turned up the outer edge of his upper lip, a bulldog chin, and a
005546 pair of very penetrating dark eyes, which present a singular
005547 contrast to the colour of his hair, all mark him out from amid
005548 the common crowd of mendicants and so, too, does his wit, for he
005549 is ever ready with a reply to any piece of chaff which may be
005550 thrown at him by the passers-by. This is the man whom we now
005551 learn to have been the lodger at the opium den, and to have been
005552 the last man to see the gentleman of whom we are in quest."
005553 
005554 "But a cripple!" said I. "What could he have done single-handed
005555 against a man in the prime of life?"
005556 
005557 "He is a cripple in the sense that he walks with a limp; but in
005558 other respects he appears to be a powerful and well-nurtured man.
005559 Surely your medical experience would tell you, Watson, that
005560 weakness in one limb is often compensated for by exceptional
005561 strength in the others."
005562 
005563 "Pray continue your narrative."
005564 
005565 "Mrs. St. Clair had fainted at the sight of the blood upon the
005566 window, and she was escorted home in a cab by the police, as her
005567 presence could be of no help to them in their investigations.
005568 Inspector Barton, who had charge of the case, made a very careful
005569 examination of the premises, but without finding anything which
005570 threw any light upon the matter. One mistake had been made in not
005571 arresting Boone instantly, as he was allowed some few minutes
005572 during which he might have communicated with his friend the
005573 Lascar, but this fault was soon remedied, and he was seized and
005574 searched, without anything being found which could incriminate
005575 him. There were, it is true, some blood-stains upon his right
005576 shirt-sleeve, but he pointed to his ring-finger, which had been
005577 cut near the nail, and explained that the bleeding came from
005578 there, adding that he had been to the window not long before, and
005579 that the stains which had been observed there came doubtless from
005580 the same source. He denied strenuously having ever seen Mr.
005581 Neville St. Clair and swore that the presence of the clothes in
005582 his room was as much a mystery to him as to the police. As to
005583 Mrs. St. Clair's assertion that she had actually seen her husband
005584 at the window, he declared that she must have been either mad or
005585 dreaming. He was removed, loudly protesting, to the
005586 police-station, while the inspector remained upon the premises in
005587 the hope that the ebbing tide might afford some fresh clue.
005588 
005589 "And it did, though they hardly found upon the mud-bank what they
005590 had feared to find. It was Neville St. Clair's coat, and not
005591 Neville St. Clair, which lay uncovered as the tide receded. And
005592 what do you think they found in the pockets?"
005593 
005594 "I cannot imagine."
005595 
005596 "No, I don't think you would guess. Every pocket stuffed with
005597 pennies and half-pennies--421 pennies and 270 half-pennies. It
005598 was no wonder that it had not been swept away by the tide. But a
005599 human body is a different matter. There is a fierce eddy between
005600 the wharf and the house. It seemed likely enough that the
005601 weighted coat had remained when the stripped body had been sucked
005602 away into the river."
005603 
005604 "But I understand that all the other clothes were found in the
005605 room. Would the body be dressed in a coat alone?"
005606 
005607 "No, sir, but the facts might be met speciously enough. Suppose
005608 that this man Boone had thrust Neville St. Clair through the
005609 window, there is no human eye which could have seen the deed.
005610 What would he do then? It would of course instantly strike him
005611 that he must get rid of the tell-tale garments. He would seize
005612 the coat, then, and be in the act of throwing it out, when it
005613 would occur to him that it would swim and not sink. He has little
005614 time, for he has heard the scuffle downstairs when the wife tried
005615 to force her way up, and perhaps he has already heard from his
005616 Lascar confederate that the police are hurrying up the street.
005617 There is not an instant to be lost. He rushes to some secret
005618 hoard, where he has accumulated the fruits of his beggary, and he
005619 stuffs all the coins upon which he can lay his hands into the
005620 pockets to make sure of the coat's sinking. He throws it out, and
005621 would have done the same with the other garments had not he heard
005622 the rush of steps below, and only just had time to close the
005623 window when the police appeared."
005624 
005625 "It certainly sounds feasible."
005626 
005627 "Well, we will take it as a working hypothesis for want of a
005628 better. Boone, as I have told you, was arrested and taken to the
005629 station, but it could not be shown that there had ever before
005630 been anything against him. He had for years been known as a
005631 professional beggar, but his life appeared to have been a very
005632 quiet and innocent one. There the matter stands at present, and
005633 the questions which have to be solved--what Neville St. Clair was
005634 doing in the opium den, what happened to him when there, where is
005635 he now, and what Hugh Boone had to do with his disappearance--are
005636 all as far from a solution as ever. I confess that I cannot
005637 recall any case within my experience which looked at the first
005638 glance so simple and yet which presented such difficulties."
005639 
005640 While Sherlock Holmes had been detailing this singular series of
005641 events, we had been whirling through the outskirts of the great
005642 town until the last straggling houses had been left behind, and
005643 we rattled along with a country hedge upon either side of us.
005644 Just as he finished, however, we drove through two scattered
005645 villages, where a few lights still glimmered in the windows.
005646 
005647 "We are on the outskirts of Lee," said my companion. "We have
005648 touched on three English counties in our short drive, starting in
005649 Middlesex, passing over an angle of Surrey, and ending in Kent.
005650 See that light among the trees? That is The Cedars, and beside
005651 that lamp sits a woman whose anxious ears have already, I have
005652 little doubt, caught the clink of our horse's feet."
005653 
005654 "But why are you not conducting the case from Baker Street?" I
005655 asked.
005656 
005657 "Because there are many inquiries which must be made out here.
005658 Mrs. St. Clair has most kindly put two rooms at my disposal, and
005659 you may rest assured that she will have nothing but a welcome for
005660 my friend and colleague. I hate to meet her, Watson, when I have
005661 no news of her husband. Here we are. Whoa, there, whoa!"
005662 
005663 We had pulled up in front of a large villa which stood within its
005664 own grounds. A stable-boy had run out to the horse's head, and
005665 springing down, I followed Holmes up the small, winding
005666 gravel-drive which led to the house. As we approached, the door
005667 flew open, and a little blonde woman stood in the opening, clad
005668 in some sort of light mousseline de soie, with a touch of fluffy
005669 pink chiffon at her neck and wrists. She stood with her figure
005670 outlined against the flood of light, one hand upon the door, one
005671 half-raised in her eagerness, her body slightly bent, her head
005672 and face protruded, with eager eyes and parted lips, a standing
005673 question.
005674 
005675 "Well?" she cried, "well?" And then, seeing that there were two
005676 of us, she gave a cry of hope which sank into a groan as she saw
005677 that my companion shook his head and shrugged his shoulders.
005678 
005679 "No good news?"
005680 
005681 "None."
005682 
005683 "No bad?"
005684 
005685 "No."
005686 
005687 "Thank God for that. But come in. You must be weary, for you have
005688 had a long day."
005689 
005690 "This is my friend, Dr. Watson. He has been of most vital use to
005691 me in several of my cases, and a lucky chance has made it
005692 possible for me to bring him out and associate him with this
005693 investigation."
005694 
005695 "I am delighted to see you," said she, pressing my hand warmly.
005696 "You will, I am sure, forgive anything that may be wanting in our
005697 arrangements, when you consider the blow which has come so
005698 suddenly upon us."
005699 
005700 "My dear madam," said I, "I am an old campaigner, and if I were
005701 not I can very well see that no apology is needed. If I can be of
005702 any assistance, either to you or to my friend here, I shall be
005703 indeed happy."
005704 
005705 "Now, Mr. Sherlock Holmes," said the lady as we entered a
005706 well-lit dining-room, upon the table of which a cold supper had
005707 been laid out, "I should very much like to ask you one or two
005708 plain questions, to which I beg that you will give a plain
005709 answer."
005710 
005711 "Certainly, madam."
005712 
005713 "Do not trouble about my feelings. I am not hysterical, nor given
005714 to fainting. I simply wish to hear your real, real opinion."
005715 
005716 "Upon what point?"
005717 
005718 "In your heart of hearts, do you think that Neville is alive?"
005719 
005720 Sherlock Holmes seemed to be embarrassed by the question.
005721 "Frankly, now!" she repeated, standing upon the rug and looking
005722 keenly down at him as he leaned back in a basket-chair.
005723 
005724 "Frankly, then, madam, I do not."
005725 
005726 "You think that he is dead?"
005727 
005728 "I do."
005729 
005730 "Murdered?"
005731 
005732 "I don't say that. Perhaps."
005733 
005734 "And on what day did he meet his death?"
005735 
005736 "On Monday."
005737 
005738 "Then perhaps, Mr. Holmes, you will be good enough to explain how
005739 it is that I have received a letter from him to-day."
005740 
005741 Sherlock Holmes sprang out of his chair as if he had been
005742 galvanised.
005743 
005744 "What!" he roared.
005745 
005746 "Yes, to-day." She stood smiling, holding up a little slip of
005747 paper in the air.
005748 
005749 "May I see it?"
005750 
005751 "Certainly."
005752 
005753 He snatched it from her in his eagerness, and smoothing it out
005754 upon the table he drew over the lamp and examined it intently. I
005755 had left my chair and was gazing at it over his shoulder. The
005756 envelope was a very coarse one and was stamped with the Gravesend
005757 postmark and with the date of that very day, or rather of the day
005758 before, for it was considerably after midnight.
005759 
005760 "Coarse writing," murmured Holmes. "Surely this is not your
005761 husband's writing, madam."
005762 
005763 "No, but the enclosure is."
005764 
005765 "I perceive also that whoever addressed the envelope had to go
005766 and inquire as to the address."
005767 
005768 "How can you tell that?"
005769 
005770 "The name, you see, is in perfectly black ink, which has dried
005771 itself. The rest is of the greyish colour, which shows that
005772 blotting-paper has been used. If it had been written straight
005773 off, and then blotted, none would be of a deep black shade. This
005774 man has written the name, and there has then been a pause before
005775 he wrote the address, which can only mean that he was not
005776 familiar with it. It is, of course, a trifle, but there is
005777 nothing so important as trifles. Let us now see the letter. Ha!
005778 there has been an enclosure here!"
005779 
005780 "Yes, there was a ring. His signet-ring."
005781 
005782 "And you are sure that this is your husband's hand?"
005783 
005784 "One of his hands."
005785 
005786 "One?"
005787 
005788 "His hand when he wrote hurriedly. It is very unlike his usual
005789 writing, and yet I know it well."
005790 
005791 "'Dearest do not be frightened. All will come well. There is a
005792 huge error which it may take some little time to rectify.
005793 Wait in patience.--NEVILLE.' Written in pencil upon the fly-leaf
005794 of a book, octavo size, no water-mark. Hum! Posted to-day in
005795 Gravesend by a man with a dirty thumb. Ha! And the flap has been
005796 gummed, if I am not very much in error, by a person who had been
005797 chewing tobacco. And you have no doubt that it is your husband's
005798 hand, madam?"
005799 
005800 "None. Neville wrote those words."
005801 
005802 "And they were posted to-day at Gravesend. Well, Mrs. St. Clair,
005803 the clouds lighten, though I should not venture to say that the
005804 danger is over."
005805 
005806 "But he must be alive, Mr. Holmes."
005807 
005808 "Unless this is a clever forgery to put us on the wrong scent.
005809 The ring, after all, proves nothing. It may have been taken from
005810 him."
005811 
005812 "No, no; it is, it is his very own writing!"
005813 
005814 "Very well. It may, however, have been written on Monday and only
005815 posted to-day."
005816 
005817 "That is possible."
005818 
005819 "If so, much may have happened between."
005820 
005821 "Oh, you must not discourage me, Mr. Holmes. I know that all is
005822 well with him. There is so keen a sympathy between us that I
005823 should know if evil came upon him. On the very day that I saw him
005824 last he cut himself in the bedroom, and yet I in the dining-room
005825 rushed upstairs instantly with the utmost certainty that
005826 something had happened. Do you think that I would respond to such
005827 a trifle and yet be ignorant of his death?"
005828 
005829 "I have seen too much not to know that the impression of a woman
005830 may be more valuable than the conclusion of an analytical
005831 reasoner. And in this letter you certainly have a very strong
005832 piece of evidence to corroborate your view. But if your husband
005833 is alive and able to write letters, why should he remain away
005834 from you?"
005835 
005836 "I cannot imagine. It is unthinkable."
005837 
005838 "And on Monday he made no remarks before leaving you?"
005839 
005840 "No."
005841 
005842 "And you were surprised to see him in Swandam Lane?"
005843 
005844 "Very much so."
005845 
005846 "Was the window open?"
005847 
005848 "Yes."
005849 
005850 "Then he might have called to you?"
005851 
005852 "He might."
005853 
005854 "He only, as I understand, gave an inarticulate cry?"
005855 
005856 "Yes."
005857 
005858 "A call for help, you thought?"
005859 
005860 "Yes. He waved his hands."
005861 
005862 "But it might have been a cry of surprise. Astonishment at the
005863 unexpected sight of you might cause him to throw up his hands?"
005864 
005865 "It is possible."
005866 
005867 "And you thought he was pulled back?"
005868 
005869 "He disappeared so suddenly."
005870 
005871 "He might have leaped back. You did not see anyone else in the
005872 room?"
005873 
005874 "No, but this horrible man confessed to having been there, and
005875 the Lascar was at the foot of the stairs."
005876 
005877 "Quite so. Your husband, as far as you could see, had his
005878 ordinary clothes on?"
005879 
005880 "But without his collar or tie. I distinctly saw his bare
005881 throat."
005882 
005883 "Had he ever spoken of Swandam Lane?"
005884 
005885 "Never."
005886 
005887 "Had he ever showed any signs of having taken opium?"
005888 
005889 "Never."
005890 
005891 "Thank you, Mrs. St. Clair. Those are the principal points about
005892 which I wished to be absolutely clear. We shall now have a little
005893 supper and then retire, for we may have a very busy day
005894 to-morrow."
005895 
005896 A large and comfortable double-bedded room had been placed at our
005897 disposal, and I was quickly between the sheets, for I was weary
005898 after my night of adventure. Sherlock Holmes was a man, however,
005899 who, when he had an unsolved problem upon his mind, would go for
005900 days, and even for a week, without rest, turning it over,
005901 rearranging his facts, looking at it from every point of view
005902 until he had either fathomed it or convinced himself that his
005903 data were insufficient. It was soon evident to me that he was now
005904 preparing for an all-night sitting. He took off his coat and
005905 waistcoat, put on a large blue dressing-gown, and then wandered
005906 about the room collecting pillows from his bed and cushions from
005907 the sofa and armchairs. With these he constructed a sort of
005908 Eastern divan, upon which he perched himself cross-legged, with
005909 an ounce of shag tobacco and a box of matches laid out in front
005910 of him. In the dim light of the lamp I saw him sitting there, an
005911 old briar pipe between his lips, his eyes fixed vacantly upon the
005912 corner of the ceiling, the blue smoke curling up from him,
005913 silent, motionless, with the light shining upon his strong-set
005914 aquiline features. So he sat as I dropped off to sleep, and so he
005915 sat when a sudden ejaculation caused me to wake up, and I found
005916 the summer sun shining into the apartment. The pipe was still
005917 between his lips, the smoke still curled upward, and the room was
005918 full of a dense tobacco haze, but nothing remained of the heap of
005919 shag which I had seen upon the previous night.
005920 
005921 "Awake, Watson?" he asked.
005922 
005923 "Yes."
005924 
005925 "Game for a morning drive?"
005926 
005927 "Certainly."
005928 
005929 "Then dress. No one is stirring yet, but I know where the
005930 stable-boy sleeps, and we shall soon have the trap out." He
005931 chuckled to himself as he spoke, his eyes twinkled, and he seemed
005932 a different man to the sombre thinker of the previous night.
005933 
005934 As I dressed I glanced at my watch. It was no wonder that no one
005935 was stirring. It was twenty-five minutes past four. I had hardly
005936 finished when Holmes returned with the news that the boy was
005937 putting in the horse.
005938 
005939 "I want to test a little theory of mine," said he, pulling on his
005940 boots. "I think, Watson, that you are now standing in the
005941 presence of one of the most absolute fools in Europe. I deserve
005942 to be kicked from here to Charing Cross. But I think I have the
005943 key of the affair now."
005944 
005945 "And where is it?" I asked, smiling.
005946 
005947 "In the bathroom," he answered. "Oh, yes, I am not joking," he
005948 continued, seeing my look of incredulity. "I have just been
005949 there, and I have taken it out, and I have got it in this
005950 Gladstone bag. Come on, my boy, and we shall see whether it will
005951 not fit the lock."
005952 
005953 We made our way downstairs as quietly as possible, and out into
005954 the bright morning sunshine. In the road stood our horse and
005955 trap, with the half-clad stable-boy waiting at the head. We both
005956 sprang in, and away we dashed down the London Road. A few country
005957 carts were stirring, bearing in vegetables to the metropolis, but
005958 the lines of villas on either side were as silent and lifeless as
005959 some city in a dream.
005960 
005961 "It has been in some points a singular case," said Holmes,
005962 flicking the horse on into a gallop. "I confess that I have been
005963 as blind as a mole, but it is better to learn wisdom late than
005964 never to learn it at all."
005965 
005966 In town the earliest risers were just beginning to look sleepily
005967 from their windows as we drove through the streets of the Surrey
005968 side. Passing down the Waterloo Bridge Road we crossed over the
005969 river, and dashing up Wellington Street wheeled sharply to the
005970 right and found ourselves in Bow Street. Sherlock Holmes was well
005971 known to the force, and the two constables at the door saluted
005972 him. One of them held the horse's head while the other led us in.
005973 
005974 "Who is on duty?" asked Holmes.
005975 
005976 "Inspector Bradstreet, sir."
005977 
005978 "Ah, Bradstreet, how are you?" A tall, stout official had come
005979 down the stone-flagged passage, in a peaked cap and frogged
005980 jacket. "I wish to have a quiet word with you, Bradstreet."
005981 "Certainly, Mr. Holmes. Step into my room here." It was a small,
005982 office-like room, with a huge ledger upon the table, and a
005983 telephone projecting from the wall. The inspector sat down at his
005984 desk.
005985 
005986 "What can I do for you, Mr. Holmes?"
005987 
005988 "I called about that beggarman, Boone--the one who was charged
005989 with being concerned in the disappearance of Mr. Neville St.
005990 Clair, of Lee."
005991 
005992 "Yes. He was brought up and remanded for further inquiries."
005993 
005994 "So I heard. You have him here?"
005995 
005996 "In the cells."
005997 
005998 "Is he quiet?"
005999 
006000 "Oh, he gives no trouble. But he is a dirty scoundrel."
006001 
006002 "Dirty?"
006003 
006004 "Yes, it is all we can do to make him wash his hands, and his
006005 face is as black as a tinker's. Well, when once his case has been
006006 settled, he will have a regular prison bath; and I think, if you
006007 saw him, you would agree with me that he needed it."
006008 
006009 "I should like to see him very much."
006010 
006011 "Would you? That is easily done. Come this way. You can leave
006012 your bag."
006013 
006014 "No, I think that I'll take it."
006015 
006016 "Very good. Come this way, if you please." He led us down a
006017 passage, opened a barred door, passed down a winding stair, and
006018 brought us to a whitewashed corridor with a line of doors on each
006019 side.
006020 
006021 "The third on the right is his," said the inspector. "Here it
006022 is!" He quietly shot back a panel in the upper part of the door
006023 and glanced through.
006024 
006025 "He is asleep," said he. "You can see him very well."
006026 
006027 We both put our eyes to the grating. The prisoner lay with his
006028 face towards us, in a very deep sleep, breathing slowly and
006029 heavily. He was a middle-sized man, coarsely clad as became his
006030 calling, with a coloured shirt protruding through the rent in his
006031 tattered coat. He was, as the inspector had said, extremely
006032 dirty, but the grime which covered his face could not conceal its
006033 repulsive ugliness. A broad wheal from an old scar ran right
006034 across it from eye to chin, and by its contraction had turned up
006035 one side of the upper lip, so that three teeth were exposed in a
006036 perpetual snarl. A shock of very bright red hair grew low over
006037 his eyes and forehead.
006038 
006039 "He's a beauty, isn't he?" said the inspector.
006040 
006041 "He certainly needs a wash," remarked Holmes. "I had an idea that
006042 he might, and I took the liberty of bringing the tools with me."
006043 He opened the Gladstone bag as he spoke, and took out, to my
006044 astonishment, a very large bath-sponge.
006045 
006046 "He! he! You are a funny one," chuckled the inspector.
006047 
006048 "Now, if you will have the great goodness to open that door very
006049 quietly, we will soon make him cut a much more respectable
006050 figure."
006051 
006052 "Well, I don't know why not," said the inspector. "He doesn't
006053 look a credit to the Bow Street cells, does he?" He slipped his
006054 key into the lock, and we all very quietly entered the cell. The
006055 sleeper half turned, and then settled down once more into a deep
006056 slumber. Holmes stooped to the water-jug, moistened his sponge,
006057 and then rubbed it twice vigorously across and down the
006058 prisoner's face.
006059 
006060 "Let me introduce you," he shouted, "to Mr. Neville St. Clair, of
006061 Lee, in the county of Kent."
006062 
006063 Never in my life have I seen such a sight. The man's face peeled
006064 off under the sponge like the bark from a tree. Gone was the
006065 coarse brown tint! Gone, too, was the horrid scar which had
006066 seamed it across, and the twisted lip which had given the
006067 repulsive sneer to the face! A twitch brought away the tangled
006068 red hair, and there, sitting up in his bed, was a pale,
006069 sad-faced, refined-looking man, black-haired and smooth-skinned,
006070 rubbing his eyes and staring about him with sleepy bewilderment.
006071 Then suddenly realising the exposure, he broke into a scream and
006072 threw himself down with his face to the pillow.
006073 
006074 "Great heavens!" cried the inspector, "it is, indeed, the missing
006075 man. I know him from the photograph."
006076 
006077 The prisoner turned with the reckless air of a man who abandons
006078 himself to his destiny. "Be it so," said he. "And pray what am I
006079 charged with?"
006080 
006081 "With making away with Mr. Neville St.-- Oh, come, you can't be
006082 charged with that unless they make a case of attempted suicide of
006083 it," said the inspector with a grin. "Well, I have been
006084 twenty-seven years in the force, but this really takes the cake."
006085 
006086 "If I am Mr. Neville St. Clair, then it is obvious that no crime
006087 has been committed, and that, therefore, I am illegally
006088 detained."
006089 
006090 "No crime, but a very great error has been committed," said
006091 Holmes. "You would have done better to have trusted your wife."
006092 
006093 "It was not the wife; it was the children," groaned the prisoner.
006094 "God help me, I would not have them ashamed of their father. My
006095 God! What an exposure! What can I do?"
006096 
006097 Sherlock Holmes sat down beside him on the couch and patted him
006098 kindly on the shoulder.
006099 
006100 "If you leave it to a court of law to clear the matter up," said
006101 he, "of course you can hardly avoid publicity. On the other hand,
006102 if you convince the police authorities that there is no possible
006103 case against you, I do not know that there is any reason that the
006104 details should find their way into the papers. Inspector
006105 Bradstreet would, I am sure, make notes upon anything which you
006106 might tell us and submit it to the proper authorities. The case
006107 would then never go into court at all."
006108 
006109 "God bless you!" cried the prisoner passionately. "I would have
006110 endured imprisonment, ay, even execution, rather than have left
006111 my miserable secret as a family blot to my children.
006112 
006113 "You are the first who have ever heard my story. My father was a
006114 schoolmaster in Chesterfield, where I received an excellent
006115 education. I travelled in my youth, took to the stage, and
006116 finally became a reporter on an evening paper in London. One day
006117 my editor wished to have a series of articles upon begging in the
006118 metropolis, and I volunteered to supply them. There was the point
006119 from which all my adventures started. It was only by trying
006120 begging as an amateur that I could get the facts upon which to
006121 base my articles. When an actor I had, of course, learned all the
006122 secrets of making up, and had been famous in the green-room for
006123 my skill. I took advantage now of my attainments. I painted my
006124 face, and to make myself as pitiable as possible I made a good
006125 scar and fixed one side of my lip in a twist by the aid of a
006126 small slip of flesh-coloured plaster. Then with a red head of
006127 hair, and an appropriate dress, I took my station in the business
006128 part of the city, ostensibly as a match-seller but really as a
006129 beggar. For seven hours I plied my trade, and when I returned
006130 home in the evening I found to my surprise that I had received no
006131 less than 26s. 4d.
006132 
006133 "I wrote my articles and thought little more of the matter until,
006134 some time later, I backed a bill for a friend and had a writ
006135 served upon me for 25 pounds. I was at my wit's end where to get
006136 the money, but a sudden idea came to me. I begged a fortnight's
006137 grace from the creditor, asked for a holiday from my employers,
006138 and spent the time in begging in the City under my disguise. In
006139 ten days I had the money and had paid the debt.
006140 
006141 "Well, you can imagine how hard it was to settle down to arduous
006142 work at 2 pounds a week when I knew that I could earn as much in
006143 a day by smearing my face with a little paint, laying my cap on
006144 the ground, and sitting still. It was a long fight between my
006145 pride and the money, but the dollars won at last, and I threw up
006146 reporting and sat day after day in the corner which I had first
006147 chosen, inspiring pity by my ghastly face and filling my pockets
006148 with coppers. Only one man knew my secret. He was the keeper of a
006149 low den in which I used to lodge in Swandam Lane, where I could
006150 every morning emerge as a squalid beggar and in the evenings
006151 transform myself into a well-dressed man about town. This fellow,
006152 a Lascar, was well paid by me for his rooms, so that I knew that
006153 my secret was safe in his possession.
006154 
006155 "Well, very soon I found that I was saving considerable sums of
006156 money. I do not mean that any beggar in the streets of London
006157 could earn 700 pounds a year--which is less than my average
006158 takings--but I had exceptional advantages in my power of making
006159 up, and also in a facility of repartee, which improved by
006160 practice and made me quite a recognised character in the City.
006161 All day a stream of pennies, varied by silver, poured in upon me,
006162 and it was a very bad day in which I failed to take 2 pounds.
006163 
006164 "As I grew richer I grew more ambitious, took a house in the
006165 country, and eventually married, without anyone having a
006166 suspicion as to my real occupation. My dear wife knew that I had
006167 business in the City. She little knew what.
006168 
006169 "Last Monday I had finished for the day and was dressing in my
006170 room above the opium den when I looked out of my window and saw,
006171 to my horror and astonishment, that my wife was standing in the
006172 street, with her eyes fixed full upon me. I gave a cry of
006173 surprise, threw up my arms to cover my face, and, rushing to my
006174 confidant, the Lascar, entreated him to prevent anyone from
006175 coming up to me. I heard her voice downstairs, but I knew that
006176 she could not ascend. Swiftly I threw off my clothes, pulled on
006177 those of a beggar, and put on my pigments and wig. Even a wife's
006178 eyes could not pierce so complete a disguise. But then it
006179 occurred to me that there might be a search in the room, and that
006180 the clothes might betray me. I threw open the window, reopening
006181 by my violence a small cut which I had inflicted upon myself in
006182 the bedroom that morning. Then I seized my coat, which was
006183 weighted by the coppers which I had just transferred to it from
006184 the leather bag in which I carried my takings. I hurled it out of
006185 the window, and it disappeared into the Thames. The other clothes
006186 would have followed, but at that moment there was a rush of
006187 constables up the stair, and a few minutes after I found, rather,
006188 I confess, to my relief, that instead of being identified as Mr.
006189 Neville St. Clair, I was arrested as his murderer.
006190 
006191 "I do not know that there is anything else for me to explain. I
006192 was determined to preserve my disguise as long as possible, and
006193 hence my preference for a dirty face. Knowing that my wife would
006194 be terribly anxious, I slipped off my ring and confided it to the
006195 Lascar at a moment when no constable was watching me, together
006196 with a hurried scrawl, telling her that she had no cause to
006197 fear."
006198 
006199 "That note only reached her yesterday," said Holmes.
006200 
006201 "Good God! What a week she must have spent!"
006202 
006203 "The police have watched this Lascar," said Inspector Bradstreet,
006204 "and I can quite understand that he might find it difficult to
006205 post a letter unobserved. Probably he handed it to some sailor
006206 customer of his, who forgot all about it for some days."
006207 
006208 "That was it," said Holmes, nodding approvingly; "I have no doubt
006209 of it. But have you never been prosecuted for begging?"
006210 
006211 "Many times; but what was a fine to me?"
006212 
006213 "It must stop here, however," said Bradstreet. "If the police are
006214 to hush this thing up, there must be no more of Hugh Boone."
006215 
006216 "I have sworn it by the most solemn oaths which a man can take."
006217 
006218 "In that case I think that it is probable that no further steps
006219 may be taken. But if you are found again, then all must come out.
006220 I am sure, Mr. Holmes, that we are very much indebted to you for
006221 having cleared the matter up. I wish I knew how you reach your
006222 results."
006223 
006224 "I reached this one," said my friend, "by sitting upon five
006225 pillows and consuming an ounce of shag. I think, Watson, that if
006226 we drive to Baker Street we shall just be in time for breakfast."
006227 
006228 
006229 
006230 VII. THE ADVENTURE OF THE BLUE CARBUNCLE
006231 
006232 I had called upon my friend Sherlock Holmes upon the second
006233 morning after Christmas, with the intention of wishing him the
006234 compliments of the season. He was lounging upon the sofa in a
006235 purple dressing-gown, a pipe-rack within his reach upon the
006236 right, and a pile of crumpled morning papers, evidently newly
006237 studied, near at hand. Beside the couch was a wooden chair, and
006238 on the angle of the back hung a very seedy and disreputable
006239 hard-felt hat, much the worse for wear, and cracked in several
006240 places. A lens and a forceps lying upon the seat of the chair
006241 suggested that the hat had been suspended in this manner for the
006242 purpose of examination.
006243 
006244 "You are engaged," said I; "perhaps I interrupt you."
006245 
006246 "Not at all. I am glad to have a friend with whom I can discuss
006247 my results. The matter is a perfectly trivial one"--he jerked his
006248 thumb in the direction of the old hat--"but there are points in
006249 connection with it which are not entirely devoid of interest and
006250 even of instruction."
006251 
006252 I seated myself in his armchair and warmed my hands before his
006253 crackling fire, for a sharp frost had set in, and the windows
006254 were thick with the ice crystals. "I suppose," I remarked, "that,
006255 homely as it looks, this thing has some deadly story linked on to
006256 it--that it is the clue which will guide you in the solution of
006257 some mystery and the punishment of some crime."
006258 
006259 "No, no. No crime," said Sherlock Holmes, laughing. "Only one of
006260 those whimsical little incidents which will happen when you have
006261 four million human beings all jostling each other within the
006262 space of a few square miles. Amid the action and reaction of so
006263 dense a swarm of humanity, every possible combination of events
006264 may be expected to take place, and many a little problem will be
006265 presented which may be striking and bizarre without being
006266 criminal. We have already had experience of such."
006267 
006268 "So much so," I remarked, "that of the last six cases which I
006269 have added to my notes, three have been entirely free of any
006270 legal crime."
006271 
006272 "Precisely. You allude to my attempt to recover the Irene Adler
006273 papers, to the singular case of Miss Mary Sutherland, and to the
006274 adventure of the man with the twisted lip. Well, I have no doubt
006275 that this small matter will fall into the same innocent category.
006276 You know Peterson, the commissionaire?"
006277 
006278 "Yes."
006279 
006280 "It is to him that this trophy belongs."
006281 
006282 "It is his hat."
006283 
006284 "No, no, he found it. Its owner is unknown. I beg that you will
006285 look upon it not as a battered billycock but as an intellectual
006286 problem. And, first, as to how it came here. It arrived upon
006287 Christmas morning, in company with a good fat goose, which is, I
006288 have no doubt, roasting at this moment in front of Peterson's
006289 fire. The facts are these: about four o'clock on Christmas
006290 morning, Peterson, who, as you know, is a very honest fellow, was
006291 returning from some small jollification and was making his way
006292 homeward down Tottenham Court Road. In front of him he saw, in
006293 the gaslight, a tallish man, walking with a slight stagger, and
006294 carrying a white goose slung over his shoulder. As he reached the
006295 corner of Goodge Street, a row broke out between this stranger
006296 and a little knot of roughs. One of the latter knocked off the
006297 man's hat, on which he raised his stick to defend himself and,
006298 swinging it over his head, smashed the shop window behind him.
006299 Peterson had rushed forward to protect the stranger from his
006300 assailants; but the man, shocked at having broken the window, and
006301 seeing an official-looking person in uniform rushing towards him,
006302 dropped his goose, took to his heels, and vanished amid the
006303 labyrinth of small streets which lie at the back of Tottenham
006304 Court Road. The roughs had also fled at the appearance of
006305 Peterson, so that he was left in possession of the field of
006306 battle, and also of the spoils of victory in the shape of this
006307 battered hat and a most unimpeachable Christmas goose."
006308 
006309 "Which surely he restored to their owner?"
006310 
006311 "My dear fellow, there lies the problem. It is true that 'For
006312 Mrs. Henry Baker' was printed upon a small card which was tied to
006313 the bird's left leg, and it is also true that the initials 'H.
006314 B.' are legible upon the lining of this hat, but as there are
006315 some thousands of Bakers, and some hundreds of Henry Bakers in
006316 this city of ours, it is not easy to restore lost property to any
006317 one of them."
006318 
006319 "What, then, did Peterson do?"
006320 
006321 "He brought round both hat and goose to me on Christmas morning,
006322 knowing that even the smallest problems are of interest to me.
006323 The goose we retained until this morning, when there were signs
006324 that, in spite of the slight frost, it would be well that it
006325 should be eaten without unnecessary delay. Its finder has carried
006326 it off, therefore, to fulfil the ultimate destiny of a goose,
006327 while I continue to retain the hat of the unknown gentleman who
006328 lost his Christmas dinner."
006329 
006330 "Did he not advertise?"
006331 
006332 "No."
006333 
006334 "Then, what clue could you have as to his identity?"
006335 
006336 "Only as much as we can deduce."
006337 
006338 "From his hat?"
006339 
006340 "Precisely."
006341 
006342 "But you are joking. What can you gather from this old battered
006343 felt?"
006344 
006345 "Here is my lens. You know my methods. What can you gather
006346 yourself as to the individuality of the man who has worn this
006347 article?"
006348 
006349 I took the tattered object in my hands and turned it over rather
