006350 ruefully. It was a very ordinary black hat of the usual round
006351 shape, hard and much the worse for wear. The lining had been of
006352 red silk, but was a good deal discoloured. There was no maker's
006353 name; but, as Holmes had remarked, the initials "H. B." were
006354 scrawled upon one side. It was pierced in the brim for a
006355 hat-securer, but the elastic was missing. For the rest, it was
006356 cracked, exceedingly dusty, and spotted in several places,
006357 although there seemed to have been some attempt to hide the
006358 discoloured patches by smearing them with ink.
006359 
006360 "I can see nothing," said I, handing it back to my friend.
006361 
006362 "On the contrary, Watson, you can see everything. You fail,
006363 however, to reason from what you see. You are too timid in
006364 drawing your inferences."
006365 
006366 "Then, pray tell me what it is that you can infer from this hat?"
006367 
006368 He picked it up and gazed at it in the peculiar introspective
006369 fashion which was characteristic of him. "It is perhaps less
006370 suggestive than it might have been," he remarked, "and yet there
006371 are a few inferences which are very distinct, and a few others
006372 which represent at least a strong balance of probability. That
006373 the man was highly intellectual is of course obvious upon the
006374 face of it, and also that he was fairly well-to-do within the
006375 last three years, although he has now fallen upon evil days. He
006376 had foresight, but has less now than formerly, pointing to a
006377 moral retrogression, which, when taken with the decline of his
006378 fortunes, seems to indicate some evil influence, probably drink,
006379 at work upon him. This may account also for the obvious fact that
006380 his wife has ceased to love him."
006381 
006382 "My dear Holmes!"
006383 
006384 "He has, however, retained some degree of self-respect," he
006385 continued, disregarding my remonstrance. "He is a man who leads a
006386 sedentary life, goes out little, is out of training entirely, is
006387 middle-aged, has grizzled hair which he has had cut within the
006388 last few days, and which he anoints with lime-cream. These are
006389 the more patent facts which are to be deduced from his hat. Also,
006390 by the way, that it is extremely improbable that he has gas laid
006391 on in his house."
006392 
006393 "You are certainly joking, Holmes."
006394 
006395 "Not in the least. Is it possible that even now, when I give you
006396 these results, you are unable to see how they are attained?"
006397 
006398 "I have no doubt that I am very stupid, but I must confess that I
006399 am unable to follow you. For example, how did you deduce that
006400 this man was intellectual?"
006401 
006402 For answer Holmes clapped the hat upon his head. It came right
006403 over the forehead and settled upon the bridge of his nose. "It is
006404 a question of cubic capacity," said he; "a man with so large a
006405 brain must have something in it."
006406 
006407 "The decline of his fortunes, then?"
006408 
006409 "This hat is three years old. These flat brims curled at the edge
006410 came in then. It is a hat of the very best quality. Look at the
006411 band of ribbed silk and the excellent lining. If this man could
006412 afford to buy so expensive a hat three years ago, and has had no
006413 hat since, then he has assuredly gone down in the world."
006414 
006415 "Well, that is clear enough, certainly. But how about the
006416 foresight and the moral retrogression?"
006417 
006418 Sherlock Holmes laughed. "Here is the foresight," said he putting
006419 his finger upon the little disc and loop of the hat-securer.
006420 "They are never sold upon hats. If this man ordered one, it is a
006421 sign of a certain amount of foresight, since he went out of his
006422 way to take this precaution against the wind. But since we see
006423 that he has broken the elastic and has not troubled to replace
006424 it, it is obvious that he has less foresight now than formerly,
006425 which is a distinct proof of a weakening nature. On the other
006426 hand, he has endeavoured to conceal some of these stains upon the
006427 felt by daubing them with ink, which is a sign that he has not
006428 entirely lost his self-respect."
006429 
006430 "Your reasoning is certainly plausible."
006431 
006432 "The further points, that he is middle-aged, that his hair is
006433 grizzled, that it has been recently cut, and that he uses
006434 lime-cream, are all to be gathered from a close examination of the
006435 lower part of the lining. The lens discloses a large number of
006436 hair-ends, clean cut by the scissors of the barber. They all
006437 appear to be adhesive, and there is a distinct odour of
006438 lime-cream. This dust, you will observe, is not the gritty, grey
006439 dust of the street but the fluffy brown dust of the house,
006440 showing that it has been hung up indoors most of the time, while
006441 the marks of moisture upon the inside are proof positive that the
006442 wearer perspired very freely, and could therefore, hardly be in
006443 the best of training."
006444 
006445 "But his wife--you said that she had ceased to love him."
006446 
006447 "This hat has not been brushed for weeks. When I see you, my dear
006448 Watson, with a week's accumulation of dust upon your hat, and
006449 when your wife allows you to go out in such a state, I shall fear
006450 that you also have been unfortunate enough to lose your wife's
006451 affection."
006452 
006453 "But he might be a bachelor."
006454 
006455 "Nay, he was bringing home the goose as a peace-offering to his
006456 wife. Remember the card upon the bird's leg."
006457 
006458 "You have an answer to everything. But how on earth do you deduce
006459 that the gas is not laid on in his house?"
006460 
006461 "One tallow stain, or even two, might come by chance; but when I
006462 see no less than five, I think that there can be little doubt
006463 that the individual must be brought into frequent contact with
006464 burning tallow--walks upstairs at night probably with his hat in
006465 one hand and a guttering candle in the other. Anyhow, he never
006466 got tallow-stains from a gas-jet. Are you satisfied?"
006467 
006468 "Well, it is very ingenious," said I, laughing; "but since, as
006469 you said just now, there has been no crime committed, and no harm
006470 done save the loss of a goose, all this seems to be rather a
006471 waste of energy."
006472 
006473 Sherlock Holmes had opened his mouth to reply, when the door flew
006474 open, and Peterson, the commissionaire, rushed into the apartment
006475 with flushed cheeks and the face of a man who is dazed with
006476 astonishment.
006477 
006478 "The goose, Mr. Holmes! The goose, sir!" he gasped.
006479 
006480 "Eh? What of it, then? Has it returned to life and flapped off
006481 through the kitchen window?" Holmes twisted himself round upon
006482 the sofa to get a fairer view of the man's excited face.
006483 
006484 "See here, sir! See what my wife found in its crop!" He held out
006485 his hand and displayed upon the centre of the palm a brilliantly
006486 scintillating blue stone, rather smaller than a bean in size, but
006487 of such purity and radiance that it twinkled like an electric
006488 point in the dark hollow of his hand.
006489 
006490 Sherlock Holmes sat up with a whistle. "By Jove, Peterson!" said
006491 he, "this is treasure trove indeed. I suppose you know what you
006492 have got?"
006493 
006494 "A diamond, sir? A precious stone. It cuts into glass as though
006495 it were putty."
006496 
006497 "It's more than a precious stone. It is the precious stone."
006498 
006499 "Not the Countess of Morcar's blue carbuncle!" I ejaculated.
006500 
006501 "Precisely so. I ought to know its size and shape, seeing that I
006502 have read the advertisement about it in The Times every day
006503 lately. It is absolutely unique, and its value can only be
006504 conjectured, but the reward offered of 1000 pounds is certainly
006505 not within a twentieth part of the market price."
006506 
006507 "A thousand pounds! Great Lord of mercy!" The commissionaire
006508 plumped down into a chair and stared from one to the other of us.
006509 
006510 "That is the reward, and I have reason to know that there are
006511 sentimental considerations in the background which would induce
006512 the Countess to part with half her fortune if she could but
006513 recover the gem."
006514 
006515 "It was lost, if I remember aright, at the Hotel Cosmopolitan," I
006516 remarked.
006517 
006518 "Precisely so, on December 22nd, just five days ago. John Horner,
006519 a plumber, was accused of having abstracted it from the lady's
006520 jewel-case. The evidence against him was so strong that the case
006521 has been referred to the Assizes. I have some account of the
006522 matter here, I believe." He rummaged amid his newspapers,
006523 glancing over the dates, until at last he smoothed one out,
006524 doubled it over, and read the following paragraph:
006525 
006526 "Hotel Cosmopolitan Jewel Robbery. John Horner, 26, plumber, was
006527 brought up upon the charge of having upon the 22nd inst.,
006528 abstracted from the jewel-case of the Countess of Morcar the
006529 valuable gem known as the blue carbuncle. James Ryder,
006530 upper-attendant at the hotel, gave his evidence to the effect
006531 that he had shown Horner up to the dressing-room of the Countess
006532 of Morcar upon the day of the robbery in order that he might
006533 solder the second bar of the grate, which was loose. He had
006534 remained with Horner some little time, but had finally been
006535 called away. On returning, he found that Horner had disappeared,
006536 that the bureau had been forced open, and that the small morocco
006537 casket in which, as it afterwards transpired, the Countess was
006538 accustomed to keep her jewel, was lying empty upon the
006539 dressing-table. Ryder instantly gave the alarm, and Horner was
006540 arrested the same evening; but the stone could not be found
006541 either upon his person or in his rooms. Catherine Cusack, maid to
006542 the Countess, deposed to having heard Ryder's cry of dismay on
006543 discovering the robbery, and to having rushed into the room,
006544 where she found matters as described by the last witness.
006545 Inspector Bradstreet, B division, gave evidence as to the arrest
006546 of Horner, who struggled frantically, and protested his innocence
006547 in the strongest terms. Evidence of a previous conviction for
006548 robbery having been given against the prisoner, the magistrate
006549 refused to deal summarily with the offence, but referred it to
006550 the Assizes. Horner, who had shown signs of intense emotion
006551 during the proceedings, fainted away at the conclusion and was
006552 carried out of court."
006553 
006554 "Hum! So much for the police-court," said Holmes thoughtfully,
006555 tossing aside the paper. "The question for us now to solve is the
006556 sequence of events leading from a rifled jewel-case at one end to
006557 the crop of a goose in Tottenham Court Road at the other. You
006558 see, Watson, our little deductions have suddenly assumed a much
006559 more important and less innocent aspect. Here is the stone; the
006560 stone came from the goose, and the goose came from Mr. Henry
006561 Baker, the gentleman with the bad hat and all the other
006562 characteristics with which I have bored you. So now we must set
006563 ourselves very seriously to finding this gentleman and
006564 ascertaining what part he has played in this little mystery. To
006565 do this, we must try the simplest means first, and these lie
006566 undoubtedly in an advertisement in all the evening papers. If
006567 this fail, I shall have recourse to other methods."
006568 
006569 "What will you say?"
006570 
006571 "Give me a pencil and that slip of paper. Now, then: 'Found at
006572 the corner of Goodge Street, a goose and a black felt hat. Mr.
006573 Henry Baker can have the same by applying at 6:30 this evening at
006574 221B, Baker Street.' That is clear and concise."
006575 
006576 "Very. But will he see it?"
006577 
006578 "Well, he is sure to keep an eye on the papers, since, to a poor
006579 man, the loss was a heavy one. He was clearly so scared by his
006580 mischance in breaking the window and by the approach of Peterson
006581 that he thought of nothing but flight, but since then he must
006582 have bitterly regretted the impulse which caused him to drop his
006583 bird. Then, again, the introduction of his name will cause him to
006584 see it, for everyone who knows him will direct his attention to
006585 it. Here you are, Peterson, run down to the advertising agency
006586 and have this put in the evening papers."
006587 
006588 "In which, sir?"
006589 
006590 "Oh, in the Globe, Star, Pall Mall, St. James's, Evening News,
006591 Standard, Echo, and any others that occur to you."
006592 
006593 "Very well, sir. And this stone?"
006594 
006595 "Ah, yes, I shall keep the stone. Thank you. And, I say,
006596 Peterson, just buy a goose on your way back and leave it here
006597 with me, for we must have one to give to this gentleman in place
006598 of the one which your family is now devouring."
006599 
006600 When the commissionaire had gone, Holmes took up the stone and
006601 held it against the light. "It's a bonny thing," said he. "Just
006602 see how it glints and sparkles. Of course it is a nucleus and
006603 focus of crime. Every good stone is. They are the devil's pet
006604 baits. In the larger and older jewels every facet may stand for a
006605 bloody deed. This stone is not yet twenty years old. It was found
006606 in the banks of the Amoy River in southern China and is remarkable
006607 in having every characteristic of the carbuncle, save that it is
006608 blue in shade instead of ruby red. In spite of its youth, it has
006609 already a sinister history. There have been two murders, a
006610 vitriol-throwing, a suicide, and several robberies brought about
006611 for the sake of this forty-grain weight of crystallised charcoal.
006612 Who would think that so pretty a toy would be a purveyor to the
006613 gallows and the prison? I'll lock it up in my strong box now and
006614 drop a line to the Countess to say that we have it."
006615 
006616 "Do you think that this man Horner is innocent?"
006617 
006618 "I cannot tell."
006619 
006620 "Well, then, do you imagine that this other one, Henry Baker, had
006621 anything to do with the matter?"
006622 
006623 "It is, I think, much more likely that Henry Baker is an
006624 absolutely innocent man, who had no idea that the bird which he
006625 was carrying was of considerably more value than if it were made
006626 of solid gold. That, however, I shall determine by a very simple
006627 test if we have an answer to our advertisement."
006628 
006629 "And you can do nothing until then?"
006630 
006631 "Nothing."
006632 
006633 "In that case I shall continue my professional round. But I shall
006634 come back in the evening at the hour you have mentioned, for I
006635 should like to see the solution of so tangled a business."
006636 
006637 "Very glad to see you. I dine at seven. There is a woodcock, I
006638 believe. By the way, in view of recent occurrences, perhaps I
006639 ought to ask Mrs. Hudson to examine its crop."
006640 
006641 I had been delayed at a case, and it was a little after half-past
006642 six when I found myself in Baker Street once more. As I
006643 approached the house I saw a tall man in a Scotch bonnet with a
006644 coat which was buttoned up to his chin waiting outside in the
006645 bright semicircle which was thrown from the fanlight. Just as I
006646 arrived the door was opened, and we were shown up together to
006647 Holmes' room.
006648 
006649 "Mr. Henry Baker, I believe," said he, rising from his armchair
006650 and greeting his visitor with the easy air of geniality which he
006651 could so readily assume. "Pray take this chair by the fire, Mr.
006652 Baker. It is a cold night, and I observe that your circulation is
006653 more adapted for summer than for winter. Ah, Watson, you have
006654 just come at the right time. Is that your hat, Mr. Baker?"
006655 
006656 "Yes, sir, that is undoubtedly my hat."
006657 
006658 He was a large man with rounded shoulders, a massive head, and a
006659 broad, intelligent face, sloping down to a pointed beard of
006660 grizzled brown. A touch of red in nose and cheeks, with a slight
006661 tremor of his extended hand, recalled Holmes' surmise as to his
006662 habits. His rusty black frock-coat was buttoned right up in
006663 front, with the collar turned up, and his lank wrists protruded
006664 from his sleeves without a sign of cuff or shirt. He spoke in a
006665 slow staccato fashion, choosing his words with care, and gave the
006666 impression generally of a man of learning and letters who had had
006667 ill-usage at the hands of fortune.
006668 
006669 "We have retained these things for some days," said Holmes,
006670 "because we expected to see an advertisement from you giving your
006671 address. I am at a loss to know now why you did not advertise."
006672 
006673 Our visitor gave a rather shamefaced laugh. "Shillings have not
006674 been so plentiful with me as they once were," he remarked. "I had
006675 no doubt that the gang of roughs who assaulted me had carried off
006676 both my hat and the bird. I did not care to spend more money in a
006677 hopeless attempt at recovering them."
006678 
006679 "Very naturally. By the way, about the bird, we were compelled to
006680 eat it."
006681 
006682 "To eat it!" Our visitor half rose from his chair in his
006683 excitement.
006684 
006685 "Yes, it would have been of no use to anyone had we not done so.
006686 But I presume that this other goose upon the sideboard, which is
006687 about the same weight and perfectly fresh, will answer your
006688 purpose equally well?"
006689 
006690 "Oh, certainly, certainly," answered Mr. Baker with a sigh of
006691 relief.
006692 
006693 "Of course, we still have the feathers, legs, crop, and so on of
006694 your own bird, so if you wish--"
006695 
006696 The man burst into a hearty laugh. "They might be useful to me as
006697 relics of my adventure," said he, "but beyond that I can hardly
006698 see what use the disjecta membra of my late acquaintance are
006699 going to be to me. No, sir, I think that, with your permission, I
006700 will confine my attentions to the excellent bird which I perceive
006701 upon the sideboard."
006702 
006703 Sherlock Holmes glanced sharply across at me with a slight shrug
006704 of his shoulders.
006705 
006706 "There is your hat, then, and there your bird," said he. "By the
006707 way, would it bore you to tell me where you got the other one
006708 from? I am somewhat of a fowl fancier, and I have seldom seen a
006709 better grown goose."
006710 
006711 "Certainly, sir," said Baker, who had risen and tucked his newly
006712 gained property under his arm. "There are a few of us who
006713 frequent the Alpha Inn, near the Museum--we are to be found in
006714 the Museum itself during the day, you understand. This year our
006715 good host, Windigate by name, instituted a goose club, by which,
006716 on consideration of some few pence every week, we were each to
006717 receive a bird at Christmas. My pence were duly paid, and the
006718 rest is familiar to you. I am much indebted to you, sir, for a
006719 Scotch bonnet is fitted neither to my years nor my gravity." With
006720 a comical pomposity of manner he bowed solemnly to both of us and
006721 strode off upon his way.
006722 
006723 "So much for Mr. Henry Baker," said Holmes when he had closed the
006724 door behind him. "It is quite certain that he knows nothing
006725 whatever about the matter. Are you hungry, Watson?"
006726 
006727 "Not particularly."
006728 
006729 "Then I suggest that we turn our dinner into a supper and follow
006730 up this clue while it is still hot."
006731 
006732 "By all means."
006733 
006734 It was a bitter night, so we drew on our ulsters and wrapped
006735 cravats about our throats. Outside, the stars were shining coldly
006736 in a cloudless sky, and the breath of the passers-by blew out
006737 into smoke like so many pistol shots. Our footfalls rang out
006738 crisply and loudly as we swung through the doctors' quarter,
006739 Wimpole Street, Harley Street, and so through Wigmore Street into
006740 Oxford Street. In a quarter of an hour we were in Bloomsbury at
006741 the Alpha Inn, which is a small public-house at the corner of one
006742 of the streets which runs down into Holborn. Holmes pushed open
006743 the door of the private bar and ordered two glasses of beer from
006744 the ruddy-faced, white-aproned landlord.
006745 
006746 "Your beer should be excellent if it is as good as your geese,"
006747 said he.
006748 
006749 "My geese!" The man seemed surprised.
006750 
006751 "Yes. I was speaking only half an hour ago to Mr. Henry Baker,
006752 who was a member of your goose club."
006753 
006754 "Ah! yes, I see. But you see, sir, them's not our geese."
006755 
006756 "Indeed! Whose, then?"
006757 
006758 "Well, I got the two dozen from a salesman in Covent Garden."
006759 
006760 "Indeed? I know some of them. Which was it?"
006761 
006762 "Breckinridge is his name."
006763 
006764 "Ah! I don't know him. Well, here's your good health landlord,
006765 and prosperity to your house. Good-night."
006766 
006767 "Now for Mr. Breckinridge," he continued, buttoning up his coat
006768 as we came out into the frosty air. "Remember, Watson that though
006769 we have so homely a thing as a goose at one end of this chain, we
006770 have at the other a man who will certainly get seven years' penal
006771 servitude unless we can establish his innocence. It is possible
006772 that our inquiry may but confirm his guilt; but, in any case, we
006773 have a line of investigation which has been missed by the police,
006774 and which a singular chance has placed in our hands. Let us
006775 follow it out to the bitter end. Faces to the south, then, and
006776 quick march!"
006777 
006778 We passed across Holborn, down Endell Street, and so through a
006779 zigzag of slums to Covent Garden Market. One of the largest
006780 stalls bore the name of Breckinridge upon it, and the proprietor
006781 a horsey-looking man, with a sharp face and trim side-whiskers was
006782 helping a boy to put up the shutters.
006783 
006784 "Good-evening. It's a cold night," said Holmes.
006785 
006786 The salesman nodded and shot a questioning glance at my
006787 companion.
006788 
006789 "Sold out of geese, I see," continued Holmes, pointing at the
006790 bare slabs of marble.
006791 
006792 "Let you have five hundred to-morrow morning."
006793 
006794 "That's no good."
006795 
006796 "Well, there are some on the stall with the gas-flare."
006797 
006798 "Ah, but I was recommended to you."
006799 
006800 "Who by?"
006801 
006802 "The landlord of the Alpha."
006803 
006804 "Oh, yes; I sent him a couple of dozen."
006805 
006806 "Fine birds they were, too. Now where did you get them from?"
006807 
006808 To my surprise the question provoked a burst of anger from the
006809 salesman.
006810 
006811 "Now, then, mister," said he, with his head cocked and his arms
006812 akimbo, "what are you driving at? Let's have it straight, now."
006813 
006814 "It is straight enough. I should like to know who sold you the
006815 geese which you supplied to the Alpha."
006816 
006817 "Well then, I shan't tell you. So now!"
006818 
006819 "Oh, it is a matter of no importance; but I don't know why you
006820 should be so warm over such a trifle."
006821 
006822 "Warm! You'd be as warm, maybe, if you were as pestered as I am.
006823 When I pay good money for a good article there should be an end
006824 of the business; but it's 'Where are the geese?' and 'Who did you
006825 sell the geese to?' and 'What will you take for the geese?' One
006826 would think they were the only geese in the world, to hear the
006827 fuss that is made over them."
006828 
006829 "Well, I have no connection with any other people who have been
006830 making inquiries," said Holmes carelessly. "If you won't tell us
006831 the bet is off, that is all. But I'm always ready to back my
006832 opinion on a matter of fowls, and I have a fiver on it that the
006833 bird I ate is country bred."
006834 
006835 "Well, then, you've lost your fiver, for it's town bred," snapped
006836 the salesman.
006837 
006838 "It's nothing of the kind."
006839 
006840 "I say it is."
006841 
006842 "I don't believe it."
006843 
006844 "D'you think you know more about fowls than I, who have handled
006845 them ever since I was a nipper? I tell you, all those birds that
006846 went to the Alpha were town bred."
006847 
006848 "You'll never persuade me to believe that."
006849 
006850 "Will you bet, then?"
006851 
006852 "It's merely taking your money, for I know that I am right. But
006853 I'll have a sovereign on with you, just to teach you not to be
006854 obstinate."
006855 
006856 The salesman chuckled grimly. "Bring me the books, Bill," said
006857 he.
006858 
006859 The small boy brought round a small thin volume and a great
006860 greasy-backed one, laying them out together beneath the hanging
006861 lamp.
006862 
006863 "Now then, Mr. Cocksure," said the salesman, "I thought that I
006864 was out of geese, but before I finish you'll find that there is
006865 still one left in my shop. You see this little book?"
006866 
006867 "Well?"
006868 
006869 "That's the list of the folk from whom I buy. D'you see? Well,
006870 then, here on this page are the country folk, and the numbers
006871 after their names are where their accounts are in the big ledger.
006872 Now, then! You see this other page in red ink? Well, that is a
006873 list of my town suppliers. Now, look at that third name. Just
006874 read it out to me."
006875 
006876 "Mrs. Oakshott, 117, Brixton Road--249," read Holmes.
006877 
006878 "Quite so. Now turn that up in the ledger."
006879 
006880 Holmes turned to the page indicated. "Here you are, 'Mrs.
006881 Oakshott, 117, Brixton Road, egg and poultry supplier.'"
006882 
006883 "Now, then, what's the last entry?"
006884 
006885 "'December 22nd. Twenty-four geese at 7s. 6d.'"
006886 
006887 "Quite so. There you are. And underneath?"
006888 
006889 "'Sold to Mr. Windigate of the Alpha, at 12s.'"
006890 
006891 "What have you to say now?"
006892 
006893 Sherlock Holmes looked deeply chagrined. He drew a sovereign from
006894 his pocket and threw it down upon the slab, turning away with the
006895 air of a man whose disgust is too deep for words. A few yards off
006896 he stopped under a lamp-post and laughed in the hearty, noiseless
006897 fashion which was peculiar to him.
006898 
006899 "When you see a man with whiskers of that cut and the 'Pink 'un'
006900 protruding out of his pocket, you can always draw him by a bet,"
006901 said he. "I daresay that if I had put 100 pounds down in front of
006902 him, that man would not have given me such complete information
006903 as was drawn from him by the idea that he was doing me on a
006904 wager. Well, Watson, we are, I fancy, nearing the end of our
006905 quest, and the only point which remains to be determined is
006906 whether we should go on to this Mrs. Oakshott to-night, or
006907 whether we should reserve it for to-morrow. It is clear from what
006908 that surly fellow said that there are others besides ourselves
006909 who are anxious about the matter, and I should--"
006910 
006911 His remarks were suddenly cut short by a loud hubbub which broke
006912 out from the stall which we had just left. Turning round we saw a
006913 little rat-faced fellow standing in the centre of the circle of
006914 yellow light which was thrown by the swinging lamp, while
006915 Breckinridge, the salesman, framed in the door of his stall, was
006916 shaking his fists fiercely at the cringing figure.
006917 
006918 "I've had enough of you and your geese," he shouted. "I wish you
006919 were all at the devil together. If you come pestering me any more
006920 with your silly talk I'll set the dog at you. You bring Mrs.
006921 Oakshott here and I'll answer her, but what have you to do with
006922 it? Did I buy the geese off you?"
006923 
006924 "No; but one of them was mine all the same," whined the little
006925 man.
006926 
006927 "Well, then, ask Mrs. Oakshott for it."
006928 
006929 "She told me to ask you."
006930 
006931 "Well, you can ask the King of Proosia, for all I care. I've had
006932 enough of it. Get out of this!" He rushed fiercely forward, and
006933 the inquirer flitted away into the darkness.
006934 
006935 "Ha! this may save us a visit to Brixton Road," whispered Holmes.
006936 "Come with me, and we will see what is to be made of this
006937 fellow." Striding through the scattered knots of people who
006938 lounged round the flaring stalls, my companion speedily overtook
006939 the little man and touched him upon the shoulder. He sprang
006940 round, and I could see in the gas-light that every vestige of
006941 colour had been driven from his face.
006942 
006943 "Who are you, then? What do you want?" he asked in a quavering
006944 voice.
006945 
006946 "You will excuse me," said Holmes blandly, "but I could not help
006947 overhearing the questions which you put to the salesman just now.
006948 I think that I could be of assistance to you."
006949 
006950 "You? Who are you? How could you know anything of the matter?"
006951 
006952 "My name is Sherlock Holmes. It is my business to know what other
006953 people don't know."
006954 
006955 "But you can know nothing of this?"
006956 
006957 "Excuse me, I know everything of it. You are endeavouring to
006958 trace some geese which were sold by Mrs. Oakshott, of Brixton
006959 Road, to a salesman named Breckinridge, by him in turn to Mr.
006960 Windigate, of the Alpha, and by him to his club, of which Mr.
006961 Henry Baker is a member."
006962 
006963 "Oh, sir, you are the very man whom I have longed to meet," cried
006964 the little fellow with outstretched hands and quivering fingers.
006965 "I can hardly explain to you how interested I am in this matter."
006966 
006967 Sherlock Holmes hailed a four-wheeler which was passing. "In that
006968 case we had better discuss it in a cosy room rather than in this
006969 wind-swept market-place," said he. "But pray tell me, before we
006970 go farther, who it is that I have the pleasure of assisting."
006971 
006972 The man hesitated for an instant. "My name is John Robinson," he
006973 answered with a sidelong glance.
006974 
006975 "No, no; the real name," said Holmes sweetly. "It is always
006976 awkward doing business with an alias."
006977 
006978 A flush sprang to the white cheeks of the stranger. "Well then,"
006979 said he, "my real name is James Ryder."
006980 
006981 "Precisely so. Head attendant at the Hotel Cosmopolitan. Pray
006982 step into the cab, and I shall soon be able to tell you
006983 everything which you would wish to know."
006984 
006985 The little man stood glancing from one to the other of us with
006986 half-frightened, half-hopeful eyes, as one who is not sure
006987 whether he is on the verge of a windfall or of a catastrophe.
006988 Then he stepped into the cab, and in half an hour we were back in
006989 the sitting-room at Baker Street. Nothing had been said during
006990 our drive, but the high, thin breathing of our new companion, and
006991 the claspings and unclaspings of his hands, spoke of the nervous
006992 tension within him.
006993 
006994 "Here we are!" said Holmes cheerily as we filed into the room.
006995 "The fire looks very seasonable in this weather. You look cold,
006996 Mr. Ryder. Pray take the basket-chair. I will just put on my
006997 slippers before we settle this little matter of yours. Now, then!
006998 You want to know what became of those geese?"
006999 
007000 "Yes, sir."
007001 
007002 "Or rather, I fancy, of that goose. It was one bird, I imagine in
007003 which you were interested--white, with a black bar across the
007004 tail."
007005 
007006 Ryder quivered with emotion. "Oh, sir," he cried, "can you tell
007007 me where it went to?"
007008 
007009 "It came here."
007010 
007011 "Here?"
007012 
007013 "Yes, and a most remarkable bird it proved. I don't wonder that
007014 you should take an interest in it. It laid an egg after it was
007015 dead--the bonniest, brightest little blue egg that ever was seen.
007016 I have it here in my museum."
007017 
007018 Our visitor staggered to his feet and clutched the mantelpiece
007019 with his right hand. Holmes unlocked his strong-box and held up
007020 the blue carbuncle, which shone out like a star, with a cold,
007021 brilliant, many-pointed radiance. Ryder stood glaring with a
007022 drawn face, uncertain whether to claim or to disown it.
007023 
007024 "The game's up, Ryder," said Holmes quietly. "Hold up, man, or
007025 you'll be into the fire! Give him an arm back into his chair,
007026 Watson. He's not got blood enough to go in for felony with
007027 impunity. Give him a dash of brandy. So! Now he looks a little
007028 more human. What a shrimp it is, to be sure!"
007029 
007030 For a moment he had staggered and nearly fallen, but the brandy
007031 brought a tinge of colour into his cheeks, and he sat staring
007032 with frightened eyes at his accuser.
007033 
007034 "I have almost every link in my hands, and all the proofs which I
007035 could possibly need, so there is little which you need tell me.
007036 Still, that little may as well be cleared up to make the case
007037 complete. You had heard, Ryder, of this blue stone of the
007038 Countess of Morcar's?"
007039 
007040 "It was Catherine Cusack who told me of it," said he in a
007041 crackling voice.
007042 
007043 "I see--her ladyship's waiting-maid. Well, the temptation of
007044 sudden wealth so easily acquired was too much for you, as it has
007045 been for better men before you; but you were not very scrupulous
007046 in the means you used. It seems to me, Ryder, that there is the
007047 making of a very pretty villain in you. You knew that this man
007048 Horner, the plumber, had been concerned in some such matter
007049 before, and that suspicion would rest the more readily upon him.
007050 What did you do, then? You made some small job in my lady's
007051 room--you and your confederate Cusack--and you managed that he
007052 should be the man sent for. Then, when he had left, you rifled
007053 the jewel-case, raised the alarm, and had this unfortunate man
007054 arrested. You then--"
007055 
007056 Ryder threw himself down suddenly upon the rug and clutched at my
007057 companion's knees. "For God's sake, have mercy!" he shrieked.
007058 "Think of my father! Of my mother! It would break their hearts. I
007059 never went wrong before! I never will again. I swear it. I'll
007060 swear it on a Bible. Oh, don't bring it into court! For Christ's
007061 sake, don't!"
007062 
007063 "Get back into your chair!" said Holmes sternly. "It is very well
007064 to cringe and crawl now, but you thought little enough of this
007065 poor Horner in the dock for a crime of which he knew nothing."
007066 
007067 "I will fly, Mr. Holmes. I will leave the country, sir. Then the
007068 charge against him will break down."
007069 
007070 "Hum! We will talk about that. And now let us hear a true account
007071 of the next act. How came the stone into the goose, and how came
007072 the goose into the open market? Tell us the truth, for there lies
007073 your only hope of safety."
007074 
007075 Ryder passed his tongue over his parched lips. "I will tell you
007076 it just as it happened, sir," said he. "When Horner had been
007077 arrested, it seemed to me that it would be best for me to get
007078 away with the stone at once, for I did not know at what moment
007079 the police might not take it into their heads to search me and my
007080 room. There was no place about the hotel where it would be safe.
007081 I went out, as if on some commission, and I made for my sister's
007082 house. She had married a man named Oakshott, and lived in Brixton
007083 Road, where she fattened fowls for the market. All the way there
007084 every man I met seemed to me to be a policeman or a detective;
007085 and, for all that it was a cold night, the sweat was pouring down
007086 my face before I came to the Brixton Road. My sister asked me
007087 what was the matter, and why I was so pale; but I told her that I
007088 had been upset by the jewel robbery at the hotel. Then I went
007089 into the back yard and smoked a pipe and wondered what it would
007090 be best to do.
007091 
007092 "I had a friend once called Maudsley, who went to the bad, and
007093 has just been serving his time in Pentonville. One day he had met
007094 me, and fell into talk about the ways of thieves, and how they
007095 could get rid of what they stole. I knew that he would be true to
007096 me, for I knew one or two things about him; so I made up my mind
007097 to go right on to Kilburn, where he lived, and take him into my
007098 confidence. He would show me how to turn the stone into money.
007099 But how to get to him in safety? I thought of the agonies I had
007100 gone through in coming from the hotel. I might at any moment be
007101 seized and searched, and there would be the stone in my waistcoat
007102 pocket. I was leaning against the wall at the time and looking at
007103 the geese which were waddling about round my feet, and suddenly
007104 an idea came into my head which showed me how I could beat the
007105 best detective that ever lived.
007106 
007107 "My sister had told me some weeks before that I might have the
007108 pick of her geese for a Christmas present, and I knew that she
007109 was always as good as her word. I would take my goose now, and in
007110 it I would carry my stone to Kilburn. There was a little shed in
007111 the yard, and behind this I drove one of the birds--a fine big
007112 one, white, with a barred tail. I caught it, and prying its bill
007113 open, I thrust the stone down its throat as far as my finger
007114 could reach. The bird gave a gulp, and I felt the stone pass
007115 along its gullet and down into its crop. But the creature flapped
007116 and struggled, and out came my sister to know what was the
007117 matter. As I turned to speak to her the brute broke loose and
007118 fluttered off among the others.
007119 
007120 "'Whatever were you doing with that bird, Jem?' says she.
007121 
007122 "'Well,' said I, 'you said you'd give me one for Christmas, and I
007123 was feeling which was the fattest.'
007124 
007125 "'Oh,' says she, 'we've set yours aside for you--Jem's bird, we
007126 call it. It's the big white one over yonder. There's twenty-six
007127 of them, which makes one for you, and one for us, and two dozen
007128 for the market.'
007129 
007130 "'Thank you, Maggie,' says I; 'but if it is all the same to you,
007131 I'd rather have that one I was handling just now.'
007132 
007133 "'The other is a good three pound heavier,' said she, 'and we
007134 fattened it expressly for you.'
007135 
007136 "'Never mind. I'll have the other, and I'll take it now,' said I.
007137 
007138 "'Oh, just as you like,' said she, a little huffed. 'Which is it
007139 you want, then?'
007140 
007141 "'That white one with the barred tail, right in the middle of the
007142 flock.'
007143 
007144 "'Oh, very well. Kill it and take it with you.'
007145 
007146 "Well, I did what she said, Mr. Holmes, and I carried the bird
007147 all the way to Kilburn. I told my pal what I had done, for he was
007148 a man that it was easy to tell a thing like that to. He laughed
007149 until he choked, and we got a knife and opened the goose. My
007150 heart turned to water, for there was no sign of the stone, and I
007151 knew that some terrible mistake had occurred. I left the bird,
007152 rushed back to my sister's, and hurried into the back yard. There
007153 was not a bird to be seen there.
007154 
007155 "'Where are they all, Maggie?' I cried.
007156 
007157 "'Gone to the dealer's, Jem.'
007158 
007159 "'Which dealer's?'
007160 
007161 "'Breckinridge, of Covent Garden.'
007162 
007163 "'But was there another with a barred tail?' I asked, 'the same
007164 as the one I chose?'
007165 
007166 "'Yes, Jem; there were two barred-tailed ones, and I could never
007167 tell them apart.'
007168 
007169 "Well, then, of course I saw it all, and I ran off as hard as my
007170 feet would carry me to this man Breckinridge; but he had sold the
007171 lot at once, and not one word would he tell me as to where they
007172 had gone. You heard him yourselves to-night. Well, he has always
007173 answered me like that. My sister thinks that I am going mad.
007174 Sometimes I think that I am myself. And now--and now I am myself
007175 a branded thief, without ever having touched the wealth for which
007176 I sold my character. God help me! God help me!" He burst into
007177 convulsive sobbing, with his face buried in his hands.
007178 
007179 There was a long silence, broken only by his heavy breathing and
007180 by the measured tapping of Sherlock Holmes' finger-tips upon the
007181 edge of the table. Then my friend rose and threw open the door.
007182 
007183 "Get out!" said he.
007184 
007185 "What, sir! Oh, Heaven bless you!"
007186 
007187 "No more words. Get out!"
007188 
007189 And no more words were needed. There was a rush, a clatter upon
007190 the stairs, the bang of a door, and the crisp rattle of running
007191 footfalls from the street.
007192 
007193 "After all, Watson," said Holmes, reaching up his hand for his
007194 clay pipe, "I am not retained by the police to supply their
007195 deficiencies. If Horner were in danger it would be another thing;
007196 but this fellow will not appear against him, and the case must
007197 collapse. I suppose that I am commuting a felony, but it is just
007198 possible that I am saving a soul. This fellow will not go wrong
007199 again; he is too terribly frightened. Send him to gaol now, and
007200 you make him a gaol-bird for life. Besides, it is the season of
007201 forgiveness. Chance has put in our way a most singular and
007202 whimsical problem, and its solution is its own reward. If you
007203 will have the goodness to touch the bell, Doctor, we will begin
007204 another investigation, in which, also a bird will be the chief
007205 feature."
007206 
007207 
007208 
007209 VIII. THE ADVENTURE OF THE SPECKLED BAND
007210 
007211 On glancing over my notes of the seventy odd cases in which I
007212 have during the last eight years studied the methods of my friend
007213 Sherlock Holmes, I find many tragic, some comic, a large number
007214 merely strange, but none commonplace; for, working as he did
007215 rather for the love of his art than for the acquirement of
007216 wealth, he refused to associate himself with any investigation
007217 which did not tend towards the unusual, and even the fantastic.
007218 Of all these varied cases, however, I cannot recall any which
007219 presented more singular features than that which was associated
007220 with the well-known Surrey family of the Roylotts of Stoke Moran.
007221 The events in question occurred in the early days of my
007222 association with Holmes, when we were sharing rooms as bachelors
007223 in Baker Street. It is possible that I might have placed them
007224 upon record before, but a promise of secrecy was made at the
007225 time, from which I have only been freed during the last month by
007226 the untimely death of the lady to whom the pledge was given. It
007227 is perhaps as well that the facts should now come to light, for I
007228 have reasons to know that there are widespread rumours as to the
007229 death of Dr. Grimesby Roylott which tend to make the matter even
007230 more terrible than the truth.
007231 
007232 It was early in April in the year '83 that I woke one morning to
007233 find Sherlock Holmes standing, fully dressed, by the side of my
007234 bed. He was a late riser, as a rule, and as the clock on the
007235 mantelpiece showed me that it was only a quarter-past seven, I
007236 blinked up at him in some surprise, and perhaps just a little
007237 resentment, for I was myself regular in my habits.
007238 
007239 "Very sorry to knock you up, Watson," said he, "but it's the
007240 common lot this morning. Mrs. Hudson has been knocked up, she
007241 retorted upon me, and I on you."
007242 
007243 "What is it, then--a fire?"
007244 
007245 "No; a client. It seems that a young lady has arrived in a
007246 considerable state of excitement, who insists upon seeing me. She
007247 is waiting now in the sitting-room. Now, when young ladies wander
007248 about the metropolis at this hour of the morning, and knock
007249 sleepy people up out of their beds, I presume that it is
007250 something very pressing which they have to communicate. Should it
007251 prove to be an interesting case, you would, I am sure, wish to
007252 follow it from the outset. I thought, at any rate, that I should
007253 call you and give you the chance."
007254 
007255 "My dear fellow, I would not miss it for anything."
007256 
007257 I had no keener pleasure than in following Holmes in his
007258 professional investigations, and in admiring the rapid
007259 deductions, as swift as intuitions, and yet always founded on a
007260 logical basis with which he unravelled the problems which were
007261 submitted to him. I rapidly threw on my clothes and was ready in
007262 a few minutes to accompany my friend down to the sitting-room. A
007263 lady dressed in black and heavily veiled, who had been sitting in
007264 the window, rose as we entered.
007265 
007266 "Good-morning, madam," said Holmes cheerily. "My name is Sherlock
007267 Holmes. This is my intimate friend and associate, Dr. Watson,
007268 before whom you can speak as freely as before myself. Ha! I am
007269 glad to see that Mrs. Hudson has had the good sense to light the
007270 fire. Pray draw up to it, and I shall order you a cup of hot
007271 coffee, for I observe that you are shivering."
007272 
007273 "It is not cold which makes me shiver," said the woman in a low
007274 voice, changing her seat as requested.
007275 
007276 "What, then?"
007277 
007278 "It is fear, Mr. Holmes. It is terror." She raised her veil as
007279 she spoke, and we could see that she was indeed in a pitiable
007280 state of agitation, her face all drawn and grey, with restless
007281 frightened eyes, like those of some hunted animal. Her features
007282 and figure were those of a woman of thirty, but her hair was shot
007283 with premature grey, and her expression was weary and haggard.
007284 Sherlock Holmes ran her over with one of his quick,
007285 all-comprehensive glances.
007286 
007287 "You must not fear," said he soothingly, bending forward and
007288 patting her forearm. "We shall soon set matters right, I have no
007289 doubt. You have come in by train this morning, I see."
007290 
007291 "You know me, then?"
007292 
007293 "No, but I observe the second half of a return ticket in the palm
007294 of your left glove. You must have started early, and yet you had
007295 a good drive in a dog-cart, along heavy roads, before you reached
007296 the station."
007297 
007298 The lady gave a violent start and stared in bewilderment at my
007299 companion.
007300 
007301 "There is no mystery, my dear madam," said he, smiling. "The left
007302 arm of your jacket is spattered with mud in no less than seven
007303 places. The marks are perfectly fresh. There is no vehicle save a
007304 dog-cart which throws up mud in that way, and then only when you
007305 sit on the left-hand side of the driver."
007306 
007307 "Whatever your reasons may be, you are perfectly correct," said
007308 she. "I started from home before six, reached Leatherhead at
007309 twenty past, and came in by the first train to Waterloo. Sir, I
007310 can stand this strain no longer; I shall go mad if it continues.
007311 I have no one to turn to--none, save only one, who cares for me,
007312 and he, poor fellow, can be of little aid. I have heard of you,
007313 Mr. Holmes; I have heard of you from Mrs. Farintosh, whom you
007314 helped in the hour of her sore need. It was from her that I had
007315 your address. Oh, sir, do you not think that you could help me,
007316 too, and at least throw a little light through the dense darkness
007317 which surrounds me? At present it is out of my power to reward
007318 you for your services, but in a month or six weeks I shall be
007319 married, with the control of my own income, and then at least you
007320 shall not find me ungrateful."
007321 
007322 Holmes turned to his desk and, unlocking it, drew out a small
007323 case-book, which he consulted.
007324 
007325 "Farintosh," said he. "Ah yes, I recall the case; it was
007326 concerned with an opal tiara. I think it was before your time,
007327 Watson. I can only say, madam, that I shall be happy to devote
007328 the same care to your case as I did to that of your friend. As to
007329 reward, my profession is its own reward; but you are at liberty
007330 to defray whatever expenses I may be put to, at the time which
007331 suits you best. And now I beg that you will lay before us
007332 everything that may help us in forming an opinion upon the
007333 matter."
007334 
007335 "Alas!" replied our visitor, "the very horror of my situation
007336 lies in the fact that my fears are so vague, and my suspicions
007337 depend so entirely upon small points, which might seem trivial to
007338 another, that even he to whom of all others I have a right to
007339 look for help and advice looks upon all that I tell him about it
007340 as the fancies of a nervous woman. He does not say so, but I can
007341 read it from his soothing answers and averted eyes. But I have
007342 heard, Mr. Holmes, that you can see deeply into the manifold
007343 wickedness of the human heart. You may advise me how to walk amid
007344 the dangers which encompass me."
007345 
007346 "I am all attention, madam."
007347 
007348 "My name is Helen Stoner, and I am living with my stepfather, who
007349 is the last survivor of one of the oldest Saxon families in
007350 England, the Roylotts of Stoke Moran, on the western border of
007351 Surrey."
007352 
007353 Holmes nodded his head. "The name is familiar to me," said he.
007354 
007355 "The family was at one time among the richest in England, and the
007356 estates extended over the borders into Berkshire in the north,
007357 and Hampshire in the west. In the last century, however, four
007358 successive heirs were of a dissolute and wasteful disposition,
007359 and the family ruin was eventually completed by a gambler in the
007360 days of the Regency. Nothing was left save a few acres of ground,
007361 and the two-hundred-year-old house, which is itself crushed under
007362 a heavy mortgage. The last squire dragged out his existence
007363 there, living the horrible life of an aristocratic pauper; but
007364 his only son, my stepfather, seeing that he must adapt himself to
007365 the new conditions, obtained an advance from a relative, which
007366 enabled him to take a medical degree and went out to Calcutta,
007367 where, by his professional skill and his force of character, he
007368 established a large practice. In a fit of anger, however, caused
007369 by some robberies which had been perpetrated in the house, he
007370 beat his native butler to death and narrowly escaped a capital
007371 sentence. As it was, he suffered a long term of imprisonment and
007372 afterwards returned to England a morose and disappointed man.
007373 
007374 "When Dr. Roylott was in India he married my mother, Mrs. Stoner,
007375 the young widow of Major-General Stoner, of the Bengal Artillery.
007376 My sister Julia and I were twins, and we were only two years old
007377 at the time of my mother's re-marriage. She had a considerable
007378 sum of money--not less than 1000 pounds a year--and this she
007379 bequeathed to Dr. Roylott entirely while we resided with him,
007380 with a provision that a certain annual sum should be allowed to
007381 each of us in the event of our marriage. Shortly after our return
007382 to England my mother died--she was killed eight years ago in a
007383 railway accident near Crewe. Dr. Roylott then abandoned his
007384 attempts to establish himself in practice in London and took us
007385 to live with him in the old ancestral house at Stoke Moran. The
007386 money which my mother had left was enough for all our wants, and
007387 there seemed to be no obstacle to our happiness.
007388 
007389 "But a terrible change came over our stepfather about this time.
007390 Instead of making friends and exchanging visits with our
007391 neighbours, who had at first been overjoyed to see a Roylott of
007392 Stoke Moran back in the old family seat, he shut himself up in
007393 his house and seldom came out save to indulge in ferocious
007394 quarrels with whoever might cross his path. Violence of temper
007395 approaching to mania has been hereditary in the men of the
007396 family, and in my stepfather's case it had, I believe, been
007397 intensified by his long residence in the tropics. A series of
007398 disgraceful brawls took place, two of which ended in the
007399 police-court, until at last he became the terror of the village,
007400 and the folks would fly at his approach, for he is a man of
007401 immense strength, and absolutely uncontrollable in his anger.
007402 
007403 "Last week he hurled the local blacksmith over a parapet into a
007404 stream, and it was only by paying over all the money which I
007405 could gather together that I was able to avert another public
007406 exposure. He had no friends at all save the wandering gipsies,
007407 and he would give these vagabonds leave to encamp upon the few
007408 acres of bramble-covered land which represent the family estate,
007409 and would accept in return the hospitality of their tents,
007410 wandering away with them sometimes for weeks on end. He has a
007411 passion also for Indian animals, which are sent over to him by a
007412 correspondent, and he has at this moment a cheetah and a baboon,
007413 which wander freely over his grounds and are feared by the
007414 villagers almost as much as their master.
007415 
007416 "You can imagine from what I say that my poor sister Julia and I
007417 had no great pleasure in our lives. No servant would stay with
007418 us, and for a long time we did all the work of the house. She was
007419 but thirty at the time of her death, and yet her hair had already
007420 begun to whiten, even as mine has."
007421 
007422 "Your sister is dead, then?"
007423 
007424 "She died just two years ago, and it is of her death that I wish
007425 to speak to you. You can understand that, living the life which I
007426 have described, we were little likely to see anyone of our own
007427 age and position. We had, however, an aunt, my mother's maiden
007428 sister, Miss Honoria Westphail, who lives near Harrow, and we
007429 were occasionally allowed to pay short visits at this lady's
007430 house. Julia went there at Christmas two years ago, and met there
007431 a half-pay major of marines, to whom she became engaged. My
007432 stepfather learned of the engagement when my sister returned and
007433 offered no objection to the marriage; but within a fortnight of
007434 the day which had been fixed for the wedding, the terrible event
007435 occurred which has deprived me of my only companion."
007436 
007437 Sherlock Holmes had been leaning back in his chair with his eyes
007438 closed and his head sunk in a cushion, but he half opened his
007439 lids now and glanced across at his visitor.
007440 
007441 "Pray be precise as to details," said he.
007442 
007443 "It is easy for me to be so, for every event of that dreadful
007444 time is seared into my memory. The manor-house is, as I have
007445 already said, very old, and only one wing is now inhabited. The
007446 bedrooms in this wing are on the ground floor, the sitting-rooms
007447 being in the central block of the buildings. Of these bedrooms
007448 the first is Dr. Roylott's, the second my sister's, and the third
007449 my own. There is no communication between them, but they all open
007450 out into the same corridor. Do I make myself plain?"
007451 
007452 "Perfectly so."
007453 
007454 "The windows of the three rooms open out upon the lawn. That
007455 fatal night Dr. Roylott had gone to his room early, though we
007456 knew that he had not retired to rest, for my sister was troubled
007457 by the smell of the strong Indian cigars which it was his custom
007458 to smoke. She left her room, therefore, and came into mine, where
007459 she sat for some time, chatting about her approaching wedding. At
007460 eleven o'clock she rose to leave me, but she paused at the door
007461 and looked back.
007462 
007463 "'Tell me, Helen,' said she, 'have you ever heard anyone whistle
007464 in the dead of the night?'
007465 
007466 "'Never,' said I.
007467 
007468 "'I suppose that you could not possibly whistle, yourself, in
007469 your sleep?'
007470 
007471 "'Certainly not. But why?'
007472 
007473 "'Because during the last few nights I have always, about three
007474 in the morning, heard a low, clear whistle. I am a light sleeper,
007475 and it has awakened me. I cannot tell where it came from--perhaps
007476 from the next room, perhaps from the lawn. I thought that I would
007477 just ask you whether you had heard it.'
007478 
007479 "'No, I have not. It must be those wretched gipsies in the
007480 plantation.'
007481 
007482 "'Very likely. And yet if it were on the lawn, I wonder that you
007483 did not hear it also.'
007484 
007485 "'Ah, but I sleep more heavily than you.'
007486 
007487 "'Well, it is of no great consequence, at any rate.' She smiled
007488 back at me, closed my door, and a few moments later I heard her
007489 key turn in the lock."
007490 
007491 "Indeed," said Holmes. "Was it your custom always to lock
007492 yourselves in at night?"
007493 
007494 "Always."
007495 
007496 "And why?"
007497 
007498 "I think that I mentioned to you that the doctor kept a cheetah
007499 and a baboon. We had no feeling of security unless our doors were
007500 locked."
007501 
007502 "Quite so. Pray proceed with your statement."
007503 
007504 "I could not sleep that night. A vague feeling of impending
007505 misfortune impressed me. My sister and I, you will recollect,
007506 were twins, and you know how subtle are the links which bind two
007507 souls which are so closely allied. It was a wild night. The wind
007508 was howling outside, and the rain was beating and splashing
007509 against the windows. Suddenly, amid all the hubbub of the gale,
007510 there burst forth the wild scream of a terrified woman. I knew
007511 that it was my sister's voice. I sprang from my bed, wrapped a
007512 shawl round me, and rushed into the corridor. As I opened my door
007513 I seemed to hear a low whistle, such as my sister described, and
007514 a few moments later a clanging sound, as if a mass of metal had
007515 fallen. As I ran down the passage, my sister's door was unlocked,
007516 and revolved slowly upon its hinges. I stared at it
007517 horror-stricken, not knowing what was about to issue from it. By
007518 the light of the corridor-lamp I saw my sister appear at the
007519 opening, her face blanched with terror, her hands groping for
007520 help, her whole figure swaying to and fro like that of a
007521 drunkard. I ran to her and threw my arms round her, but at that
007522 moment her knees seemed to give way and she fell to the ground.
007523 She writhed as one who is in terrible pain, and her limbs were
007524 dreadfully convulsed. At first I thought that she had not
007525 recognised me, but as I bent over her she suddenly shrieked out
007526 in a voice which I shall never forget, 'Oh, my God! Helen! It was
007527 the band! The speckled band!' There was something else which she
007528 would fain have said, and she stabbed with her finger into the
007529 air in the direction of the doctor's room, but a fresh convulsion
007530 seized her and choked her words. I rushed out, calling loudly for
007531 my stepfather, and I met him hastening from his room in his
007532 dressing-gown. When he reached my sister's side she was
007533 unconscious, and though he poured brandy down her throat and sent
007534 for medical aid from the village, all efforts were in vain, for
007535 she slowly sank and died without having recovered her
007536 consciousness. Such was the dreadful end of my beloved sister."
007537 
007538 "One moment," said Holmes, "are you sure about this whistle and
007539 metallic sound? Could you swear to it?"
007540 
007541 "That was what the county coroner asked me at the inquiry. It is
007542 my strong impression that I heard it, and yet, among the crash of
007543 the gale and the creaking of an old house, I may possibly have
007544 been deceived."
007545 
007546 "Was your sister dressed?"
007547 
007548 "No, she was in her night-dress. In her right hand was found the
007549 charred stump of a match, and in her left a match-box."
007550 
007551 "Showing that she had struck a light and looked about her when
007552 the alarm took place. That is important. And what conclusions did
007553 the coroner come to?"
007554 
007555 "He investigated the case with great care, for Dr. Roylott's
007556 conduct had long been notorious in the county, but he was unable
007557 to find any satisfactory cause of death. My evidence showed that
007558 the door had been fastened upon the inner side, and the windows
007559 were blocked by old-fashioned shutters with broad iron bars,
007560 which were secured every night. The walls were carefully sounded,
007561 and were shown to be quite solid all round, and the flooring was
007562 also thoroughly examined, with the same result. The chimney is
007563 wide, but is barred up by four large staples. It is certain,
007564 therefore, that my sister was quite alone when she met her end.
007565 Besides, there were no marks of any violence upon her."
007566 
007567 "How about poison?"
007568 
007569 "The doctors examined her for it, but without success."
007570 
007571 "What do you think that this unfortunate lady died of, then?"
007572 
007573 "It is my belief that she died of pure fear and nervous shock,
007574 though what it was that frightened her I cannot imagine."
007575 
007576 "Were there gipsies in the plantation at the time?"
007577 
007578 "Yes, there are nearly always some there."
007579 
007580 "Ah, and what did you gather from this allusion to a band--a
007581 speckled band?"
007582 
007583 "Sometimes I have thought that it was merely the wild talk of
007584 delirium, sometimes that it may have referred to some band of
007585 people, perhaps to these very gipsies in the plantation. I do not
007586 know whether the spotted handkerchiefs which so many of them wear
007587 over their heads might have suggested the strange adjective which
007588 she used."
007589 
007590 Holmes shook his head like a man who is far from being satisfied.
007591 
007592 "These are very deep waters," said he; "pray go on with your
007593 narrative."
007594 
007595 "Two years have passed since then, and my life has been until
007596 lately lonelier than ever. A month ago, however, a dear friend,
007597 whom I have known for many years, has done me the honour to ask
007598 my hand in marriage. His name is Armitage--Percy Armitage--the
007599 second son of Mr. Armitage, of Crane Water, near Reading. My
007600 stepfather has offered no opposition to the match, and we are to
007601 be married in the course of the spring. Two days ago some repairs
007602 were started in the west wing of the building, and my bedroom
007603 wall has been pierced, so that I have had to move into the
007604 chamber in which my sister died, and to sleep in the very bed in
007605 which she slept. Imagine, then, my thrill of terror when last
007606 night, as I lay awake, thinking over her terrible fate, I
007607 suddenly heard in the silence of the night the low whistle which
007608 had been the herald of her own death. I sprang up and lit the
007609 lamp, but nothing was to be seen in the room. I was too shaken to
007610 go to bed again, however, so I dressed, and as soon as it was
007611 daylight I slipped down, got a dog-cart at the Crown Inn, which
007612 is opposite, and drove to Leatherhead, from whence I have come on
007613 this morning with the one object of seeing you and asking your
007614 advice."
007615 
007616 "You have done wisely," said my friend. "But have you told me
007617 all?"
007618 
007619 "Yes, all."
007620 
007621 "Miss Roylott, you have not. You are screening your stepfather."
007622 
007623 "Why, what do you mean?"
007624 
007625 For answer Holmes pushed back the frill of black lace which
007626 fringed the hand that lay upon our visitor's knee. Five little
007627 livid spots, the marks of four fingers and a thumb, were printed
007628 upon the white wrist.
007629 
007630 "You have been cruelly used," said Holmes.
007631 
007632 The lady coloured deeply and covered over her injured wrist. "He
007633 is a hard man," she said, "and perhaps he hardly knows his own
007634 strength."
007635 
007636 There was a long silence, during which Holmes leaned his chin
007637 upon his hands and stared into the crackling fire.
007638 
007639 "This is a very deep business," he said at last. "There are a
007640 thousand details which I should desire to know before I decide
007641 upon our course of action. Yet we have not a moment to lose. If
007642 we were to come to Stoke Moran to-day, would it be possible for
007643 us to see over these rooms without the knowledge of your
007644 stepfather?"
007645 
007646 "As it happens, he spoke of coming into town to-day upon some
007647 most important business. It is probable that he will be away all
007648 day, and that there would be nothing to disturb you. We have a
007649 housekeeper now, but she is old and foolish, and I could easily
007650 get her out of the way."
007651 
007652 "Excellent. You are not averse to this trip, Watson?"
007653 
007654 "By no means."
007655 
007656 "Then we shall both come. What are you going to do yourself?"
007657 
007658 "I have one or two things which I would wish to do now that I am
007659 in town. But I shall return by the twelve o'clock train, so as to
007660 be there in time for your coming."
007661 
007662 "And you may expect us early in the afternoon. I have myself some
007663 small business matters to attend to. Will you not wait and
007664 breakfast?"
007665 
007666 "No, I must go. My heart is lightened already since I have
007667 confided my trouble to you. I shall look forward to seeing you
007668 again this afternoon." She dropped her thick black veil over her
007669 face and glided from the room.
007670 
007671 "And what do you think of it all, Watson?" asked Sherlock Holmes,
007672 leaning back in his chair.
007673 
007674 "It seems to me to be a most dark and sinister business."
007675 
007676 "Dark enough and sinister enough."
007677 
007678 "Yet if the lady is correct in saying that the flooring and walls
007679 are sound, and that the door, window, and chimney are impassable,
007680 then her sister must have been undoubtedly alone when she met her
007681 mysterious end."
007682 
007683 "What becomes, then, of these nocturnal whistles, and what of the
007684 very peculiar words of the dying woman?"
007685 
007686 "I cannot think."
007687 
007688 "When you combine the ideas of whistles at night, the presence of
007689 a band of gipsies who are on intimate terms with this old doctor,
007690 the fact that we have every reason to believe that the doctor has
007691 an interest in preventing his stepdaughter's marriage, the dying
007692 allusion to a band, and, finally, the fact that Miss Helen Stoner
007693 heard a metallic clang, which might have been caused by one of
007694 those metal bars that secured the shutters falling back into its
007695 place, I think that there is good ground to think that the
007696 mystery may be cleared along those lines."
007697 
007698 "But what, then, did the gipsies do?"
007699 
007700 "I cannot imagine."
007701 
007702 "I see many objections to any such theory."
007703 
007704 "And so do I. It is precisely for that reason that we are going
007705 to Stoke Moran this day. I want to see whether the objections are
007706 fatal, or if they may be explained away. But what in the name of
007707 the devil!"
007708 
007709 The ejaculation had been drawn from my companion by the fact that
007710 our door had been suddenly dashed open, and that a huge man had
007711 framed himself in the aperture. His costume was a peculiar
007712 mixture of the professional and of the agricultural, having a
007713 black top-hat, a long frock-coat, and a pair of high gaiters,
007714 with a hunting-crop swinging in his hand. So tall was he that his
007715 hat actually brushed the cross bar of the doorway, and his
007716 breadth seemed to span it across from side to side. A large face,
007717 seared with a thousand wrinkles, burned yellow with the sun, and
007718 marked with every evil passion, was turned from one to the other
007719 of us, while his deep-set, bile-shot eyes, and his high, thin,
007720 fleshless nose, gave him somewhat the resemblance to a fierce old
007721 bird of prey.
007722 
007723 "Which of you is Holmes?" asked this apparition.
007724 
007725 "My name, sir; but you have the advantage of me," said my
007726 companion quietly.
007727 
007728 "I am Dr. Grimesby Roylott, of Stoke Moran."
007729 
007730 "Indeed, Doctor," said Holmes blandly. "Pray take a seat."
007731 
007732 "I will do nothing of the kind. My stepdaughter has been here. I
007733 have traced her. What has she been saying to you?"
007734 
007735 "It is a little cold for the time of the year," said Holmes.
007736 
007737 "What has she been saying to you?" screamed the old man
007738 furiously.
007739 
007740 "But I have heard that the crocuses promise well," continued my
007741 companion imperturbably.
007742 
007743 "Ha! You put me off, do you?" said our new visitor, taking a step
007744 forward and shaking his hunting-crop. "I know you, you scoundrel!
007745 I have heard of you before. You are Holmes, the meddler."
007746 
007747 My friend smiled.
007748 
007749 "Holmes, the busybody!"
007750 
007751 His smile broadened.
007752 
007753 "Holmes, the Scotland Yard Jack-in-office!"
007754 
007755 Holmes chuckled heartily. "Your conversation is most
007756 entertaining," said he. "When you go out close the door, for
007757 there is a decided draught."
007758 
007759 "I will go when I have said my say. Don't you dare to meddle with
007760 my affairs. I know that Miss Stoner has been here. I traced her!
007761 I am a dangerous man to fall foul of! See here." He stepped
007762 swiftly forward, seized the poker, and bent it into a curve with
007763 his huge brown hands.
007764 
007765 "See that you keep yourself out of my grip," he snarled, and
007766 hurling the twisted poker into the fireplace he strode out of the
007767 room.
007768 
007769 "He seems a very amiable person," said Holmes, laughing. "I am
007770 not quite so bulky, but if he had remained I might have shown him
007771 that my grip was not much more feeble than his own." As he spoke
007772 he picked up the steel poker and, with a sudden effort,
007773 straightened it out again.
007774 
007775 "Fancy his having the insolence to confound me with the official
007776 detective force! This incident gives zest to our investigation,
007777 however, and I only trust that our little friend will not suffer
007778 from her imprudence in allowing this brute to trace her. And now,
007779 Watson, we shall order breakfast, and afterwards I shall walk
007780 down to Doctors' Commons, where I hope to get some data which may
007781 help us in this matter."
007782 
007783 
007784 It was nearly one o'clock when Sherlock Holmes returned from his
007785 excursion. He held in his hand a sheet of blue paper, scrawled
007786 over with notes and figures.
007787 
007788 "I have seen the will of the deceased wife," said he. "To
007789 determine its exact meaning I have been obliged to work out the
007790 present prices of the investments with which it is concerned. The
007791 total income, which at the time of the wife's death was little
007792 short of 1100 pounds, is now, through the fall in agricultural
007793 prices, not more than 750 pounds. Each daughter can claim an
007794 income of 250 pounds, in case of marriage. It is evident,
007795 therefore, that if both girls had married, this beauty would have
007796 had a mere pittance, while even one of them would cripple him to
007797 a very serious extent. My morning's work has not been wasted,
007798 since it has proved that he has the very strongest motives for
007799 standing in the way of anything of the sort. And now, Watson,
007800 this is too serious for dawdling, especially as the old man is
007801 aware that we are interesting ourselves in his affairs; so if you
007802 are ready, we shall call a cab and drive to Waterloo. I should be
007803 very much obliged if you would slip your revolver into your
007804 pocket. An Eley's No. 2 is an excellent argument with gentlemen
007805 who can twist steel pokers into knots. That and a tooth-brush
007806 are, I think, all that we need."
007807 
007808 At Waterloo we were fortunate in catching a train for
007809 Leatherhead, where we hired a trap at the station inn and drove
007810 for four or five miles through the lovely Surrey lanes. It was a
007811 perfect day, with a bright sun and a few fleecy clouds in the
007812 heavens. The trees and wayside hedges were just throwing out
007813 their first green shoots, and the air was full of the pleasant
007814 smell of the moist earth. To me at least there was a strange
007815 contrast between the sweet promise of the spring and this
007816 sinister quest upon which we were engaged. My companion sat in
007817 the front of the trap, his arms folded, his hat pulled down over
007818 his eyes, and his chin sunk upon his breast, buried in the
007819 deepest thought. Suddenly, however, he started, tapped me on the
007820 shoulder, and pointed over the meadows.
007821 
007822 "Look there!" said he.
007823 
007824 A heavily timbered park stretched up in a gentle slope,
007825 thickening into a grove at the highest point. From amid the
007826 branches there jutted out the grey gables and high roof-tree of a
007827 very old mansion.
007828 
007829 "Stoke Moran?" said he.
007830 
007831 "Yes, sir, that be the house of Dr. Grimesby Roylott," remarked
007832 the driver.
007833 
007834 "There is some building going on there," said Holmes; "that is
007835 where we are going."
007836 
007837 "There's the village," said the driver, pointing to a cluster of
007838 roofs some distance to the left; "but if you want to get to the
007839 house, you'll find it shorter to get over this stile, and so by
007840 the foot-path over the fields. There it is, where the lady is
007841 walking."
007842 
007843 "And the lady, I fancy, is Miss Stoner," observed Holmes, shading
007844 his eyes. "Yes, I think we had better do as you suggest."
007845 
007846 We got off, paid our fare, and the trap rattled back on its way
007847 to Leatherhead.
007848 
007849 "I thought it as well," said Holmes as we climbed the stile,
007850 "that this fellow should think we had come here as architects, or
007851 on some definite business. It may stop his gossip.
007852 Good-afternoon, Miss Stoner. You see that we have been as good as
007853 our word."
007854 
007855 Our client of the morning had hurried forward to meet us with a
007856 face which spoke her joy. "I have been waiting so eagerly for
007857 you," she cried, shaking hands with us warmly. "All has turned
007858 out splendidly. Dr. Roylott has gone to town, and it is unlikely
007859 that he will be back before evening."
007860 
007861 "We have had the pleasure of making the doctor's acquaintance,"
007862 said Holmes, and in a few words he sketched out what had
007863 occurred. Miss Stoner turned white to the lips as she listened.
007864 
007865 "Good heavens!" she cried, "he has followed me, then."
007866 
007867 "So it appears."
007868 
007869 "He is so cunning that I never know when I am safe from him. What
007870 will he say when he returns?"
007871 
007872 "He must guard himself, for he may find that there is someone
007873 more cunning than himself upon his track. You must lock yourself
007874 up from him to-night. If he is violent, we shall take you away to
007875 your aunt's at Harrow. Now, we must make the best use of our
007876 time, so kindly take us at once to the rooms which we are to
007877 examine."
007878 
007879 The building was of grey, lichen-blotched stone, with a high
007880 central portion and two curving wings, like the claws of a crab,
007881 thrown out on each side. In one of these wings the windows were
007882 broken and blocked with wooden boards, while the roof was partly
007883 caved in, a picture of ruin. The central portion was in little
007884 better repair, but the right-hand block was comparatively modern,
007885 and the blinds in the windows, with the blue smoke curling up
007886 from the chimneys, showed that this was where the family resided.
007887 Some scaffolding had been erected against the end wall, and the
007888 stone-work had been broken into, but there were no signs of any
007889 workmen at the moment of our visit. Holmes walked slowly up and
007890 down the ill-trimmed lawn and examined with deep attention the
007891 outsides of the windows.
007892 
007893 "This, I take it, belongs to the room in which you used to sleep,
007894 the centre one to your sister's, and the one next to the main
007895 building to Dr. Roylott's chamber?"
007896 
007897 "Exactly so. But I am now sleeping in the middle one."
007898 
007899 "Pending the alterations, as I understand. By the way, there does
007900 not seem to be any very pressing need for repairs at that end
007901 wall."
007902 
007903 "There were none. I believe that it was an excuse to move me from
007904 my room."
007905 
007906 "Ah! that is suggestive. Now, on the other side of this narrow
007907 wing runs the corridor from which these three rooms open. There
007908 are windows in it, of course?"
007909 
007910 "Yes, but very small ones. Too narrow for anyone to pass
007911 through."
007912 
007913 "As you both locked your doors at night, your rooms were
007914 unapproachable from that side. Now, would you have the kindness
007915 to go into your room and bar your shutters?"
007916 
007917 Miss Stoner did so, and Holmes, after a careful examination
007918 through the open window, endeavoured in every way to force the
007919 shutter open, but without success. There was no slit through
007920 which a knife could be passed to raise the bar. Then with his
007921 lens he tested the hinges, but they were of solid iron, built
007922 firmly into the massive masonry. "Hum!" said he, scratching his
007923 chin in some perplexity, "my theory certainly presents some
007924 difficulties. No one could pass these shutters if they were
