007925 bolted. Well, we shall see if the inside throws any light upon
007926 the matter."
007927 
007928 A small side door led into the whitewashed corridor from which
007929 the three bedrooms opened. Holmes refused to examine the third
007930 chamber, so we passed at once to the second, that in which Miss
007931 Stoner was now sleeping, and in which her sister had met with her
007932 fate. It was a homely little room, with a low ceiling and a
007933 gaping fireplace, after the fashion of old country-houses. A
007934 brown chest of drawers stood in one corner, a narrow
007935 white-counterpaned bed in another, and a dressing-table on the
007936 left-hand side of the window. These articles, with two small
007937 wicker-work chairs, made up all the furniture in the room save
007938 for a square of Wilton carpet in the centre. The boards round and
007939 the panelling of the walls were of brown, worm-eaten oak, so old
007940 and discoloured that it may have dated from the original building
007941 of the house. Holmes drew one of the chairs into a corner and sat
007942 silent, while his eyes travelled round and round and up and down,
007943 taking in every detail of the apartment.
007944 
007945 "Where does that bell communicate with?" he asked at last
007946 pointing to a thick bell-rope which hung down beside the bed, the
007947 tassel actually lying upon the pillow.
007948 
007949 "It goes to the housekeeper's room."
007950 
007951 "It looks newer than the other things?"
007952 
007953 "Yes, it was only put there a couple of years ago."
007954 
007955 "Your sister asked for it, I suppose?"
007956 
007957 "No, I never heard of her using it. We used always to get what we
007958 wanted for ourselves."
007959 
007960 "Indeed, it seemed unnecessary to put so nice a bell-pull there.
007961 You will excuse me for a few minutes while I satisfy myself as to
007962 this floor." He threw himself down upon his face with his lens in
007963 his hand and crawled swiftly backward and forward, examining
007964 minutely the cracks between the boards. Then he did the same with
007965 the wood-work with which the chamber was panelled. Finally he
007966 walked over to the bed and spent some time in staring at it and
007967 in running his eye up and down the wall. Finally he took the
007968 bell-rope in his hand and gave it a brisk tug.
007969 
007970 "Why, it's a dummy," said he.
007971 
007972 "Won't it ring?"
007973 
007974 "No, it is not even attached to a wire. This is very interesting.
007975 You can see now that it is fastened to a hook just above where
007976 the little opening for the ventilator is."
007977 
007978 "How very absurd! I never noticed that before."
007979 
007980 "Very strange!" muttered Holmes, pulling at the rope. "There are
007981 one or two very singular points about this room. For example,
007982 what a fool a builder must be to open a ventilator into another
007983 room, when, with the same trouble, he might have communicated
007984 with the outside air!"
007985 
007986 "That is also quite modern," said the lady.
007987 
007988 "Done about the same time as the bell-rope?" remarked Holmes.
007989 
007990 "Yes, there were several little changes carried out about that
007991 time."
007992 
007993 "They seem to have been of a most interesting character--dummy
007994 bell-ropes, and ventilators which do not ventilate. With your
007995 permission, Miss Stoner, we shall now carry our researches into
007996 the inner apartment."
007997 
007998 Dr. Grimesby Roylott's chamber was larger than that of his
007999 step-daughter, but was as plainly furnished. A camp-bed, a small
008000 wooden shelf full of books, mostly of a technical character, an
008001 armchair beside the bed, a plain wooden chair against the wall, a
008002 round table, and a large iron safe were the principal things
008003 which met the eye. Holmes walked slowly round and examined each
008004 and all of them with the keenest interest.
008005 
008006 "What's in here?" he asked, tapping the safe.
008007 
008008 "My stepfather's business papers."
008009 
008010 "Oh! you have seen inside, then?"
008011 
008012 "Only once, some years ago. I remember that it was full of
008013 papers."
008014 
008015 "There isn't a cat in it, for example?"
008016 
008017 "No. What a strange idea!"
008018 
008019 "Well, look at this!" He took up a small saucer of milk which
008020 stood on the top of it.
008021 
008022 "No; we don't keep a cat. But there is a cheetah and a baboon."
008023 
008024 "Ah, yes, of course! Well, a cheetah is just a big cat, and yet a
008025 saucer of milk does not go very far in satisfying its wants, I
008026 daresay. There is one point which I should wish to determine." He
008027 squatted down in front of the wooden chair and examined the seat
008028 of it with the greatest attention.
008029 
008030 "Thank you. That is quite settled," said he, rising and putting
008031 his lens in his pocket. "Hullo! Here is something interesting!"
008032 
008033 The object which had caught his eye was a small dog lash hung on
008034 one corner of the bed. The lash, however, was curled upon itself
008035 and tied so as to make a loop of whipcord.
008036 
008037 "What do you make of that, Watson?"
008038 
008039 "It's a common enough lash. But I don't know why it should be
008040 tied."
008041 
008042 "That is not quite so common, is it? Ah, me! it's a wicked world,
008043 and when a clever man turns his brains to crime it is the worst
008044 of all. I think that I have seen enough now, Miss Stoner, and
008045 with your permission we shall walk out upon the lawn."
008046 
008047 I had never seen my friend's face so grim or his brow so dark as
008048 it was when we turned from the scene of this investigation. We
008049 had walked several times up and down the lawn, neither Miss
008050 Stoner nor myself liking to break in upon his thoughts before he
008051 roused himself from his reverie.
008052 
008053 "It is very essential, Miss Stoner," said he, "that you should
008054 absolutely follow my advice in every respect."
008055 
008056 "I shall most certainly do so."
008057 
008058 "The matter is too serious for any hesitation. Your life may
008059 depend upon your compliance."
008060 
008061 "I assure you that I am in your hands."
008062 
008063 "In the first place, both my friend and I must spend the night in
008064 your room."
008065 
008066 Both Miss Stoner and I gazed at him in astonishment.
008067 
008068 "Yes, it must be so. Let me explain. I believe that that is the
008069 village inn over there?"
008070 
008071 "Yes, that is the Crown."
008072 
008073 "Very good. Your windows would be visible from there?"
008074 
008075 "Certainly."
008076 
008077 "You must confine yourself to your room, on pretence of a
008078 headache, when your stepfather comes back. Then when you hear him
008079 retire for the night, you must open the shutters of your window,
008080 undo the hasp, put your lamp there as a signal to us, and then
008081 withdraw quietly with everything which you are likely to want
008082 into the room which you used to occupy. I have no doubt that, in
008083 spite of the repairs, you could manage there for one night."
008084 
008085 "Oh, yes, easily."
008086 
008087 "The rest you will leave in our hands."
008088 
008089 "But what will you do?"
008090 
008091 "We shall spend the night in your room, and we shall investigate
008092 the cause of this noise which has disturbed you."
008093 
008094 "I believe, Mr. Holmes, that you have already made up your mind,"
008095 said Miss Stoner, laying her hand upon my companion's sleeve.
008096 
008097 "Perhaps I have."
008098 
008099 "Then, for pity's sake, tell me what was the cause of my sister's
008100 death."
008101 
008102 "I should prefer to have clearer proofs before I speak."
008103 
008104 "You can at least tell me whether my own thought is correct, and
008105 if she died from some sudden fright."
008106 
008107 "No, I do not think so. I think that there was probably some more
008108 tangible cause. And now, Miss Stoner, we must leave you for if
008109 Dr. Roylott returned and saw us our journey would be in vain.
008110 Good-bye, and be brave, for if you will do what I have told you,
008111 you may rest assured that we shall soon drive away the dangers
008112 that threaten you."
008113 
008114 Sherlock Holmes and I had no difficulty in engaging a bedroom and
008115 sitting-room at the Crown Inn. They were on the upper floor, and
008116 from our window we could command a view of the avenue gate, and
008117 of the inhabited wing of Stoke Moran Manor House. At dusk we saw
008118 Dr. Grimesby Roylott drive past, his huge form looming up beside
008119 the little figure of the lad who drove him. The boy had some
008120 slight difficulty in undoing the heavy iron gates, and we heard
008121 the hoarse roar of the doctor's voice and saw the fury with which
008122 he shook his clinched fists at him. The trap drove on, and a few
008123 minutes later we saw a sudden light spring up among the trees as
008124 the lamp was lit in one of the sitting-rooms.
008125 
008126 "Do you know, Watson," said Holmes as we sat together in the
008127 gathering darkness, "I have really some scruples as to taking you
008128 to-night. There is a distinct element of danger."
008129 
008130 "Can I be of assistance?"
008131 
008132 "Your presence might be invaluable."
008133 
008134 "Then I shall certainly come."
008135 
008136 "It is very kind of you."
008137 
008138 "You speak of danger. You have evidently seen more in these rooms
008139 than was visible to me."
008140 
008141 "No, but I fancy that I may have deduced a little more. I imagine
008142 that you saw all that I did."
008143 
008144 "I saw nothing remarkable save the bell-rope, and what purpose
008145 that could answer I confess is more than I can imagine."
008146 
008147 "You saw the ventilator, too?"
008148 
008149 "Yes, but I do not think that it is such a very unusual thing to
008150 have a small opening between two rooms. It was so small that a
008151 rat could hardly pass through."
008152 
008153 "I knew that we should find a ventilator before ever we came to
008154 Stoke Moran."
008155 
008156 "My dear Holmes!"
008157 
008158 "Oh, yes, I did. You remember in her statement she said that her
008159 sister could smell Dr. Roylott's cigar. Now, of course that
008160 suggested at once that there must be a communication between the
008161 two rooms. It could only be a small one, or it would have been
008162 remarked upon at the coroner's inquiry. I deduced a ventilator."
008163 
008164 "But what harm can there be in that?"
008165 
008166 "Well, there is at least a curious coincidence of dates. A
008167 ventilator is made, a cord is hung, and a lady who sleeps in the
008168 bed dies. Does not that strike you?"
008169 
008170 "I cannot as yet see any connection."
008171 
008172 "Did you observe anything very peculiar about that bed?"
008173 
008174 "No."
008175 
008176 "It was clamped to the floor. Did you ever see a bed fastened
008177 like that before?"
008178 
008179 "I cannot say that I have."
008180 
008181 "The lady could not move her bed. It must always be in the same
008182 relative position to the ventilator and to the rope--or so we may
008183 call it, since it was clearly never meant for a bell-pull."
008184 
008185 "Holmes," I cried, "I seem to see dimly what you are hinting at.
008186 We are only just in time to prevent some subtle and horrible
008187 crime."
008188 
008189 "Subtle enough and horrible enough. When a doctor does go wrong
008190 he is the first of criminals. He has nerve and he has knowledge.
008191 Palmer and Pritchard were among the heads of their profession.
008192 This man strikes even deeper, but I think, Watson, that we shall
008193 be able to strike deeper still. But we shall have horrors enough
008194 before the night is over; for goodness' sake let us have a quiet
008195 pipe and turn our minds for a few hours to something more
008196 cheerful."
008197 
008198 
008199 About nine o'clock the light among the trees was extinguished,
008200 and all was dark in the direction of the Manor House. Two hours
008201 passed slowly away, and then, suddenly, just at the stroke of
008202 eleven, a single bright light shone out right in front of us.
008203 
008204 "That is our signal," said Holmes, springing to his feet; "it
008205 comes from the middle window."
008206 
008207 As we passed out he exchanged a few words with the landlord,
008208 explaining that we were going on a late visit to an acquaintance,
008209 and that it was possible that we might spend the night there. A
008210 moment later we were out on the dark road, a chill wind blowing
008211 in our faces, and one yellow light twinkling in front of us
008212 through the gloom to guide us on our sombre errand.
008213 
008214 There was little difficulty in entering the grounds, for
008215 unrepaired breaches gaped in the old park wall. Making our way
008216 among the trees, we reached the lawn, crossed it, and were about
008217 to enter through the window when out from a clump of laurel
008218 bushes there darted what seemed to be a hideous and distorted
008219 child, who threw itself upon the grass with writhing limbs and
008220 then ran swiftly across the lawn into the darkness.
008221 
008222 "My God!" I whispered; "did you see it?"
008223 
008224 Holmes was for the moment as startled as I. His hand closed like
008225 a vice upon my wrist in his agitation. Then he broke into a low
008226 laugh and put his lips to my ear.
008227 
008228 "It is a nice household," he murmured. "That is the baboon."
008229 
008230 I had forgotten the strange pets which the doctor affected. There
008231 was a cheetah, too; perhaps we might find it upon our shoulders
008232 at any moment. I confess that I felt easier in my mind when,
008233 after following Holmes' example and slipping off my shoes, I
008234 found myself inside the bedroom. My companion noiselessly closed
008235 the shutters, moved the lamp onto the table, and cast his eyes
008236 round the room. All was as we had seen it in the daytime. Then
008237 creeping up to me and making a trumpet of his hand, he whispered
008238 into my ear again so gently that it was all that I could do to
008239 distinguish the words:
008240 
008241 "The least sound would be fatal to our plans."
008242 
008243 I nodded to show that I had heard.
008244 
008245 "We must sit without light. He would see it through the
008246 ventilator."
008247 
008248 I nodded again.
008249 
008250 "Do not go asleep; your very life may depend upon it. Have your
008251 pistol ready in case we should need it. I will sit on the side of
008252 the bed, and you in that chair."
008253 
008254 I took out my revolver and laid it on the corner of the table.
008255 
008256 Holmes had brought up a long thin cane, and this he placed upon
008257 the bed beside him. By it he laid the box of matches and the
008258 stump of a candle. Then he turned down the lamp, and we were left
008259 in darkness.
008260 
008261 How shall I ever forget that dreadful vigil? I could not hear a
008262 sound, not even the drawing of a breath, and yet I knew that my
008263 companion sat open-eyed, within a few feet of me, in the same
008264 state of nervous tension in which I was myself. The shutters cut
008265 off the least ray of light, and we waited in absolute darkness.
008266 
008267 From outside came the occasional cry of a night-bird, and once at
008268 our very window a long drawn catlike whine, which told us that
008269 the cheetah was indeed at liberty. Far away we could hear the
008270 deep tones of the parish clock, which boomed out every quarter of
008271 an hour. How long they seemed, those quarters! Twelve struck, and
008272 one and two and three, and still we sat waiting silently for
008273 whatever might befall.
008274 
008275 Suddenly there was the momentary gleam of a light up in the
008276 direction of the ventilator, which vanished immediately, but was
008277 succeeded by a strong smell of burning oil and heated metal.
008278 Someone in the next room had lit a dark-lantern. I heard a gentle
008279 sound of movement, and then all was silent once more, though the
008280 smell grew stronger. For half an hour I sat with straining ears.
008281 Then suddenly another sound became audible--a very gentle,
008282 soothing sound, like that of a small jet of steam escaping
008283 continually from a kettle. The instant that we heard it, Holmes
008284 sprang from the bed, struck a match, and lashed furiously with
008285 his cane at the bell-pull.
008286 
008287 "You see it, Watson?" he yelled. "You see it?"
008288 
008289 But I saw nothing. At the moment when Holmes struck the light I
008290 heard a low, clear whistle, but the sudden glare flashing into my
008291 weary eyes made it impossible for me to tell what it was at which
008292 my friend lashed so savagely. I could, however, see that his face
008293 was deadly pale and filled with horror and loathing. He had
008294 ceased to strike and was gazing up at the ventilator when
008295 suddenly there broke from the silence of the night the most
008296 horrible cry to which I have ever listened. It swelled up louder
008297 and louder, a hoarse yell of pain and fear and anger all mingled
008298 in the one dreadful shriek. They say that away down in the
008299 village, and even in the distant parsonage, that cry raised the
008300 sleepers from their beds. It struck cold to our hearts, and I
008301 stood gazing at Holmes, and he at me, until the last echoes of it
008302 had died away into the silence from which it rose.
008303 
008304 "What can it mean?" I gasped.
008305 
008306 "It means that it is all over," Holmes answered. "And perhaps,
008307 after all, it is for the best. Take your pistol, and we will
008308 enter Dr. Roylott's room."
008309 
008310 With a grave face he lit the lamp and led the way down the
008311 corridor. Twice he struck at the chamber door without any reply
008312 from within. Then he turned the handle and entered, I at his
008313 heels, with the cocked pistol in my hand.
008314 
008315 It was a singular sight which met our eyes. On the table stood a
008316 dark-lantern with the shutter half open, throwing a brilliant
008317 beam of light upon the iron safe, the door of which was ajar.
008318 Beside this table, on the wooden chair, sat Dr. Grimesby Roylott
008319 clad in a long grey dressing-gown, his bare ankles protruding
008320 beneath, and his feet thrust into red heelless Turkish slippers.
008321 Across his lap lay the short stock with the long lash which we
008322 had noticed during the day. His chin was cocked upward and his
008323 eyes were fixed in a dreadful, rigid stare at the corner of the
008324 ceiling. Round his brow he had a peculiar yellow band, with
008325 brownish speckles, which seemed to be bound tightly round his
008326 head. As we entered he made neither sound nor motion.
008327 
008328 "The band! the speckled band!" whispered Holmes.
008329 
008330 I took a step forward. In an instant his strange headgear began
008331 to move, and there reared itself from among his hair the squat
008332 diamond-shaped head and puffed neck of a loathsome serpent.
008333 
008334 "It is a swamp adder!" cried Holmes; "the deadliest snake in
008335 India. He has died within ten seconds of being bitten. Violence
008336 does, in truth, recoil upon the violent, and the schemer falls
008337 into the pit which he digs for another. Let us thrust this
008338 creature back into its den, and we can then remove Miss Stoner to
008339 some place of shelter and let the county police know what has
008340 happened."
008341 
008342 As he spoke he drew the dog-whip swiftly from the dead man's lap,
008343 and throwing the noose round the reptile's neck he drew it from
008344 its horrid perch and, carrying it at arm's length, threw it into
008345 the iron safe, which he closed upon it.
008346 
008347 Such are the true facts of the death of Dr. Grimesby Roylott, of
008348 Stoke Moran. It is not necessary that I should prolong a
008349 narrative which has already run to too great a length by telling
008350 how we broke the sad news to the terrified girl, how we conveyed
008351 her by the morning train to the care of her good aunt at Harrow,
008352 of how the slow process of official inquiry came to the
008353 conclusion that the doctor met his fate while indiscreetly
008354 playing with a dangerous pet. The little which I had yet to learn
008355 of the case was told me by Sherlock Holmes as we travelled back
008356 next day.
008357 
008358 "I had," said he, "come to an entirely erroneous conclusion which
008359 shows, my dear Watson, how dangerous it always is to reason from
008360 insufficient data. The presence of the gipsies, and the use of
008361 the word 'band,' which was used by the poor girl, no doubt, to
008362 explain the appearance which she had caught a hurried glimpse of
008363 by the light of her match, were sufficient to put me upon an
008364 entirely wrong scent. I can only claim the merit that I instantly
008365 reconsidered my position when, however, it became clear to me
008366 that whatever danger threatened an occupant of the room could not
008367 come either from the window or the door. My attention was
008368 speedily drawn, as I have already remarked to you, to this
008369 ventilator, and to the bell-rope which hung down to the bed. The
008370 discovery that this was a dummy, and that the bed was clamped to
008371 the floor, instantly gave rise to the suspicion that the rope was
008372 there as a bridge for something passing through the hole and
008373 coming to the bed. The idea of a snake instantly occurred to me,
008374 and when I coupled it with my knowledge that the doctor was
008375 furnished with a supply of creatures from India, I felt that I
008376 was probably on the right track. The idea of using a form of
008377 poison which could not possibly be discovered by any chemical
008378 test was just such a one as would occur to a clever and ruthless
008379 man who had had an Eastern training. The rapidity with which such
008380 a poison would take effect would also, from his point of view, be
008381 an advantage. It would be a sharp-eyed coroner, indeed, who could
008382 distinguish the two little dark punctures which would show where
008383 the poison fangs had done their work. Then I thought of the
008384 whistle. Of course he must recall the snake before the morning
008385 light revealed it to the victim. He had trained it, probably by
008386 the use of the milk which we saw, to return to him when summoned.
008387 He would put it through this ventilator at the hour that he
008388 thought best, with the certainty that it would crawl down the
008389 rope and land on the bed. It might or might not bite the
008390 occupant, perhaps she might escape every night for a week, but
008391 sooner or later she must fall a victim.
008392 
008393 "I had come to these conclusions before ever I had entered his
008394 room. An inspection of his chair showed me that he had been in
008395 the habit of standing on it, which of course would be necessary
008396 in order that he should reach the ventilator. The sight of the
008397 safe, the saucer of milk, and the loop of whipcord were enough to
008398 finally dispel any doubts which may have remained. The metallic
008399 clang heard by Miss Stoner was obviously caused by her stepfather
008400 hastily closing the door of his safe upon its terrible occupant.
008401 Having once made up my mind, you know the steps which I took in
008402 order to put the matter to the proof. I heard the creature hiss
008403 as I have no doubt that you did also, and I instantly lit the
008404 light and attacked it."
008405 
008406 "With the result of driving it through the ventilator."
008407 
008408 "And also with the result of causing it to turn upon its master
008409 at the other side. Some of the blows of my cane came home and
008410 roused its snakish temper, so that it flew upon the first person
008411 it saw. In this way I am no doubt indirectly responsible for Dr.
008412 Grimesby Roylott's death, and I cannot say that it is likely to
008413 weigh very heavily upon my conscience."
008414 
008415 
008416 
008417 IX. THE ADVENTURE OF THE ENGINEER'S THUMB
008418 
008419 Of all the problems which have been submitted to my friend, Mr.
008420 Sherlock Holmes, for solution during the years of our intimacy,
008421 there were only two which I was the means of introducing to his
008422 notice--that of Mr. Hatherley's thumb, and that of Colonel
008423 Warburton's madness. Of these the latter may have afforded a
008424 finer field for an acute and original observer, but the other was
008425 so strange in its inception and so dramatic in its details that
008426 it may be the more worthy of being placed upon record, even if it
008427 gave my friend fewer openings for those deductive methods of
008428 reasoning by which he achieved such remarkable results. The story
008429 has, I believe, been told more than once in the newspapers, but,
008430 like all such narratives, its effect is much less striking when
008431 set forth en bloc in a single half-column of print than when the
008432 facts slowly evolve before your own eyes, and the mystery clears
008433 gradually away as each new discovery furnishes a step which leads
008434 on to the complete truth. At the time the circumstances made a
008435 deep impression upon me, and the lapse of two years has hardly
008436 served to weaken the effect.
008437 
008438 It was in the summer of '89, not long after my marriage, that the
008439 events occurred which I am now about to summarise. I had returned
008440 to civil practice and had finally abandoned Holmes in his Baker
008441 Street rooms, although I continually visited him and occasionally
008442 even persuaded him to forgo his Bohemian habits so far as to come
008443 and visit us. My practice had steadily increased, and as I
008444 happened to live at no very great distance from Paddington
008445 Station, I got a few patients from among the officials. One of
008446 these, whom I had cured of a painful and lingering disease, was
008447 never weary of advertising my virtues and of endeavouring to send
008448 me on every sufferer over whom he might have any influence.
008449 
008450 One morning, at a little before seven o'clock, I was awakened by
008451 the maid tapping at the door to announce that two men had come
008452 from Paddington and were waiting in the consulting-room. I
008453 dressed hurriedly, for I knew by experience that railway cases
008454 were seldom trivial, and hastened downstairs. As I descended, my
008455 old ally, the guard, came out of the room and closed the door
008456 tightly behind him.
008457 
008458 "I've got him here," he whispered, jerking his thumb over his
008459 shoulder; "he's all right."
008460 
008461 "What is it, then?" I asked, for his manner suggested that it was
008462 some strange creature which he had caged up in my room.
008463 
008464 "It's a new patient," he whispered. "I thought I'd bring him
008465 round myself; then he couldn't slip away. There he is, all safe
008466 and sound. I must go now, Doctor; I have my dooties, just the
008467 same as you." And off he went, this trusty tout, without even
008468 giving me time to thank him.
008469 
008470 I entered my consulting-room and found a gentleman seated by the
008471 table. He was quietly dressed in a suit of heather tweed with a
008472 soft cloth cap which he had laid down upon my books. Round one of
008473 his hands he had a handkerchief wrapped, which was mottled all
008474 over with bloodstains. He was young, not more than
008475 five-and-twenty, I should say, with a strong, masculine face; but
008476 he was exceedingly pale and gave me the impression of a man who
008477 was suffering from some strong agitation, which it took all his
008478 strength of mind to control.
008479 
008480 "I am sorry to knock you up so early, Doctor," said he, "but I
008481 have had a very serious accident during the night. I came in by
008482 train this morning, and on inquiring at Paddington as to where I
008483 might find a doctor, a worthy fellow very kindly escorted me
008484 here. I gave the maid a card, but I see that she has left it upon
008485 the side-table."
008486 
008487 I took it up and glanced at it. "Mr. Victor Hatherley, hydraulic
008488 engineer, 16A, Victoria Street (3rd floor)." That was the name,
008489 style, and abode of my morning visitor. "I regret that I have
008490 kept you waiting," said I, sitting down in my library-chair. "You
008491 are fresh from a night journey, I understand, which is in itself
008492 a monotonous occupation."
008493 
008494 "Oh, my night could not be called monotonous," said he, and
008495 laughed. He laughed very heartily, with a high, ringing note,
008496 leaning back in his chair and shaking his sides. All my medical
008497 instincts rose up against that laugh.
008498 
008499 "Stop it!" I cried; "pull yourself together!" and I poured out
008500 some water from a caraffe.
008501 
008502 It was useless, however. He was off in one of those hysterical
008503 outbursts which come upon a strong nature when some great crisis
008504 is over and gone. Presently he came to himself once more, very
008505 weary and pale-looking.
008506 
008507 "I have been making a fool of myself," he gasped.
008508 
008509 "Not at all. Drink this." I dashed some brandy into the water,
008510 and the colour began to come back to his bloodless cheeks.
008511 
008512 "That's better!" said he. "And now, Doctor, perhaps you would
008513 kindly attend to my thumb, or rather to the place where my thumb
008514 used to be."
008515 
008516 He unwound the handkerchief and held out his hand. It gave even
008517 my hardened nerves a shudder to look at it. There were four
008518 protruding fingers and a horrid red, spongy surface where the
008519 thumb should have been. It had been hacked or torn right out from
008520 the roots.
008521 
008522 "Good heavens!" I cried, "this is a terrible injury. It must have
008523 bled considerably."
008524 
008525 "Yes, it did. I fainted when it was done, and I think that I must
008526 have been senseless for a long time. When I came to I found that
008527 it was still bleeding, so I tied one end of my handkerchief very
008528 tightly round the wrist and braced it up with a twig."
008529 
008530 "Excellent! You should have been a surgeon."
008531 
008532 "It is a question of hydraulics, you see, and came within my own
008533 province."
008534 
008535 "This has been done," said I, examining the wound, "by a very
008536 heavy and sharp instrument."
008537 
008538 "A thing like a cleaver," said he.
008539 
008540 "An accident, I presume?"
008541 
008542 "By no means."
008543 
008544 "What! a murderous attack?"
008545 
008546 "Very murderous indeed."
008547 
008548 "You horrify me."
008549 
008550 I sponged the wound, cleaned it, dressed it, and finally covered
008551 it over with cotton wadding and carbolised bandages. He lay back
008552 without wincing, though he bit his lip from time to time.
008553 
008554 "How is that?" I asked when I had finished.
008555 
008556 "Capital! Between your brandy and your bandage, I feel a new man.
008557 I was very weak, but I have had a good deal to go through."
008558 
008559 "Perhaps you had better not speak of the matter. It is evidently
008560 trying to your nerves."
008561 
008562 "Oh, no, not now. I shall have to tell my tale to the police;
008563 but, between ourselves, if it were not for the convincing
008564 evidence of this wound of mine, I should be surprised if they
008565 believed my statement, for it is a very extraordinary one, and I
008566 have not much in the way of proof with which to back it up; and,
008567 even if they believe me, the clues which I can give them are so
008568 vague that it is a question whether justice will be done."
008569 
008570 "Ha!" cried I, "if it is anything in the nature of a problem
008571 which you desire to see solved, I should strongly recommend you
008572 to come to my friend, Mr. Sherlock Holmes, before you go to the
008573 official police."
008574 
008575 "Oh, I have heard of that fellow," answered my visitor, "and I
008576 should be very glad if he would take the matter up, though of
008577 course I must use the official police as well. Would you give me
008578 an introduction to him?"
008579 
008580 "I'll do better. I'll take you round to him myself."
008581 
008582 "I should be immensely obliged to you."
008583 
008584 "We'll call a cab and go together. We shall just be in time to
008585 have a little breakfast with him. Do you feel equal to it?"
008586 
008587 "Yes; I shall not feel easy until I have told my story."
008588 
008589 "Then my servant will call a cab, and I shall be with you in an
008590 instant." I rushed upstairs, explained the matter shortly to my
008591 wife, and in five minutes was inside a hansom, driving with my
008592 new acquaintance to Baker Street.
008593 
008594 Sherlock Holmes was, as I expected, lounging about his
008595 sitting-room in his dressing-gown, reading the agony column of The
008596 Times and smoking his before-breakfast pipe, which was composed
008597 of all the plugs and dottles left from his smokes of the day
008598 before, all carefully dried and collected on the corner of the
008599 mantelpiece. He received us in his quietly genial fashion,
008600 ordered fresh rashers and eggs, and joined us in a hearty meal.
008601 When it was concluded he settled our new acquaintance upon the
008602 sofa, placed a pillow beneath his head, and laid a glass of
008603 brandy and water within his reach.
008604 
008605 "It is easy to see that your experience has been no common one,
008606 Mr. Hatherley," said he. "Pray, lie down there and make yourself
008607 absolutely at home. Tell us what you can, but stop when you are
008608 tired and keep up your strength with a little stimulant."
008609 
008610 "Thank you," said my patient, "but I have felt another man since
008611 the doctor bandaged me, and I think that your breakfast has
008612 completed the cure. I shall take up as little of your valuable
008613 time as possible, so I shall start at once upon my peculiar
008614 experiences."
008615 
008616 Holmes sat in his big armchair with the weary, heavy-lidded
008617 expression which veiled his keen and eager nature, while I sat
008618 opposite to him, and we listened in silence to the strange story
008619 which our visitor detailed to us.
008620 
008621 "You must know," said he, "that I am an orphan and a bachelor,
008622 residing alone in lodgings in London. By profession I am a
008623 hydraulic engineer, and I have had considerable experience of my
008624 work during the seven years that I was apprenticed to Venner &
008625 Matheson, the well-known firm, of Greenwich. Two years ago,
008626 having served my time, and having also come into a fair sum of
008627 money through my poor father's death, I determined to start in
008628 business for myself and took professional chambers in Victoria
008629 Street.
008630 
008631 "I suppose that everyone finds his first independent start in
008632 business a dreary experience. To me it has been exceptionally so.
008633 During two years I have had three consultations and one small
008634 job, and that is absolutely all that my profession has brought
008635 me. My gross takings amount to 27 pounds 10s. Every day, from
008636 nine in the morning until four in the afternoon, I waited in my
008637 little den, until at last my heart began to sink, and I came to
008638 believe that I should never have any practice at all.
008639 
008640 "Yesterday, however, just as I was thinking of leaving the
008641 office, my clerk entered to say there was a gentleman waiting who
008642 wished to see me upon business. He brought up a card, too, with
008643 the name of 'Colonel Lysander Stark' engraved upon it. Close at
008644 his heels came the colonel himself, a man rather over the middle
008645 size, but of an exceeding thinness. I do not think that I have
008646 ever seen so thin a man. His whole face sharpened away into nose
008647 and chin, and the skin of his cheeks was drawn quite tense over
008648 his outstanding bones. Yet this emaciation seemed to be his
008649 natural habit, and due to no disease, for his eye was bright, his
008650 step brisk, and his bearing assured. He was plainly but neatly
008651 dressed, and his age, I should judge, would be nearer forty than
008652 thirty.
008653 
008654 "'Mr. Hatherley?' said he, with something of a German accent.
008655 'You have been recommended to me, Mr. Hatherley, as being a man
008656 who is not only proficient in his profession but is also discreet
008657 and capable of preserving a secret.'
008658 
008659 "I bowed, feeling as flattered as any young man would at such an
008660 address. 'May I ask who it was who gave me so good a character?'
008661 
008662 "'Well, perhaps it is better that I should not tell you that just
008663 at this moment. I have it from the same source that you are both
008664 an orphan and a bachelor and are residing alone in London.'
008665 
008666 "'That is quite correct,' I answered; 'but you will excuse me if
008667 I say that I cannot see how all this bears upon my professional
008668 qualifications. I understand that it was on a professional matter
008669 that you wished to speak to me?'
008670 
008671 "'Undoubtedly so. But you will find that all I say is really to
008672 the point. I have a professional commission for you, but absolute
008673 secrecy is quite essential--absolute secrecy, you understand, and
008674 of course we may expect that more from a man who is alone than
008675 from one who lives in the bosom of his family.'
008676 
008677 "'If I promise to keep a secret,' said I, 'you may absolutely
008678 depend upon my doing so.'
008679 
008680 "He looked very hard at me as I spoke, and it seemed to me that I
008681 had never seen so suspicious and questioning an eye.
008682 
008683 "'Do you promise, then?' said he at last.
008684 
008685 "'Yes, I promise.'
008686 
008687 "'Absolute and complete silence before, during, and after? No
008688 reference to the matter at all, either in word or writing?'
008689 
008690 "'I have already given you my word.'
008691 
008692 "'Very good.' He suddenly sprang up, and darting like lightning
008693 across the room he flung open the door. The passage outside was
008694 empty.
008695 
008696 "'That's all right,' said he, coming back. 'I know that clerks are
008697 sometimes curious as to their master's affairs. Now we can talk
008698 in safety.' He drew up his chair very close to mine and began to
008699 stare at me again with the same questioning and thoughtful look.
008700 
008701 "A feeling of repulsion, and of something akin to fear had begun
008702 to rise within me at the strange antics of this fleshless man.
008703 Even my dread of losing a client could not restrain me from
008704 showing my impatience.
008705 
008706 "'I beg that you will state your business, sir,' said I; 'my time
008707 is of value.' Heaven forgive me for that last sentence, but the
008708 words came to my lips.
008709 
008710 "'How would fifty guineas for a night's work suit you?' he asked.
008711 
008712 "'Most admirably.'
008713 
008714 "'I say a night's work, but an hour's would be nearer the mark. I
008715 simply want your opinion about a hydraulic stamping machine which
008716 has got out of gear. If you show us what is wrong we shall soon
008717 set it right ourselves. What do you think of such a commission as
008718 that?'
008719 
008720 "'The work appears to be light and the pay munificent.'
008721 
008722 "'Precisely so. We shall want you to come to-night by the last
008723 train.'
008724 
008725 "'Where to?'
008726 
008727 "'To Eyford, in Berkshire. It is a little place near the borders
008728 of Oxfordshire, and within seven miles of Reading. There is a
008729 train from Paddington which would bring you there at about
008730 11:15.'
008731 
008732 "'Very good.'
008733 
008734 "'I shall come down in a carriage to meet you.'
008735 
008736 "'There is a drive, then?'
008737 
008738 "'Yes, our little place is quite out in the country. It is a good
008739 seven miles from Eyford Station.'
008740 
008741 "'Then we can hardly get there before midnight. I suppose there
008742 would be no chance of a train back. I should be compelled to stop
008743 the night.'
008744 
008745 "'Yes, we could easily give you a shake-down.'
008746 
008747 "'That is very awkward. Could I not come at some more convenient
008748 hour?'
008749 
008750 "'We have judged it best that you should come late. It is to
008751 recompense you for any inconvenience that we are paying to you, a
008752 young and unknown man, a fee which would buy an opinion from the
008753 very heads of your profession. Still, of course, if you would
008754 like to draw out of the business, there is plenty of time to do
008755 so.'
008756 
008757 "I thought of the fifty guineas, and of how very useful they
008758 would be to me. 'Not at all,' said I, 'I shall be very happy to
008759 accommodate myself to your wishes. I should like, however, to
008760 understand a little more clearly what it is that you wish me to
008761 do.'
008762 
008763 "'Quite so. It is very natural that the pledge of secrecy which
008764 we have exacted from you should have aroused your curiosity. I
008765 have no wish to commit you to anything without your having it all
008766 laid before you. I suppose that we are absolutely safe from
008767 eavesdroppers?'
008768 
008769 "'Entirely.'
008770 
008771 "'Then the matter stands thus. You are probably aware that
008772 fuller's-earth is a valuable product, and that it is only found
008773 in one or two places in England?'
008774 
008775 "'I have heard so.'
008776 
008777 "'Some little time ago I bought a small place--a very small
008778 place--within ten miles of Reading. I was fortunate enough to
008779 discover that there was a deposit of fuller's-earth in one of my
008780 fields. On examining it, however, I found that this deposit was a
008781 comparatively small one, and that it formed a link between two
008782 very much larger ones upon the right and left--both of them,
008783 however, in the grounds of my neighbours. These good people were
008784 absolutely ignorant that their land contained that which was
008785 quite as valuable as a gold-mine. Naturally, it was to my
008786 interest to buy their land before they discovered its true value,
008787 but unfortunately I had no capital by which I could do this. I
008788 took a few of my friends into the secret, however, and they
008789 suggested that we should quietly and secretly work our own little
008790 deposit and that in this way we should earn the money which would
008791 enable us to buy the neighbouring fields. This we have now been
008792 doing for some time, and in order to help us in our operations we
008793 erected a hydraulic press. This press, as I have already
008794 explained, has got out of order, and we wish your advice upon the
008795 subject. We guard our secret very jealously, however, and if it
008796 once became known that we had hydraulic engineers coming to our
008797 little house, it would soon rouse inquiry, and then, if the facts
008798 came out, it would be good-bye to any chance of getting these
008799 fields and carrying out our plans. That is why I have made you
008800 promise me that you will not tell a human being that you are
008801 going to Eyford to-night. I hope that I make it all plain?'
008802 
008803 "'I quite follow you,' said I. 'The only point which I could not
008804 quite understand was what use you could make of a hydraulic press
008805 in excavating fuller's-earth, which, as I understand, is dug out
008806 like gravel from a pit.'
008807 
008808 "'Ah!' said he carelessly, 'we have our own process. We compress
008809 the earth into bricks, so as to remove them without revealing
008810 what they are. But that is a mere detail. I have taken you fully
008811 into my confidence now, Mr. Hatherley, and I have shown you how I
008812 trust you.' He rose as he spoke. 'I shall expect you, then, at
008813 Eyford at 11:15.'
008814 
008815 "'I shall certainly be there.'
008816 
008817 "'And not a word to a soul.' He looked at me with a last long,
008818 questioning gaze, and then, pressing my hand in a cold, dank
008819 grasp, he hurried from the room.
008820 
008821 "Well, when I came to think it all over in cool blood I was very
008822 much astonished, as you may both think, at this sudden commission
008823 which had been intrusted to me. On the one hand, of course, I was
008824 glad, for the fee was at least tenfold what I should have asked
008825 had I set a price upon my own services, and it was possible that
008826 this order might lead to other ones. On the other hand, the face
008827 and manner of my patron had made an unpleasant impression upon
008828 me, and I could not think that his explanation of the
008829 fuller's-earth was sufficient to explain the necessity for my
008830 coming at midnight, and his extreme anxiety lest I should tell
008831 anyone of my errand. However, I threw all fears to the winds, ate
008832 a hearty supper, drove to Paddington, and started off, having
008833 obeyed to the letter the injunction as to holding my tongue.
008834 
008835 "At Reading I had to change not only my carriage but my station.
008836 However, I was in time for the last train to Eyford, and I
008837 reached the little dim-lit station after eleven o'clock. I was the
008838 only passenger who got out there, and there was no one upon the
008839 platform save a single sleepy porter with a lantern. As I passed
008840 out through the wicket gate, however, I found my acquaintance of
008841 the morning waiting in the shadow upon the other side. Without a
008842 word he grasped my arm and hurried me into a carriage, the door
008843 of which was standing open. He drew up the windows on either
008844 side, tapped on the wood-work, and away we went as fast as the
008845 horse could go."
008846 
008847 "One horse?" interjected Holmes.
008848 
008849 "Yes, only one."
008850 
008851 "Did you observe the colour?"
008852 
008853 "Yes, I saw it by the side-lights when I was stepping into the
008854 carriage. It was a chestnut."
008855 
008856 "Tired-looking or fresh?"
008857 
008858 "Oh, fresh and glossy."
008859 
008860 "Thank you. I am sorry to have interrupted you. Pray continue
008861 your most interesting statement."
008862 
008863 "Away we went then, and we drove for at least an hour. Colonel
008864 Lysander Stark had said that it was only seven miles, but I
008865 should think, from the rate that we seemed to go, and from the
008866 time that we took, that it must have been nearer twelve. He sat
008867 at my side in silence all the time, and I was aware, more than
008868 once when I glanced in his direction, that he was looking at me
008869 with great intensity. The country roads seem to be not very good
008870 in that part of the world, for we lurched and jolted terribly. I
008871 tried to look out of the windows to see something of where we
008872 were, but they were made of frosted glass, and I could make out
008873 nothing save the occasional bright blur of a passing light. Now
008874 and then I hazarded some remark to break the monotony of the
008875 journey, but the colonel answered only in monosyllables, and the
008876 conversation soon flagged. At last, however, the bumping of the
008877 road was exchanged for the crisp smoothness of a gravel-drive,
008878 and the carriage came to a stand. Colonel Lysander Stark sprang
008879 out, and, as I followed after him, pulled me swiftly into a porch
008880 which gaped in front of us. We stepped, as it were, right out of
008881 the carriage and into the hall, so that I failed to catch the
008882 most fleeting glance of the front of the house. The instant that
008883 I had crossed the threshold the door slammed heavily behind us,
008884 and I heard faintly the rattle of the wheels as the carriage
008885 drove away.
008886 
008887 "It was pitch dark inside the house, and the colonel fumbled
008888 about looking for matches and muttering under his breath.
008889 Suddenly a door opened at the other end of the passage, and a
008890 long, golden bar of light shot out in our direction. It grew
008891 broader, and a woman appeared with a lamp in her hand, which she
008892 held above her head, pushing her face forward and peering at us.
008893 I could see that she was pretty, and from the gloss with which
008894 the light shone upon her dark dress I knew that it was a rich
008895 material. She spoke a few words in a foreign tongue in a tone as
008896 though asking a question, and when my companion answered in a
008897 gruff monosyllable she gave such a start that the lamp nearly
008898 fell from her hand. Colonel Stark went up to her, whispered
008899 something in her ear, and then, pushing her back into the room
008900 from whence she had come, he walked towards me again with the
008901 lamp in his hand.
008902 
008903 "'Perhaps you will have the kindness to wait in this room for a
008904 few minutes,' said he, throwing open another door. It was a
008905 quiet, little, plainly furnished room, with a round table in the
008906 centre, on which several German books were scattered. Colonel
008907 Stark laid down the lamp on the top of a harmonium beside the
008908 door. 'I shall not keep you waiting an instant,' said he, and
008909 vanished into the darkness.
008910 
008911 "I glanced at the books upon the table, and in spite of my
008912 ignorance of German I could see that two of them were treatises
008913 on science, the others being volumes of poetry. Then I walked
008914 across to the window, hoping that I might catch some glimpse of
008915 the country-side, but an oak shutter, heavily barred, was folded
008916 across it. It was a wonderfully silent house. There was an old
008917 clock ticking loudly somewhere in the passage, but otherwise
008918 everything was deadly still. A vague feeling of uneasiness began
008919 to steal over me. Who were these German people, and what were
008920 they doing living in this strange, out-of-the-way place? And
008921 where was the place? I was ten miles or so from Eyford, that was
008922 all I knew, but whether north, south, east, or west I had no
008923 idea. For that matter, Reading, and possibly other large towns,
008924 were within that radius, so the place might not be so secluded,
008925 after all. Yet it was quite certain, from the absolute stillness,
008926 that we were in the country. I paced up and down the room,
008927 humming a tune under my breath to keep up my spirits and feeling
008928 that I was thoroughly earning my fifty-guinea fee.
008929 
008930 "Suddenly, without any preliminary sound in the midst of the
008931 utter stillness, the door of my room swung slowly open. The woman
008932 was standing in the aperture, the darkness of the hall behind
008933 her, the yellow light from my lamp beating upon her eager and
008934 beautiful face. I could see at a glance that she was sick with
008935 fear, and the sight sent a chill to my own heart. She held up one
008936 shaking finger to warn me to be silent, and she shot a few
008937 whispered words of broken English at me, her eyes glancing back,
008938 like those of a frightened horse, into the gloom behind her.
008939 
008940 "'I would go,' said she, trying hard, as it seemed to me, to
008941 speak calmly; 'I would go. I should not stay here. There is no
008942 good for you to do.'
008943 
008944 "'But, madam,' said I, 'I have not yet done what I came for. I
008945 cannot possibly leave until I have seen the machine.'
008946 
008947 "'It is not worth your while to wait,' she went on. 'You can pass
008948 through the door; no one hinders.' And then, seeing that I smiled
008949 and shook my head, she suddenly threw aside her constraint and
008950 made a step forward, with her hands wrung together. 'For the love
008951 of Heaven!' she whispered, 'get away from here before it is too
008952 late!'
008953 
008954 "But I am somewhat headstrong by nature, and the more ready to
008955 engage in an affair when there is some obstacle in the way. I
008956 thought of my fifty-guinea fee, of my wearisome journey, and of
008957 the unpleasant night which seemed to be before me. Was it all to
008958 go for nothing? Why should I slink away without having carried
008959 out my commission, and without the payment which was my due? This
008960 woman might, for all I knew, be a monomaniac. With a stout
008961 bearing, therefore, though her manner had shaken me more than I
008962 cared to confess, I still shook my head and declared my intention
008963 of remaining where I was. She was about to renew her entreaties
008964 when a door slammed overhead, and the sound of several footsteps
008965 was heard upon the stairs. She listened for an instant, threw up
008966 her hands with a despairing gesture, and vanished as suddenly and
008967 as noiselessly as she had come.
008968 
008969 "The newcomers were Colonel Lysander Stark and a short thick man
008970 with a chinchilla beard growing out of the creases of his double
008971 chin, who was introduced to me as Mr. Ferguson.
008972 
008973 "'This is my secretary and manager,' said the colonel. 'By the
008974 way, I was under the impression that I left this door shut just
008975 now. I fear that you have felt the draught.'
008976 
008977 "'On the contrary,' said I, 'I opened the door myself because I
008978 felt the room to be a little close.'
008979 
008980 "He shot one of his suspicious looks at me. 'Perhaps we had
008981 better proceed to business, then,' said he. 'Mr. Ferguson and I
008982 will take you up to see the machine.'
008983 
008984 "'I had better put my hat on, I suppose.'
008985 
008986 "'Oh, no, it is in the house.'
008987 
008988 "'What, you dig fuller's-earth in the house?'
008989 
008990 "'No, no. This is only where we compress it. But never mind that.
008991 All we wish you to do is to examine the machine and to let us
008992 know what is wrong with it.'
008993 
008994 "We went upstairs together, the colonel first with the lamp, the
008995 fat manager and I behind him. It was a labyrinth of an old house,
008996 with corridors, passages, narrow winding staircases, and little
008997 low doors, the thresholds of which were hollowed out by the
008998 generations who had crossed them. There were no carpets and no
008999 signs of any furniture above the ground floor, while the plaster
009000 was peeling off the walls, and the damp was breaking through in
009001 green, unhealthy blotches. I tried to put on as unconcerned an
009002 air as possible, but I had not forgotten the warnings of the
009003 lady, even though I disregarded them, and I kept a keen eye upon
009004 my two companions. Ferguson appeared to be a morose and silent
009005 man, but I could see from the little that he said that he was at
009006 least a fellow-countryman.
009007 
009008 "Colonel Lysander Stark stopped at last before a low door, which
009009 he unlocked. Within was a small, square room, in which the three
009010 of us could hardly get at one time. Ferguson remained outside,
009011 and the colonel ushered me in.
009012 
009013 "'We are now,' said he, 'actually within the hydraulic press, and
009014 it would be a particularly unpleasant thing for us if anyone were
009015 to turn it on. The ceiling of this small chamber is really the
009016 end of the descending piston, and it comes down with the force of
009017 many tons upon this metal floor. There are small lateral columns
009018 of water outside which receive the force, and which transmit and
009019 multiply it in the manner which is familiar to you. The machine
009020 goes readily enough, but there is some stiffness in the working
009021 of it, and it has lost a little of its force. Perhaps you will
009022 have the goodness to look it over and to show us how we can set
009023 it right.'
009024 
009025 "I took the lamp from him, and I examined the machine very
009026 thoroughly. It was indeed a gigantic one, and capable of
009027 exercising enormous pressure. When I passed outside, however, and
009028 pressed down the levers which controlled it, I knew at once by
009029 the whishing sound that there was a slight leakage, which allowed
009030 a regurgitation of water through one of the side cylinders. An
009031 examination showed that one of the india-rubber bands which was
009032 round the head of a driving-rod had shrunk so as not quite to
009033 fill the socket along which it worked. This was clearly the cause
009034 of the loss of power, and I pointed it out to my companions, who
009035 followed my remarks very carefully and asked several practical
009036 questions as to how they should proceed to set it right. When I
009037 had made it clear to them, I returned to the main chamber of the
009038 machine and took a good look at it to satisfy my own curiosity.
009039 It was obvious at a glance that the story of the fuller's-earth
009040 was the merest fabrication, for it would be absurd to suppose
009041 that so powerful an engine could be designed for so inadequate a
009042 purpose. The walls were of wood, but the floor consisted of a
009043 large iron trough, and when I came to examine it I could see a
009044 crust of metallic deposit all over it. I had stooped and was
009045 scraping at this to see exactly what it was when I heard a
009046 muttered exclamation in German and saw the cadaverous face of the
009047 colonel looking down at me.
009048 
009049 "'What are you doing there?' he asked.
009050 
009051 "I felt angry at having been tricked by so elaborate a story as
009052 that which he had told me. 'I was admiring your fuller's-earth,'
009053 said I; 'I think that I should be better able to advise you as to
009054 your machine if I knew what the exact purpose was for which it
009055 was used.'
009056 
009057 "The instant that I uttered the words I regretted the rashness of
009058 my speech. His face set hard, and a baleful light sprang up in
009059 his grey eyes.
009060 
009061 "'Very well,' said he, 'you shall know all about the machine.' He
009062 took a step backward, slammed the little door, and turned the key
009063 in the lock. I rushed towards it and pulled at the handle, but it
009064 was quite secure, and did not give in the least to my kicks and
009065 shoves. 'Hullo!' I yelled. 'Hullo! Colonel! Let me out!'
009066 
009067 "And then suddenly in the silence I heard a sound which sent my
009068 heart into my mouth. It was the clank of the levers and the swish
009069 of the leaking cylinder. He had set the engine at work. The lamp
009070 still stood upon the floor where I had placed it when examining
009071 the trough. By its light I saw that the black ceiling was coming
009072 down upon me, slowly, jerkily, but, as none knew better than
009073 myself, with a force which must within a minute grind me to a
009074 shapeless pulp. I threw myself, screaming, against the door, and
009075 dragged with my nails at the lock. I implored the colonel to let
009076 me out, but the remorseless clanking of the levers drowned my
009077 cries. The ceiling was only a foot or two above my head, and with
009078 my hand upraised I could feel its hard, rough surface. Then it
009079 flashed through my mind that the pain of my death would depend
009080 very much upon the position in which I met it. If I lay on my
009081 face the weight would come upon my spine, and I shuddered to
009082 think of that dreadful snap. Easier the other way, perhaps; and
009083 yet, had I the nerve to lie and look up at that deadly black
009084 shadow wavering down upon me? Already I was unable to stand
009085 erect, when my eye caught something which brought a gush of hope
009086 back to my heart.
009087 
009088 "I have said that though the floor and ceiling were of iron, the
009089 walls were of wood. As I gave a last hurried glance around, I saw
009090 a thin line of yellow light between two of the boards, which
009091 broadened and broadened as a small panel was pushed backward. For
009092 an instant I could hardly believe that here was indeed a door
009093 which led away from death. The next instant I threw myself
009094 through, and lay half-fainting upon the other side. The panel had
009095 closed again behind me, but the crash of the lamp, and a few
009096 moments afterwards the clang of the two slabs of metal, told me
009097 how narrow had been my escape.
009098 
009099 "I was recalled to myself by a frantic plucking at my wrist, and
009100 I found myself lying upon the stone floor of a narrow corridor,
009101 while a woman bent over me and tugged at me with her left hand,
009102 while she held a candle in her right. It was the same good friend
009103 whose warning I had so foolishly rejected.
009104 
009105 "'Come! come!' she cried breathlessly. 'They will be here in a
009106 moment. They will see that you are not there. Oh, do not waste
009107 the so-precious time, but come!'
009108 
009109 "This time, at least, I did not scorn her advice. I staggered to
009110 my feet and ran with her along the corridor and down a winding
009111 stair. The latter led to another broad passage, and just as we
009112 reached it we heard the sound of running feet and the shouting of
009113 two voices, one answering the other from the floor on which  we
009114 were and from the one beneath. My guide stopped and looked about
009115 her like one  who is at her wit's end. Then she threw open a door
009116 which led into a bedroom, through the window of which the moon
009117 was shining brightly.
009118 
009119 "'It is your only chance,' said she. 'It is high, but it may be
009120 that you can jump it.'
009121 
009122 "As she spoke a light sprang into view at the further end of the
009123 passage, and I saw the lean figure of Colonel Lysander Stark
009124 rushing forward with a lantern in one hand and a weapon like a
009125 butcher's cleaver in the other. I rushed across the bedroom,
009126 flung open the window, and looked out. How quiet and sweet and
009127 wholesome the garden looked in the moonlight, and it could not be
009128 more than thirty feet down. I clambered out upon the sill, but I
009129 hesitated to jump until I should have heard what passed between
009130 my saviour and the ruffian who pursued me. If she were ill-used,
009131 then at any risks I was determined to go back to her assistance.
009132 The thought had hardly flashed through my mind before he was at
009133 the door, pushing his way past her; but she threw her arms round
009134 him and tried to hold him back.
009135 
009136 "'Fritz! Fritz!' she cried in English, 'remember your promise
009137 after the last time. You said it should not be again. He will be
009138 silent! Oh, he will be silent!'
009139 
009140 "'You are mad, Elise!' he shouted, struggling to break away from
009141 her. 'You will be the ruin of us. He has seen too much. Let me
009142 pass, I say!' He dashed her to one side, and, rushing to the
009143 window, cut at me with his heavy weapon. I had let myself go, and
009144 was hanging by the hands to the sill, when his blow fell. I was
009145 conscious of a dull pain, my grip loosened, and I fell into the
009146 garden below.
009147 
009148 "I was shaken but not hurt by the fall; so I picked myself up and
009149 rushed off among the bushes as hard as I could run, for I
009150 understood that I was far from being out of danger yet. Suddenly,
009151 however, as I ran, a deadly dizziness and sickness came over me.
009152 I glanced down at my hand, which was throbbing painfully, and
009153 then, for the first time, saw that my thumb had been cut off and
009154 that the blood was pouring from my wound. I endeavoured to tie my
009155 handkerchief round it, but there came a sudden buzzing in my
009156 ears, and next moment I fell in a dead faint among the
009157 rose-bushes.
009158 
009159 "How long I remained unconscious I cannot tell. It must have been
009160 a very long time, for the moon had sunk, and a bright morning was
009161 breaking when I came to myself. My clothes were all sodden with
009162 dew, and my coat-sleeve was drenched with blood from my wounded
009163 thumb. The smarting of it recalled in an instant all the
009164 particulars of my night's adventure, and I sprang to my feet with
009165 the feeling that I might hardly yet be safe from my pursuers. But
009166 to my astonishment, when I came to look round me, neither house
009167 nor garden were to be seen. I had been lying in an angle of the
009168 hedge close by the highroad, and just a little lower down was a
009169 long building, which proved, upon my approaching it, to be the
009170 very station at which I had arrived upon the previous night. Were
009171 it not for the ugly wound upon my hand, all that had passed
009172 during those dreadful hours might have been an evil dream.
009173 
009174 "Half dazed, I went into the station and asked about the morning
009175 train. There would be one to Reading in less than an hour. The
009176 same porter was on duty, I found, as had been there when I
009177 arrived. I inquired of him whether he had ever heard of Colonel
009178 Lysander Stark. The name was strange to him. Had he observed a
009179 carriage the night before waiting for me? No, he had not. Was
009180 there a police-station anywhere near? There was one about three
009181 miles off.
009182 
009183 "It was too far for me to go, weak and ill as I was. I determined
009184 to wait until I got back to town before telling my story to the
009185 police. It was a little past six when I arrived, so I went first
009186 to have my wound dressed, and then the doctor was kind enough to
009187 bring me along here. I put the case into your hands and shall do
009188 exactly what you advise."
009189 
009190 We both sat in silence for some little time after listening to
009191 this extraordinary narrative. Then Sherlock Holmes pulled down
009192 from the shelf one of the ponderous commonplace books in which he
009193 placed his cuttings.
009194 
009195 "Here is an advertisement which will interest you," said he. "It
009196 appeared in all the papers about a year ago. Listen to this:
009197 'Lost, on the 9th inst., Mr. Jeremiah Hayling, aged
009198 twenty-six, a hydraulic engineer. Left his lodgings at ten
009199 o'clock at night, and has not been heard of since. Was
009200 dressed in,' etc., etc. Ha! That represents the last time that
009201 the colonel needed to have his machine overhauled, I fancy."
009202 
009203 "Good heavens!" cried my patient. "Then that explains what the
009204 girl said."
009205 
009206 "Undoubtedly. It is quite clear that the colonel was a cool and
009207 desperate man, who was absolutely determined that nothing should
009208 stand in the way of his little game, like those out-and-out
009209 pirates who will leave no survivor from a captured ship. Well,
009210 every moment now is precious, so if you feel equal to it we shall
009211 go down to Scotland Yard at once as a preliminary to starting for
009212 Eyford."
009213 
009214 Some three hours or so afterwards we were all in the train
009215 together, bound from Reading to the little Berkshire village.
009216 There were Sherlock Holmes, the hydraulic engineer, Inspector
009217 Bradstreet, of Scotland Yard, a plain-clothes man, and myself.
009218 Bradstreet had spread an ordnance map of the county out upon the
009219 seat and was busy with his compasses drawing a circle with Eyford
009220 for its centre.
009221 
009222 "There you are," said he. "That circle is drawn at a radius of
009223 ten miles from the village. The place we want must be somewhere
009224 near that line. You said ten miles, I think, sir."
009225 
009226 "It was an hour's good drive."
009227 
009228 "And you think that they brought you back all that way when you
009229 were unconscious?"
009230 
009231 "They must have done so. I have a confused memory, too, of having
009232 been lifted and conveyed somewhere."
009233 
009234 "What I cannot understand," said I, "is why they should have
009235 spared you when they found you lying fainting in the garden.
009236 Perhaps the villain was softened by the woman's entreaties."
009237 
009238 "I hardly think that likely. I never saw a more inexorable face
009239 in my life."
009240 
009241 "Oh, we shall soon clear up all that," said Bradstreet. "Well, I
009242 have drawn my circle, and I only wish I knew at what point upon
009243 it the folk that we are in search of are to be found."
009244 
009245 "I think I could lay my finger on it," said Holmes quietly.
009246 
009247 "Really, now!" cried the inspector, "you have formed your
009248 opinion! Come, now, we shall see who agrees with you. I say it is
009249 south, for the country is more deserted there."
009250 
009251 "And I say east," said my patient.
009252 
009253 "I am for west," remarked the plain-clothes man. "There are
009254 several quiet little villages up there."
009255 
009256 "And I am for north," said I, "because there are no hills there,
009257 and our friend says that he did not notice the carriage go up
009258 any."
009259 
009260 "Come," cried the inspector, laughing; "it's a very pretty
009261 diversity of opinion. We have boxed the compass among us. Who do
009262 you give your casting vote to?"
009263 
009264 "You are all wrong."
009265 
009266 "But we can't all be."
009267 
009268 "Oh, yes, you can. This is my point." He placed his finger in the
009269 centre of the circle. "This is where we shall find them."
009270 
009271 "But the twelve-mile drive?" gasped Hatherley.
009272 
009273 "Six out and six back. Nothing simpler. You say yourself that the
009274 horse was fresh and glossy when you got in. How could it be that
009275 if it had gone twelve miles over heavy roads?"
009276 
009277 "Indeed, it is a likely ruse enough," observed Bradstreet
009278 thoughtfully. "Of course there can be no doubt as to the nature
009279 of this gang."
009280 
009281 "None at all," said Holmes. "They are coiners on a large scale,
009282 and have used the machine to form the amalgam which has taken the
009283 place of silver."
009284 
009285 "We have known for some time that a clever gang was at work,"
009286 said the inspector. "They have been turning out half-crowns by
009287 the thousand. We even traced them as far as Reading, but could
009288 get no farther, for they had covered their traces in a way that
009289 showed that they were very old hands. But now, thanks to this
009290 lucky chance, I think that we have got them right enough."
009291 
009292 But the inspector was mistaken, for those criminals were not
009293 destined to fall into the hands of justice. As we rolled into
009294 Eyford Station we saw a gigantic column of smoke which streamed
009295 up from behind a small clump of trees in the neighbourhood and
009296 hung like an immense ostrich feather over the landscape.
009297 
009298 "A house on fire?" asked Bradstreet as the train steamed off
009299 again on its way.
009300 
009301 "Yes, sir!" said the station-master.
009302 
009303 "When did it break out?"
009304 
009305 "I hear that it was during the night, sir, but it has got worse,
009306 and the whole place is in a blaze."
009307 
009308 "Whose house is it?"
009309 
009310 "Dr. Becher's."
009311 
009312 "Tell me," broke in the engineer, "is Dr. Becher a German, very
009313 thin, with a long, sharp nose?"
009314 
009315 The station-master laughed heartily. "No, sir, Dr. Becher is an
009316 Englishman, and there isn't a man in the parish who has a
009317 better-lined waistcoat. But he has a gentleman staying with him,
009318 a patient, as I understand, who is a foreigner, and he looks as
009319 if a little good Berkshire beef would do him no harm."
009320 
009321 The station-master had not finished his speech before we were all
009322 hastening in the direction of the fire. The road topped a low
009323 hill, and there was a great widespread whitewashed building in
009324 front of us, spouting fire at every chink and window, while in
009325 the garden in front three fire-engines were vainly striving to
009326 keep the flames under.
009327 
009328 "That's it!" cried Hatherley, in intense excitement. "There is
009329 the gravel-drive, and there are the rose-bushes where I lay. That
009330 second window is the one that I jumped from."
009331 
009332 "Well, at least," said Holmes, "you have had your revenge upon
009333 them. There can be no question that it was your oil-lamp which,
009334 when it was crushed in the press, set fire to the wooden walls,
009335 though no doubt they were too excited in the chase after you to
009336 observe it at the time. Now keep your eyes open in this crowd for
009337 your friends of last night, though I very much fear that they are
009338 a good hundred miles off by now."
009339 
009340 And Holmes' fears came to be realised, for from that day to this
009341 no word has ever been heard either of the beautiful woman, the
009342 sinister German, or the morose Englishman. Early that morning a
009343 peasant had met a cart containing several people and some very
009344 bulky boxes driving rapidly in the direction of Reading, but
009345 there all traces of the fugitives disappeared, and even Holmes'
009346 ingenuity failed ever to discover the least clue as to their
009347 whereabouts.
009348 
009349 The firemen had been much perturbed at the strange arrangements
009350 which they had found within, and still more so by discovering a
009351 newly severed human thumb upon a window-sill of the second floor.
009352 About sunset, however, their efforts were at last successful, and
009353 they subdued the flames, but not before the roof had fallen in,
009354 and the whole place been reduced to such absolute ruin that, save
009355 some twisted cylinders and iron piping, not a trace remained of
009356 the machinery which had cost our unfortunate acquaintance so
009357 dearly. Large masses of nickel and of tin were discovered stored
009358 in an out-house, but no coins were to be found, which may have
009359 explained the presence of those bulky boxes which have been
009360 already referred to.
009361 
009362 How our hydraulic engineer had been conveyed from the garden to
009363 the spot where he recovered his senses might have remained
009364 forever a mystery were it not for the soft mould, which told us a
009365 very plain tale. He had evidently been carried down by two
009366 persons, one of whom had remarkably small feet and the other
009367 unusually large ones. On the whole, it was most probable that the
009368 silent Englishman, being less bold or less murderous than his
009369 companion, had assisted the woman to bear the unconscious man out
009370 of the way of danger.
009371 
009372 "Well," said our engineer ruefully as we took our seats to return
009373 once more to London, "it has been a pretty business for me! I
009374 have lost my thumb and I have lost a fifty-guinea fee, and what
009375 have I gained?"
009376 
009377 "Experience," said Holmes, laughing. "Indirectly it may be of
009378 value, you know; you have only to put it into words to gain the
009379 reputation of being excellent company for the remainder of your
009380 existence."
009381 
009382 
009383 
009384 X. THE ADVENTURE OF THE NOBLE BACHELOR
009385 
009386 The Lord St. Simon marriage, and its curious termination, have
009387 long ceased to be a subject of interest in those exalted circles
009388 in which the unfortunate bridegroom moves. Fresh scandals have
009389 eclipsed it, and their more piquant details have drawn the
009390 gossips away from this four-year-old drama. As I have reason to
009391 believe, however, that the full facts have never been revealed to
009392 the general public, and as my friend Sherlock Holmes had a
009393 considerable share in clearing the matter up, I feel that no
009394 memoir of him would be complete without some little sketch of
009395 this remarkable episode.
009396 
009397 It was a few weeks before my own marriage, during the days when I
009398 was still sharing rooms with Holmes in Baker Street, that he came
009399 home from an afternoon stroll to find a letter on the table
009400 waiting for him. I had remained indoors all day, for the weather
009401 had taken a sudden turn to rain, with high autumnal winds, and
009402 the Jezail bullet which I had brought back in one of my limbs as
009403 a relic of my Afghan campaign throbbed with dull persistence.
009404 With my body in one easy-chair and my legs upon another, I had
009405 surrounded myself with a cloud of newspapers until at last,
009406 saturated with the news of the day, I tossed them all aside and
009407 lay listless, watching the huge crest and monogram upon the
009408 envelope upon the table and wondering lazily who my friend's
009409 noble correspondent could be.
009410 
009411 "Here is a very fashionable epistle," I remarked as he entered.
009412 "Your morning letters, if I remember right, were from a
009413 fish-monger and a tide-waiter."
009414 
009415 "Yes, my correspondence has certainly the charm of variety," he
009416 answered, smiling, "and the humbler are usually the more
009417 interesting. This looks like one of those unwelcome social
009418 summonses which call upon a man either to be bored or to lie."
009419 
009420 He broke the seal and glanced over the contents.
009421 
009422 "Oh, come, it may prove to be something of interest, after all."
009423 
009424 "Not social, then?"
009425 
009426 "No, distinctly professional."
009427 
009428 "And from a noble client?"
009429 
009430 "One of the highest in England."
009431 
009432 "My dear fellow, I congratulate you."
009433 
009434 "I assure you, Watson, without affectation, that the status of my
009435 client is a matter of less moment to me than the interest of his
009436 case. It is just possible, however, that that also may not be
009437 wanting in this new investigation. You have been reading the
009438 papers diligently of late, have you not?"
009439 
009440 "It looks like it," said I ruefully, pointing to a huge bundle in
009441 the corner. "I have had nothing else to do."
009442 
009443 "It is fortunate, for you will perhaps be able to post me up. I
009444 read nothing except the criminal news and the agony column. The
009445 latter is always instructive. But if you have followed recent
009446 events so closely you must have read about Lord St. Simon and his
009447 wedding?"
009448 
009449 "Oh, yes, with the deepest interest."
009450 
009451 "That is well. The letter which I hold in my hand is from Lord
009452 St. Simon. I will read it to you, and in return you must turn
009453 over these papers and let me have whatever bears upon the matter.
009454 This is what he says:
009455 
009456 "'MY DEAR MR. SHERLOCK HOLMES:--Lord Backwater tells me that I
009457 may place implicit reliance upon your judgment and discretion. I
009458 have determined, therefore, to call upon you and to consult you
009459 in reference to the very painful event which has occurred in
009460 connection with my wedding. Mr. Lestrade, of Scotland Yard, is
009461 acting already in the matter, but he assures me that he sees no
009462 objection to your co-operation, and that he even thinks that
009463 it might be of some assistance. I will call at four o'clock in
009464 the afternoon, and, should you have any other engagement at that
009465 time, I hope that you will postpone it, as this matter is of
