009466 paramount importance. Yours faithfully, ST. SIMON.'
009467 
009468 "It is dated from Grosvenor Mansions, written with a quill pen,
009469 and the noble lord has had the misfortune to get a smear of ink
009470 upon the outer side of his right little finger," remarked Holmes
009471 as he folded up the epistle.
009472 
009473 "He says four o'clock. It is three now. He will be here in an
009474 hour."
009475 
009476 "Then I have just time, with your assistance, to get clear upon
009477 the subject. Turn over those papers and arrange the extracts in
009478 their order of time, while I take a glance as to who our client
009479 is." He picked a red-covered volume from a line of books of
009480 reference beside the mantelpiece. "Here he is," said he, sitting
009481 down and flattening it out upon his knee. "'Lord Robert Walsingham
009482 de Vere St. Simon, second son of the Duke of Balmoral.' Hum! 'Arms:
009483 Azure, three caltrops in chief over a fess sable. Born in 1846.'
009484 He's forty-one years of age, which is mature for marriage. Was
009485 Under-Secretary for the colonies in a late administration. The
009486 Duke, his father, was at one time Secretary for Foreign Affairs.
009487 They inherit Plantagenet blood by direct descent, and Tudor on
009488 the distaff side. Ha! Well, there is nothing very instructive in
009489 all this. I think that I must turn to you Watson, for something
009490 more solid."
009491 
009492 "I have very little difficulty in finding what I want," said I,
009493 "for the facts are quite recent, and the matter struck me as
009494 remarkable. I feared to refer them to you, however, as I knew
009495 that you had an inquiry on hand and that you disliked the
009496 intrusion of other matters."
009497 
009498 "Oh, you mean the little problem of the Grosvenor Square
009499 furniture van. That is quite cleared up now--though, indeed, it
009500 was obvious from the first. Pray give me the results of your
009501 newspaper selections."
009502 
009503 "Here is the first notice which I can find. It is in the personal
009504 column of the Morning Post, and dates, as you see, some weeks
009505 back: 'A marriage has been arranged,' it says, 'and will, if
009506 rumour is correct, very shortly take place, between Lord Robert
009507 St. Simon, second son of the Duke of Balmoral, and Miss Hatty
009508 Doran, the only daughter of Aloysius Doran. Esq., of San
009509 Francisco, Cal., U.S.A.' That is all."
009510 
009511 "Terse and to the point," remarked Holmes, stretching his long,
009512 thin legs towards the fire.
009513 
009514 "There was a paragraph amplifying this in one of the society
009515 papers of the same week. Ah, here it is: 'There will soon be a
009516 call for protection in the marriage market, for the present
009517 free-trade principle appears to tell heavily against our home
009518 product. One by one the management of the noble houses of Great
009519 Britain is passing into the hands of our fair cousins from across
009520 the Atlantic. An important addition has been made during the last
009521 week to the list of the prizes which have been borne away by
009522 these charming invaders. Lord St. Simon, who has shown himself
009523 for over twenty years proof against the little god's arrows, has
009524 now definitely announced his approaching marriage with Miss Hatty
009525 Doran, the fascinating daughter of a California millionaire. Miss
009526 Doran, whose graceful figure and striking face attracted much
009527 attention at the Westbury House festivities, is an only child,
009528 and it is currently reported that her dowry will run to
009529 considerably over the six figures, with expectancies for the
009530 future. As it is an open secret that the Duke of Balmoral has
009531 been compelled to sell his pictures within the last few years,
009532 and as Lord St. Simon has no property of his own save the small
009533 estate of Birchmoor, it is obvious that the Californian heiress
009534 is not the only gainer by an alliance which will enable her to
009535 make the easy and common transition from a Republican lady to a
009536 British peeress.'"
009537 
009538 "Anything else?" asked Holmes, yawning.
009539 
009540 "Oh, yes; plenty. Then there is another note in the Morning Post
009541 to say that the marriage would be an absolutely quiet one, that it
009542 would be at St. George's, Hanover Square, that only half a dozen
009543 intimate friends would be invited, and that the party would
009544 return to the furnished house at Lancaster Gate which has been
009545 taken by Mr. Aloysius Doran. Two days later--that is, on
009546 Wednesday last--there is a curt announcement that the wedding had
009547 taken place, and that the honeymoon would be passed at Lord
009548 Backwater's place, near Petersfield. Those are all the notices
009549 which appeared before the disappearance of the bride."
009550 
009551 "Before the what?" asked Holmes with a start.
009552 
009553 "The vanishing of the lady."
009554 
009555 "When did she vanish, then?"
009556 
009557 "At the wedding breakfast."
009558 
009559 "Indeed. This is more interesting than it promised to be; quite
009560 dramatic, in fact."
009561 
009562 "Yes; it struck me as being a little out of the common."
009563 
009564 "They often vanish before the ceremony, and occasionally during

009567 
009568 "I warn you that they are very incomplete."
009569 
009570 "Perhaps we may make them less so."

009572 "Such as they are, they are set forth in a single article of a

009574 headed, 'Singular Occurrence at a Fashionable Wedding':
009575 
009576 "'The family of Lord Robert St. Simon has been thrown into the
009577 greatest consternation by the strange and painful episodes which
009578 have taken place in connection with his wedding. The ceremony, as
009579 shortly announced in the papers of yesterday, occurred on the
009580 previous morning; but it is only now that it has been possible to
009581 confirm the strange rumours which have been so persistently
009582 floating about. In spite of the attempts of the friends to hush
009583 the matter up, so much public attention has now been drawn to it
009584 that no good purpose can be served by affecting to disregard what
009585 is a common subject for conversation.
009586 
009587 "'The ceremony, which was performed at St. George's, Hanover
009588 Square, was a very quiet one, no one being present save the
009589 father of the bride, Mr. Aloysius Doran, the Duchess of Balmoral,
009590 Lord Backwater, Lord Eustace and Lady Clara St. Simon (the
009591 younger brother and sister of the bridegroom), and Lady Alicia
009592 Whittington. The whole party proceeded afterwards to the house of
009593 Mr. Aloysius Doran, at Lancaster Gate, where breakfast had been
009594 prepared. It appears that some little trouble was caused by a
009595 woman, whose name has not been ascertained, who endeavoured to
009596 force her way into the house after the bridal party, alleging
009597 that she had some claim upon Lord St. Simon. It was only after a
009598 painful and prolonged scene that she was ejected by the butler
009599 and the footman. The bride, who had fortunately entered the house
009600 before this unpleasant interruption, had sat down to breakfast
009601 with the rest, when she complained of a sudden indisposition and
009602 retired to her room. Her prolonged absence having caused some
009603 comment, her father followed her, but learned from her maid that
009604 she had only come up to her chamber for an instant, caught up an
009605 ulster and bonnet, and hurried down to the passage. One of the
009606 footmen declared that he had seen a lady leave the house thus
009607 apparelled, but had refused to credit that it was his mistress,
009608 believing her to be with the company. On ascertaining that his
009609 daughter had disappeared, Mr. Aloysius Doran, in conjunction with
009610 the bridegroom, instantly put themselves in communication with
009611 the police, and very energetic inquiries are being made, which
009612 will probably result in a speedy clearing up of this very
009613 singular business. Up to a late hour last night, however, nothing
009614 had transpired as to the whereabouts of the missing lady. There
009615 are rumours of foul play in the matter, and it is said that the
009616 police have caused the arrest of the woman who had caused the
009617 original disturbance, in the belief that, from jealousy or some
009618 other motive, she may have been concerned in the strange
009619 disappearance of the bride.'"

009621 "And is that all?"
009622 
009623 "Only one little item in another of the morning papers, but it is
009624 a suggestive one."
009625 
009626 "And it is--"
009627

009630 danseuse at the Allegro, and that she has known the bridegroom
009631 for some years. There are no further particulars, and the whole
009632 case is in your hands now--so far as it has been set forth in the

009641 
009642 "Lord Robert St. Simon," announced our page-boy, throwing open

009661 matter over."

009737 with a strong nature, wild and free, unfettered by any sort of

009971 The official detective was attired in a pea-jacket and cravat,

010000 
010001 "Why? What do you mean?"
010002 
010003 "Because you have just as good a chance of finding this lady in
010004 the one as in the other."
010005 
010006 Lestrade shot an angry glance at my companion. "I suppose you

010008

010026

010029 that if the clothes were there the body would not be far off."
010030 
010031 "By the same brilliant reasoning, every man's body is to be found
010032 in the neighbourhood of his wardrobe. And pray what did you hope
010033 to arrive at through this?"
010034 
010035 "At some evidence implicating Flora Millar in the disappearance."
010036

010038

010043

010045 
010046 "In the dress is a pocket. In the pocket is a card-case. In the

010049 see me when all is ready. Come at once. F.H.M.' Now my theory all
010050 along has been that Lady St. Simon was decoyed away by Flora
010051 Millar, and that she, with confederates, no doubt, was
010052 responsible for her disappearance. Here, signed with her
010053 initials, is the very note which was no doubt quietly slipped
010054 into her hand at the door and which lured her within their
010055 reach."
010056

010061 said he.
010062 
010063 "Ha! you find it so?"
010064 
010065 "Extremely so. I congratulate you warmly."
010066 
010067 Lestrade rose in his triumph and bent his head to look. "Why," he

010069 
010070 "On the contrary, this is the right side."
010071 
010072 "The right side? You're mad! Here is the note written in pencil

010074 
010075 "And over here is what appears to be the fragment of a hotel

010077 
010078 "There's nothing in it. I looked at it before," said Lestrade.
010079 "'Oct. 4th, rooms 8s., breakfast 2s. 6d., cocktail 1s., lunch 2s.
010080 6d., glass sherry, 8d.' I see nothing in that."
010081 
010082 "Very likely not. It is most important, all the same. As to the
010083 note, it is important also, or at least the initials are, so I

010085 
010086 "I've wasted time enough," said Lestrade, rising. "I believe in

010091 
010092 "Just one hint to you, Lestrade," drawled Holmes before his rival
010093 vanished; "I will tell you the true solution of the matter. Lady
010094 St. Simon is a myth. There is not, and there never has been, any
010095 such person."
010096 
010097 Lestrade looked sadly at my companion. Then he turned to me,
010098 tapped his forehead three times, shook his head solemnly, and
010099 hurried away.
010100 
010101 He had hardly shut the door behind him when Holmes rose to put on
010102 his overcoat. "There is something in what the fellow says about
010103 outdoor work," he remarked, "so I think, Watson, that I must
010104 leave you to your papers for a little."
010105 
010106 It was after five o'clock when Sherlock Holmes left me, but I had
010107 no time to be lonely, for within an hour there arrived a
010108 confectioner's man with a very large flat box. This he unpacked
010109 with the help of a youth whom he had brought with him, and
010110 presently, to my very great astonishment, a quite epicurean
010111 little cold supper began to be laid out upon our humble
010112 lodging-house mahogany. There were a couple of brace of cold
010113 woodcock, a pheasant, a pt de foie gras pie with a group of
010114 ancient and cobwebby bottles. Having laid out all these luxuries,
010115 my two visitors vanished away, like the genii of the Arabian
010116 Nights, with no explanation save that the things had been paid
010117 for and were ordered to this address.
010118 
010119 Just before nine o'clock Sherlock Holmes stepped briskly into the
010120 room. His features were gravely set, but there was a light in his
010121 eye which made me think that he had not been disappointed in his
010122 conclusions.
010123 
010124 "They have laid the supper, then," he said, rubbing his hands.
010125 
010126 "You seem to expect company. They have laid for five."
010127 
010128 "Yes, I fancy we may have some company dropping in," said he. "I
010129 am surprised that Lord St. Simon has not already arrived. Ha! I
010130 fancy that I hear his step now upon the stairs."
010131 
010132 It was indeed our visitor of the afternoon who came bustling in,
010133 dangling his glasses more vigorously than ever, and with a very
010134 perturbed expression upon his aristocratic features.
010135 
010136 "My messenger reached you, then?" asked Holmes.
010137 
010138 "Yes, and I confess that the contents startled me beyond measure.
010139 Have you good authority for what you say?"
010140 
010141 "The best possible."
010142 
010143 Lord St. Simon sank into a chair and passed his hand over his
010144 forehead.
010145 
010146 "What will the Duke say," he murmured, "when he hears that one of
010147 the family has been subjected to such humiliation?"
010148 
010149 "It is the purest accident. I cannot allow that there is any
010150 humiliation."
010151 
010152 "Ah, you look on these things from another standpoint."
010153 
010154 "I fail to see that anyone is to blame. I can hardly see how the
010155 lady could have acted otherwise, though her abrupt method of
010156 doing it was undoubtedly to be regretted. Having no mother, she
010157 had no one to advise her at such a crisis."
010158 
010159 "It was a slight, sir, a public slight," said Lord St. Simon,
010160 tapping his fingers upon the table.
010161 
010162 "You must make allowance for this poor girl, placed in so
010163 unprecedented a position."
010164 
010165 "I will make no allowance. I am very angry indeed, and I have
010166 been shamefully used."
010167 
010168 "I think that I heard a ring," said Holmes. "Yes, there are steps
010169 on the landing. If I cannot persuade you to take a lenient view
010170 of the matter, Lord St. Simon, I have brought an advocate here
010171 who may be more successful." He opened the door and ushered in a
010172 lady and gentleman. "Lord St. Simon," said he "allow me to
010173 introduce you to Mr. and Mrs. Francis Hay Moulton. The lady, I
010174 think, you have already met."
010175 
010176 At the sight of these newcomers our client had sprung from his
010177 seat and stood very erect, with his eyes cast down and his hand
010178 thrust into the breast of his frock-coat, a picture of offended
010179 dignity. The lady had taken a quick step forward and had held out
010180 her hand to him, but he still refused to raise his eyes. It was
010181 as well for his resolution, perhaps, for her pleading face was
010182 one which it was hard to resist.
010183 
010184 "You're angry, Robert," said she. "Well, I guess you have every
010185 cause to be."
010186 
010187 "Pray make no apology to me," said Lord St. Simon bitterly.
010188 
010189 "Oh, yes, I know that I have treated you real bad and that I
010190 should have spoken to you before I went; but I was kind of
010191 rattled, and from the time when I saw Frank here again I just
010192 didn't know what I was doing or saying. I only wonder I didn't
010193 fall down and do a faint right there before the altar."
010194 
010195 "Perhaps, Mrs. Moulton, you would like my friend and me to leave
010196 the room while you explain this matter?"
010197 
010198 "If I may give an opinion," remarked the strange gentleman,
010199 "we've had just a little too much secrecy over this business
010200 already. For my part, I should like all Europe and America to
010201 hear the rights of it." He was a small, wiry, sunburnt man,
010202 clean-shaven, with a sharp face and alert manner.
010203 
010204 "Then I'll tell our story right away," said the lady. "Frank here
010205 and I met in '84, in McQuire's camp, near the Rockies, where pa
010206 was working a claim. We were engaged to each other, Frank and I;
010207 but then one day father struck a rich pocket and made a pile,
010208 while poor Frank here had a claim that petered out and came to
010209 nothing. The richer pa grew the poorer was Frank; so at last pa
010210 wouldn't hear of our engagement lasting any longer, and he took
010211 me away to 'Frisco. Frank wouldn't throw up his hand, though; so
010212 he followed me there, and he saw me without pa knowing anything
010213 about it. It would only have made him mad to know, so we just
010214 fixed it all up for ourselves. Frank said that he would go and
010215 make his pile, too, and never come back to claim me until he had
010216 as much as pa. So then I promised to wait for him to the end of
010217 time and pledged myself not to marry anyone else while he lived.
010218 'Why shouldn't we be married right away, then,' said he, 'and
010219 then I will feel sure of you; and I won't claim to be your
010220 husband until I come back?' Well, we talked it over, and he had
010221 fixed it all up so nicely, with a clergyman all ready in waiting,
010222 that we just did it right there; and then Frank went off to seek
010223 his fortune, and I went back to pa.
010224 
010225 "The next I heard of Frank was that he was in Montana, and then
010226 he went prospecting in Arizona, and then I heard of him from New
010227 Mexico. After that came a long newspaper story about how a
010228 miners' camp had been attacked by Apache Indians, and there was
010229 my Frank's name among the killed. I fainted dead away, and I was
010230 very sick for months after. Pa thought I had a decline and took
010231 me to half the doctors in 'Frisco. Not a word of news came for a
010232 year and more, so that I never doubted that Frank was really
010233 dead. Then Lord St. Simon came to 'Frisco, and we came to London,
010234 and a marriage was arranged, and pa was very pleased, but I felt
010235 all the time that no man on this earth would ever take the place
010236 in my heart that had been given to my poor Frank.
010237 
010238 "Still, if I had married Lord St. Simon, of course I'd have done
010239 my duty by him. We can't command our love, but we can our
010240 actions. I went to the altar with him with the intention to make
010241 him just as good a wife as it was in me to be. But you may
010242 imagine what I felt when, just as I came to the altar rails, I
010243 glanced back and saw Frank standing and looking at me out of the
010244 first pew. I thought it was his ghost at first; but when I looked
010245 again there he was still, with a kind of question in his eyes, as
010246 if to ask me whether I were glad or sorry to see him. I wonder I
010247 didn't drop. I know that everything was turning round, and the
010248 words of the clergyman were just like the buzz of a bee in my
010249 ear. I didn't know what to do. Should I stop the service and make
010250 a scene in the church? I glanced at him again, and he seemed to
010251 know what I was thinking, for he raised his finger to his lips to
010252 tell me to be still. Then I saw him scribble on a piece of paper,
010253 and I knew that he was writing me a note. As I passed his pew on
010254 the way out I dropped my bouquet over to him, and he slipped the
010255 note into my hand when he returned me the flowers. It was only a
010256 line asking me to join him when he made the sign to me to do so.
010257 Of course I never doubted for a moment that my first duty was now
010258 to him, and I determined to do just whatever he might direct.
010259 
010260 "When I got back I told my maid, who had known him in California,
010261 and had always been his friend. I ordered her to say nothing, but
010262 to get a few things packed and my ulster ready. I know I ought to
010263 have spoken to Lord St. Simon, but it was dreadful hard before
010264 his mother and all those great people. I just made up my mind to
010265 run away and explain afterwards. I hadn't been at the table ten
010266 minutes before I saw Frank out of the window at the other side of
010267 the road. He beckoned to me and then began walking into the Park.
010268 I slipped out, put on my things, and followed him. Some woman
010269 came talking something or other about Lord St. Simon to
010270 me--seemed to me from the little I heard as if he had a little
010271 secret of his own before marriage also--but I managed to get away
010272 from her and soon overtook Frank. We got into a cab together, and
010273 away we drove to some lodgings he had taken in Gordon Square, and
010274 that was my true wedding after all those years of waiting. Frank
010275 had been a prisoner among the Apaches, had escaped, came on to
010276 'Frisco, found that I had given him up for dead and had gone to
010277 England, followed me there, and had come upon me at last on the
010278 very morning of my second wedding."
010279 
010280 "I saw it in a paper," explained the American. "It gave the name
010281 and the church but not where the lady lived."
010282 
010283 "Then we had a talk as to what we should do, and Frank was all
010284 for openness, but I was so ashamed of it all that I felt as if I
010285 should like to vanish away and never see any of them again--just
010286 sending a line to pa, perhaps, to show him that I was alive. It
010287 was awful to me to think of all those lords and ladies sitting
010288 round that breakfast-table and waiting for me to come back. So
010289 Frank took my wedding-clothes and things and made a bundle of
010290 them, so that I should not be traced, and dropped them away
010291 somewhere where no one could find them. It is likely that we
010292 should have gone on to Paris to-morrow, only that this good
010293 gentleman, Mr. Holmes, came round to us this evening, though how
010294 he found us is more than I can think, and he showed us very
010295 clearly and kindly that I was wrong and that Frank was right, and
010296 that we should be putting ourselves in the wrong if we were so
010297 secret. Then he offered to give us a chance of talking to Lord
010298 St. Simon alone, and so we came right away round to his rooms at
010299 once. Now, Robert, you have heard it all, and I am very sorry if
010300 I have given you pain, and I hope that you do not think very
010301 meanly of me."
010302 
010303 Lord St. Simon had by no means relaxed his rigid attitude, but
010304 had listened with a frowning brow and a compressed lip to this
010305 long narrative.
010306 
010307 "Excuse me," he said, "but it is not my custom to discuss my most
010308 intimate personal affairs in this public manner."
010309 
010310 "Then you won't forgive me? You won't shake hands before I go?"
010311 
010312 "Oh, certainly, if it would give you any pleasure." He put out
010313 his hand and coldly grasped that which she extended to him.
010314 
010315 "I had hoped," suggested Holmes, "that you would have joined us
010316 in a friendly supper."
010317 
010318 "I think that there you ask a little too much," responded his
010319 Lordship. "I may be forced to acquiesce in these recent
010320 developments, but I can hardly be expected to make merry over
010321 them. I think that with your permission I will now wish you all a
010322 very good-night." He included us all in a sweeping bow and
010323 stalked out of the room.
010324 
010325 "Then I trust that you at least will honour me with your
010326 company," said Sherlock Holmes. "It is always a joy to meet an
010327 American, Mr. Moulton, for I am one of those who believe that the
010328 folly of a monarch and the blundering of a minister in far-gone
010329 years will not prevent our children from being some day citizens
010330 of the same world-wide country under a flag which shall be a
010331 quartering of the Union Jack with the Stars and Stripes."
010332 
010333 "The case has been an interesting one," remarked Holmes when our
010334 visitors had left us, "because it serves to show very clearly how
010335 simple the explanation may be of an affair which at first sight
010336 seems to be almost inexplicable. Nothing could be more natural
010337 than the sequence of events as narrated by this lady, and nothing
010338 stranger than the result when viewed, for instance, by Mr.
010339 Lestrade of Scotland Yard."
010340 
010341 "You were not yourself at fault at all, then?"
010342 
010343 "From the first, two facts were very obvious to me, the one that
010344 the lady had been quite willing to undergo the wedding ceremony,
010345 the other that she had repented of it within a few minutes of
010346 returning home. Obviously something had occurred during the
010347 morning, then, to cause her to change her mind. What could that
010348 something be? She could not have spoken to anyone when she was
010349 out, for she had been in the company of the bridegroom. Had she
010350 seen someone, then? If she had, it must be someone from America
010351 because she had spent so short a time in this country that she
010352 could hardly have allowed anyone to acquire so deep an influence
010353 over her that the mere sight of him would induce her to change
010354 her plans so completely. You see we have already arrived, by a
010355 process of exclusion, at the idea that she might have seen an
010356 American. Then who could this American be, and why should he
010357 possess so much influence over her? It might be a lover; it might
010358 be a husband. Her young womanhood had, I knew, been spent in
010359 rough scenes and under strange conditions. So far I had got
010360 before I ever heard Lord St. Simon's narrative. When he told us
010361 of a man in a pew, of the change in the bride's manner, of so
010362 transparent a device for obtaining a note as the dropping of a
010363 bouquet, of her resort to her confidential maid, and of her very
010364 significant allusion to claim-jumping--which in miners' parlance
010365 means taking possession of that which another person has a prior
010366 claim to--the whole situation became absolutely clear. She had
010367 gone off with a man, and the man was either a lover or was a
010368 previous husband--the chances being in favour of the latter."
010369 
010370 "And how in the world did you find them?"
010371 
010372 "It might have been difficult, but friend Lestrade held
010373 information in his hands the value of which he did not himself
010374 know. The initials were, of course, of the highest importance,
010375 but more valuable still was it to know that within a week he had
010376 settled his bill at one of the most select London hotels."
010377 
010378 "How did you deduce the select?"
010379 
010380 "By the select prices. Eight shillings for a bed and eightpence
010381 for a glass of sherry pointed to one of the most expensive
010382 hotels. There are not many in London which charge at that rate.
010383 In the second one which I visited in Northumberland Avenue, I
010384 learned by an inspection of the book that Francis H. Moulton, an
010385 American gentleman, had left only the day before, and on looking
010386 over the entries against him, I came upon the very items which I
010387 had seen in the duplicate bill. His letters were to be forwarded
010388 to 226 Gordon Square; so thither I travelled, and being fortunate
010389 enough to find the loving couple at home, I ventured to give them
010390 some paternal advice and to point out to them that it would be
010391 better in every way that they should make their position a little
010392 clearer both to the general public and to Lord St. Simon in
010393 particular. I invited them to meet him here, and, as you see, I
010394 made him keep the appointment."
010395 
010396 "But with no very good result," I remarked. "His conduct was
010397 certainly not very gracious."
010398 
010399 "Ah, Watson," said Holmes, smiling, "perhaps you would not be
010400 very gracious either, if, after all the trouble of wooing and
010401 wedding, you found yourself deprived in an instant of wife and of
010402 fortune. I think that we may judge Lord St. Simon very mercifully
010403 and thank our stars that we are never likely to find ourselves in
010404 the same position. Draw your chair up and hand me my violin, for
010405 the only problem we have still to solve is how to while away
010406 these bleak autumnal evenings."
010407 
010408 
010409 
010410 XI. THE ADVENTURE OF THE BERYL CORONET
010411 
010412 "Holmes," said I as I stood one morning in our bow-window looking
010413 down the street, "here is a madman coming along. It seems rather
010414 sad that his relatives should allow him to come out alone."
010415 
010416 My friend rose lazily from his armchair and stood with his hands
010417 in the pockets of his dressing-gown, looking over my shoulder. It
010418 was a bright, crisp February morning, and the snow of the day
010419 before still lay deep upon the ground, shimmering brightly in the
010420 wintry sun. Down the centre of Baker Street it had been ploughed
010421 into a brown crumbly band by the traffic, but at either side and
010422 on the heaped-up edges of the foot-paths it still lay as white as
010423 when it fell. The grey pavement had been cleaned and scraped, but
010424 was still dangerously slippery, so that there were fewer
010425 passengers than usual. Indeed, from the direction of the
010426 Metropolitan Station no one was coming save the single gentleman
010427 whose eccentric conduct had drawn my attention.
010428 
010429 He was a man of about fifty, tall, portly, and imposing, with a
010430 massive, strongly marked face and a commanding figure. He was
010431 dressed in a sombre yet rich style, in black frock-coat, shining
010432 hat, neat brown gaiters, and well-cut pearl-grey trousers. Yet
010433 his actions were in absurd contrast to the dignity of his dress
010434 and features, for he was running hard, with occasional little
010435 springs, such as a weary man gives who is little accustomed to
010436 set any tax upon his legs. As he ran he jerked his hands up and
010437 down, waggled his head, and writhed his face into the most
010438 extraordinary contortions.
010439 
010440 "What on earth can be the matter with him?" I asked. "He is
010441 looking up at the numbers of the houses."
010442 
010443 "I believe that he is coming here," said Holmes, rubbing his
010444 hands.
010445 
010446 "Here?"
010447 
010448 "Yes; I rather think he is coming to consult me professionally. I
010449 think that I recognise the symptoms. Ha! did I not tell you?" As
010450 he spoke, the man, puffing and blowing, rushed at our door and
010451 pulled at our bell until the whole house resounded with the
010452 clanging.
010453 
010454 A few moments later he was in our room, still puffing, still
010455 gesticulating, but with so fixed a look of grief and despair in
010456 his eyes that our smiles were turned in an instant to horror and
010457 pity. For a while he could not get his words out, but swayed his
010458 body and plucked at his hair like one who has been driven to the
010459 extreme limits of his reason. Then, suddenly springing to his
010460 feet, he beat his head against the wall with such force that we
010461 both rushed upon him and tore him away to the centre of the room.
010462 Sherlock Holmes pushed him down into the easy-chair and, sitting
010463 beside him, patted his hand and chatted with him in the easy,
010464 soothing tones which he knew so well how to employ.
010465 
010466 "You have come to me to tell your story, have you not?" said he.
010467 "You are fatigued with your haste. Pray wait until you have
010468 recovered yourself, and then I shall be most happy to look into
010469 any little problem which you may submit to me."
010470 
010471 The man sat for a minute or more with a heaving chest, fighting
010472 against his emotion. Then he passed his handkerchief over his
010473 brow, set his lips tight, and turned his face towards us.
010474 
010475 "No doubt you think me mad?" said he.
010476 
010477 "I see that you have had some great trouble," responded Holmes.
010478 
010479 "God knows I have!--a trouble which is enough to unseat my
010480 reason, so sudden and so terrible is it. Public disgrace I might
010481 have faced, although I am a man whose character has never yet
010482 borne a stain. Private affliction also is the lot of every man;
010483 but the two coming together, and in so frightful a form, have
010484 been enough to shake my very soul. Besides, it is not I alone.
010485 The very noblest in the land may suffer unless some way be found
010486 out of this horrible affair."
010487 
010488 "Pray compose yourself, sir," said Holmes, "and let me have a
010489 clear account of who you are and what it is that has befallen
010490 you."
010491 
010492 "My name," answered our visitor, "is probably familiar to your
010493 ears. I am Alexander Holder, of the banking firm of Holder &
010494 Stevenson, of Threadneedle Street."
010495 
010496 The name was indeed well known to us as belonging to the senior
010497 partner in the second largest private banking concern in the City
010498 of London. What could have happened, then, to bring one of the
010499 foremost citizens of London to this most pitiable pass? We
010500 waited, all curiosity, until with another effort he braced
010501 himself to tell his story.
010502 
010503 "I feel that time is of value," said he; "that is why I hastened
010504 here when the police inspector suggested that I should secure
010505 your co-operation. I came to Baker Street by the Underground and
010506 hurried from there on foot, for the cabs go slowly through this
010507 snow. That is why I was so out of breath, for I am a man who
010508 takes very little exercise. I feel better now, and I will put the
010509 facts before you as shortly and yet as clearly as I can.
010510 
010511 "It is, of course, well known to you that in a successful banking
010512 business as much depends upon our being able to find remunerative
010513 investments for our funds as upon our increasing our connection
010514 and the number of our depositors. One of our most lucrative means
010515 of laying out money is in the shape of loans, where the security
010516 is unimpeachable. We have done a good deal in this direction
010517 during the last few years, and there are many noble families to
010518 whom we have advanced large sums upon the security of their
010519 pictures, libraries, or plate.
010520 
010521 "Yesterday morning I was seated in my office at the bank when a
010522 card was brought in to me by one of the clerks. I started when I
010523 saw the name, for it was that of none other than--well, perhaps
010524 even to you I had better say no more than that it was a name
010525 which is a household word all over the earth--one of the highest,
010526 noblest, most exalted names in England. I was overwhelmed by the
010527 honour and attempted, when he entered, to say so, but he plunged
010528 at once into business with the air of a man who wishes to hurry
010529 quickly through a disagreeable task.
010530 
010531 "'Mr. Holder,' said he, 'I have been informed that you are in the
010532 habit of advancing money.'
010533 
010534 "'The firm does so when the security is good.' I answered.
010535 
010536 "'It is absolutely essential to me,' said he, 'that I should have
010537 50,000 pounds at once. I could, of course, borrow so trifling a
010538 sum ten times over from my friends, but I much prefer to make it
010539 a matter of business and to carry out that business myself. In my
010540 position you can readily understand that it is unwise to place
010541 one's self under obligations.'
010542 
010543 "'For how long, may I ask, do you want this sum?' I asked.
010544 
010545 "'Next Monday I have a large sum due to me, and I shall then most
010546 certainly repay what you advance, with whatever interest you
010547 think it right to charge. But it is very essential to me that the
010548 money should be paid at once.'
010549 
010550 "'I should be happy to advance it without further parley from my
010551 own private purse,' said I, 'were it not that the strain would be
010552 rather more than it could bear. If, on the other hand, I am to do
010553 it in the name of the firm, then in justice to my partner I must
010554 insist that, even in your case, every businesslike precaution
010555 should be taken.'
010556 
010557 "'I should much prefer to have it so,' said he, raising up a
010558 square, black morocco case which he had laid beside his chair.
010559 'You have doubtless heard of the Beryl Coronet?'
010560 
010561 "'One of the most precious public possessions of the empire,'
010562 said I.
010563 
010564 "'Precisely.' He opened the case, and there, imbedded in soft,
010565 flesh-coloured velvet, lay the magnificent piece of jewellery
010566 which he had named. 'There are thirty-nine enormous beryls,' said
010567 he, 'and the price of the gold chasing is incalculable. The
010568 lowest estimate would put the worth of the coronet at double the
010569 sum which I have asked. I am prepared to leave it with you as my
010570 security.'
010571 
010572 "I took the precious case into my hands and looked in some
010573 perplexity from it to my illustrious client.
010574 
010575 "'You doubt its value?' he asked.
010576 
010577 "'Not at all. I only doubt--'
010578 
010579 "'The propriety of my leaving it. You may set your mind at rest
010580 about that. I should not dream of doing so were it not absolutely
010581 certain that I should be able in four days to reclaim it. It is a
010582 pure matter of form. Is the security sufficient?'
010583 
010584 "'Ample.'
010585 
010586 "'You understand, Mr. Holder, that I am giving you a strong proof
010587 of the confidence which I have in you, founded upon all that I
010588 have heard of you. I rely upon you not only to be discreet and to
010589 refrain from all gossip upon the matter but, above all, to
010590 preserve this coronet with every possible precaution because I
010591 need not say that a great public scandal would be caused if any
010592 harm were to befall it. Any injury to it would be almost as
010593 serious as its complete loss, for there are no beryls in the
010594 world to match these, and it would be impossible to replace them.
010595 I leave it with you, however, with every confidence, and I shall
010596 call for it in person on Monday morning.'
010597 
010598 "Seeing that my client was anxious to leave, I said no more but,
010599 calling for my cashier, I ordered him to pay over fifty 1000
010600 pound notes. When I was alone once more, however, with the
010601 precious case lying upon the table in front of me, I could not
010602 but think with some misgivings of the immense responsibility
010603 which it entailed upon me. There could be no doubt that, as it
010604 was a national possession, a horrible scandal would ensue if any
010605 misfortune should occur to it. I already regretted having ever
010606 consented to take charge of it. However, it was too late to alter
010607 the matter now, so I locked it up in my private safe and turned
010608 once more to my work.
010609 
010610 "When evening came I felt that it would be an imprudence to leave
010611 so precious a thing in the office behind me. Bankers' safes had
010612 been forced before now, and why should not mine be? If so, how
010613 terrible would be the position in which I should find myself! I
010614 determined, therefore, that for the next few days I would always
010615 carry the case backward and forward with me, so that it might
010616 never be really out of my reach. With this intention, I called a
010617 cab and drove out to my house at Streatham, carrying the jewel
010618 with me. I did not breathe freely until I had taken it upstairs
010619 and locked it in the bureau of my dressing-room.
010620 
010621 "And now a word as to my household, Mr. Holmes, for I wish you to
010622 thoroughly understand the situation. My groom and my page sleep
010623 out of the house, and may be set aside altogether. I have three
010624 maid-servants who have been with me a number of years and whose
010625 absolute reliability is quite above suspicion. Another, Lucy
010626 Parr, the second waiting-maid, has only been in my service a few
010627 months. She came with an excellent character, however, and has
010628 always given me satisfaction. She is a very pretty girl and has
010629 attracted admirers who have occasionally hung about the place.
010630 That is the only drawback which we have found to her, but we
010631 believe her to be a thoroughly good girl in every way.
010632 
010633 "So much for the servants. My family itself is so small that it
010634 will not take me long to describe it. I am a widower and have an
010635 only son, Arthur. He has been a disappointment to me, Mr.
010636 Holmes--a grievous disappointment. I have no doubt that I am
010637 myself to blame. People tell me that I have spoiled him. Very
010638 likely I have. When my dear wife died I felt that he was all I
010639 had to love. I could not bear to see the smile fade even for a
010640 moment from his face. I have never denied him a wish. Perhaps it
010641 would have been better for both of us had I been sterner, but I
010642 meant it for the best.
010643 
010644 "It was naturally my intention that he should succeed me in my
010645 business, but he was not of a business turn. He was wild,
010646 wayward, and, to speak the truth, I could not trust him in the
010647 handling of large sums of money. When he was young he became a
010648 member of an aristocratic club, and there, having charming
010649 manners, he was soon the intimate of a number of men with long
010650 purses and expensive habits. He learned to play heavily at cards
010651 and to squander money on the turf, until he had again and again
010652 to come to me and implore me to give him an advance upon his
010653 allowance, that he might settle his debts of honour. He tried
010654 more than once to break away from the dangerous company which he
010655 was keeping, but each time the influence of his friend, Sir
010656 George Burnwell, was enough to draw him back again.
010657 
010658 "And, indeed, I could not wonder that such a man as Sir George
010659 Burnwell should gain an influence over him, for he has frequently
010660 brought him to my house, and I have found myself that I could
010661 hardly resist the fascination of his manner. He is older than
010662 Arthur, a man of the world to his finger-tips, one who had been
010663 everywhere, seen everything, a brilliant talker, and a man of
010664 great personal beauty. Yet when I think of him in cold blood, far
010665 away from the glamour of his presence, I am convinced from his
010666 cynical speech and the look which I have caught in his eyes that
010667 he is one who should be deeply distrusted. So I think, and so,
010668 too, thinks my little Mary, who has a woman's quick insight into
010669 character.
010670 
010671 "And now there is only she to be described. She is my niece; but
010672 when my brother died five years ago and left her alone in the
010673 world I adopted her, and have looked upon her ever since as my
010674 daughter. She is a sunbeam in my house--sweet, loving, beautiful,
010675 a wonderful manager and housekeeper, yet as tender and quiet and
010676 gentle as a woman could be. She is my right hand. I do not know
010677 what I could do without her. In only one matter has she ever gone
010678 against my wishes. Twice my boy has asked her to marry him, for
010679 he loves her devotedly, but each time she has refused him. I
010680 think that if anyone could have drawn him into the right path it
010681 would have been she, and that his marriage might have changed his
010682 whole life; but now, alas! it is too late--forever too late!
010683 
010684 "Now, Mr. Holmes, you know the people who live under my roof, and
010685 I shall continue with my miserable story.
010686 
010687 "When we were taking coffee in the drawing-room that night after
010688 dinner, I told Arthur and Mary my experience, and of the precious
010689 treasure which we had under our roof, suppressing only the name
010690 of my client. Lucy Parr, who had brought in the coffee, had, I am
010691 sure, left the room; but I cannot swear that the door was closed.
010692 Mary and Arthur were much interested and wished to see the famous
010693 coronet, but I thought it better not to disturb it.
010694 
010695 "'Where have you put it?' asked Arthur.
010696 
010697 "'In my own bureau.'
010698 
010699 "'Well, I hope to goodness the house won't be burgled during the
010700 night.' said he.
010701 
010702 "'It is locked up,' I answered.
010703 
010704 "'Oh, any old key will fit that bureau. When I was a youngster I
010705 have opened it myself with the key of the box-room cupboard.'
010706 
010707 "He often had a wild way of talking, so that I thought little of
010708 what he said. He followed me to my room, however, that night with
010709 a very grave face.
010710 
010711 "'Look here, dad,' said he with his eyes cast down, 'can you let
010712 me have 200 pounds?'
010713 
010714 "'No, I cannot!' I answered sharply. 'I have been far too
010715 generous with you in money matters.'
010716 
010717 "'You have been very kind,' said he, 'but I must have this money,
010718 or else I can never show my face inside the club again.'
010719 
010720 "'And a very good thing, too!' I cried.
010721 
010722 "'Yes, but you would not have me leave it a dishonoured man,'
010723 said he. 'I could not bear the disgrace. I must raise the money
010724 in some way, and if you will not let me have it, then I must try
010725 other means.'
010726 
010727 "I was very angry, for this was the third demand during the
010728 month. 'You shall not have a farthing from me,' I cried, on which
010729 he bowed and left the room without another word.
010730 
010731 "When he was gone I unlocked my bureau, made sure that my
010732 treasure was safe, and locked it again. Then I started to go
010733 round the house to see that all was secure--a duty which I
010734 usually leave to Mary but which I thought it well to perform
010735 myself that night. As I came down the stairs I saw Mary herself
010736 at the side window of the hall, which she closed and fastened as
010737 I approached.
010738 
010739 "'Tell me, dad,' said she, looking, I thought, a little
010740 disturbed, 'did you give Lucy, the maid, leave to go out
010741 to-night?'
010742 
010743 "'Certainly not.'
010744 
010745 "'She came in just now by the back door. I have no doubt that she
010746 has only been to the side gate to see someone, but I think that
010747 it is hardly safe and should be stopped.'
010748 
010749 "'You must speak to her in the morning, or I will if you prefer
010750 it. Are you sure that everything is fastened?'
010751 
010752 "'Quite sure, dad.'
010753 
010754 "'Then, good-night.' I kissed her and went up to my bedroom
010755 again, where I was soon asleep.
010756 
010757 "I am endeavouring to tell you everything, Mr. Holmes, which may
010758 have any bearing upon the case, but I beg that you will question
010759 me upon any point which I do not make clear."
010760 
010761 "On the contrary, your statement is singularly lucid."
010762 
010763 "I come to a part of my story now in which I should wish to be
010764 particularly so. I am not a very heavy sleeper, and the anxiety
010765 in my mind tended, no doubt, to make me even less so than usual.
010766 About two in the morning, then, I was awakened by some sound in
010767 the house. It had ceased ere I was wide awake, but it had left an
010768 impression behind it as though a window had gently closed
010769 somewhere. I lay listening with all my ears. Suddenly, to my
010770 horror, there was a distinct sound of footsteps moving softly in
010771 the next room. I slipped out of bed, all palpitating with fear,
010772 and peeped round the corner of my dressing-room door.
010773 
010774 "'Arthur!' I screamed, 'you villain! you thief! How dare you
010775 touch that coronet?'
010776 
010777 "The gas was half up, as I had left it, and my unhappy boy,
010778 dressed only in his shirt and trousers, was standing beside the
010779 light, holding the coronet in his hands. He appeared to be
010780 wrenching at it, or bending it with all his strength. At my cry
010781 he dropped it from his grasp and turned as pale as death. I
010782 snatched it up and examined it. One of the gold corners, with
010783 three of the beryls in it, was missing.
010784 
010785 "'You blackguard!' I shouted, beside myself with rage. 'You have
010786 destroyed it! You have dishonoured me forever! Where are the
010787 jewels which you have stolen?'
010788 
010789 "'Stolen!' he cried.
010790 
010791 "'Yes, thief!' I roared, shaking him by the shoulder.
010792 
010793 "'There are none missing. There cannot be any missing,' said he.
010794 
010795 "'There are three missing. And you know where they are. Must I
010796 call you a liar as well as a thief? Did I not see you trying to
010797 tear off another piece?'
010798 
010799 "'You have called me names enough,' said he, 'I will not stand it
010800 any longer. I shall not say another word about this business,
010801 since you have chosen to insult me. I will leave your house in
010802 the morning and make my own way in the world.'
010803 
010804 "'You shall leave it in the hands of the police!' I cried
010805 half-mad with grief and rage. 'I shall have this matter probed to
010806 the bottom.'
010807 
010808 "'You shall learn nothing from me,' said he with a passion such
010809 as I should not have thought was in his nature. 'If you choose to
010810 call the police, let the police find what they can.'
010811 
010812 "By this time the whole house was astir, for I had raised my
010813 voice in my anger. Mary was the first to rush into my room, and,
010814 at the sight of the coronet and of Arthur's face, she read the
010815 whole story and, with a scream, fell down senseless on the
010816 ground. I sent the house-maid for the police and put the
010817 investigation into their hands at once. When the inspector and a
010818 constable entered the house, Arthur, who had stood sullenly with
010819 his arms folded, asked me whether it was my intention to charge
010820 him with theft. I answered that it had ceased to be a private
010821 matter, but had become a public one, since the ruined coronet was
010822 national property. I was determined that the law should have its
010823 way in everything.
010824 
010825 "'At least,' said he, 'you will not have me arrested at once. It
010826 would be to your advantage as well as mine if I might leave the
010827 house for five minutes.'
010828 
010829 "'That you may get away, or perhaps that you may conceal what you
010830 have stolen,' said I. And then, realising the dreadful position
010831 in which I was placed, I implored him to remember that not only
010832 my honour but that of one who was far greater than I was at
010833 stake; and that he threatened to raise a scandal which would
010834 convulse the nation. He might avert it all if he would but tell
010835 me what he had done with the three missing stones.
010836 
010837 "'You may as well face the matter,' said I; 'you have been caught
010838 in the act, and no confession could make your guilt more heinous.
010839 If you but make such reparation as is in your power, by telling
010840 us where the beryls are, all shall be forgiven and forgotten.'
010841 
010842 "'Keep your forgiveness for those who ask for it,' he answered,
010843 turning away from me with a sneer. I saw that he was too hardened
010844 for any words of mine to influence him. There was but one way for
010845 it. I called in the inspector and gave him into custody. A search
010846 was made at once not only of his person but of his room and of
010847 every portion of the house where he could possibly have concealed
010848 the gems; but no trace of them could be found, nor would the
010849 wretched boy open his mouth for all our persuasions and our
010850 threats. This morning he was removed to a cell, and I, after
010851 going through all the police formalities, have hurried round to
010852 you to implore you to use your skill in unravelling the matter.
010853 The police have openly confessed that they can at present make
010854 nothing of it. You may go to any expense which you think
010855 necessary. I have already offered a reward of 1000 pounds. My
010856 God, what shall I do! I have lost my honour, my gems, and my son
010857 in one night. Oh, what shall I do!"
010858 
010859 He put a hand on either side of his head and rocked himself to
010860 and fro, droning to himself like a child whose grief has got
010861 beyond words.
010862 
010863 Sherlock Holmes sat silent for some few minutes, with his brows
010864 knitted and his eyes fixed upon the fire.
010865 
010866 "Do you receive much company?" he asked.
010867 
010868 "None save my partner with his family and an occasional friend of
010869 Arthur's. Sir George Burnwell has been several times lately. No
010870 one else, I think."
010871 
010872 "Do you go out much in society?"
010873 
010874 "Arthur does. Mary and I stay at home. We neither of us care for
010875 it."
010876 
010877 "That is unusual in a young girl."
010878 
010879 "She is of a quiet nature. Besides, she is not so very young. She
010880 is four-and-twenty."
010881 
010882 "This matter, from what you say, seems to have been a shock to
010883 her also."
010884 
010885 "Terrible! She is even more affected than I."
010886 
010887 "You have neither of you any doubt as to your son's guilt?"
010888 
010889 "How can we have when I saw him with my own eyes with the coronet
010890 in his hands."
010891 
010892 "I hardly consider that a conclusive proof. Was the remainder of
010893 the coronet at all injured?"
010894 
010895 "Yes, it was twisted."
010896 
010897 "Do you not think, then, that he might have been trying to
010898 straighten it?"
010899 
010900 "God bless you! You are doing what you can for him and for me.
010901 But it is too heavy a task. What was he doing there at all? If
010902 his purpose were innocent, why did he not say so?"
010903 
010904 "Precisely. And if it were guilty, why did he not invent a lie?
010905 His silence appears to me to cut both ways. There are several
010906 singular points about the case. What did the police think of the
010907 noise which awoke you from your sleep?"
010908 
010909 "They considered that it might be caused by Arthur's closing his
010910 bedroom door."
010911 
010912 "A likely story! As if a man bent on felony would slam his door
010913 so as to wake a household. What did they say, then, of the
010914 disappearance of these gems?"
010915 
010916 "They are still sounding the planking and probing the furniture
010917 in the hope of finding them."
010918 
010919 "Have they thought of looking outside the house?"
010920 
010921 "Yes, they have shown extraordinary energy. The whole garden has
010922 already been minutely examined."
010923 
010924 "Now, my dear sir," said Holmes, "is it not obvious to you now
010925 that this matter really strikes very much deeper than either you
010926 or the police were at first inclined to think? It appeared to you
010927 to be a simple case; to me it seems exceedingly complex. Consider
010928 what is involved by your theory. You suppose that your son came
010929 down from his bed, went, at great risk, to your dressing-room,
010930 opened your bureau, took out your coronet, broke off by main
010931 force a small portion of it, went off to some other place,
010932 concealed three gems out of the thirty-nine, with such skill that
010933 nobody can find them, and then returned with the other thirty-six
010934 into the room in which he exposed himself to the greatest danger
010935 of being discovered. I ask you now, is such a theory tenable?"
010936 
010937 "But what other is there?" cried the banker with a gesture of
010938 despair. "If his motives were innocent, why does he not explain
010939 them?"
010940 
010941 "It is our task to find that out," replied Holmes; "so now, if
010942 you please, Mr. Holder, we will set off for Streatham together,
010943 and devote an hour to glancing a little more closely into
010944 details."
010945 
010946 My friend insisted upon my accompanying them in their expedition,
010947 which I was eager enough to do, for my curiosity and sympathy
010948 were deeply stirred by the story to which we had listened. I
010949 confess that the guilt of the banker's son appeared to me to be
010950 as obvious as it did to his unhappy father, but still I had such
010951 faith in Holmes' judgment that I felt that there must be some
010952 grounds for hope as long as he was dissatisfied with the accepted
010953 explanation. He hardly spoke a word the whole way out to the
010954 southern suburb, but sat with his chin upon his breast and his
010955 hat drawn over his eyes, sunk in the deepest thought. Our client
010956 appeared to have taken fresh heart at the little glimpse of hope
010957 which had been presented to him, and he even broke into a
010958 desultory chat with me over his business affairs. A short railway
010959 journey and a shorter walk brought us to Fairbank, the modest
010960 residence of the great financier.
010961 
010962 Fairbank was a good-sized square house of white stone, standing
010963 back a little from the road. A double carriage-sweep, with a
010964 snow-clad lawn, stretched down in front to two large iron gates
010965 which closed the entrance. On the right side was a small wooden
010966 thicket, which led into a narrow path between two neat hedges
010967 stretching from the road to the kitchen door, and forming the
010968 tradesmen's entrance. On the left ran a lane which led to the
010969 stables, and was not itself within the grounds at all, being a
010970 public, though little used, thoroughfare. Holmes left us standing
010971 at the door and walked slowly all round the house, across the
010972 front, down the tradesmen's path, and so round by the garden
010973 behind into the stable lane. So long was he that Mr. Holder and I
010974 went into the dining-room and waited by the fire until he should
010975 return. We were sitting there in silence when the door opened and
010976 a young lady came in. She was rather above the middle height,
010977 slim, with dark hair and eyes, which seemed the darker against
010978 the absolute pallor of her skin. I do not think that I have ever
010979 seen such deadly paleness in a woman's face. Her lips, too, were
010980 bloodless, but her eyes were flushed with crying. As she swept
010981 silently into the room she impressed me with a greater sense of
010982 grief than the banker had done in the morning, and it was the
010983 more striking in her as she was evidently a woman of strong
010984 character, with immense capacity for self-restraint. Disregarding
010985 my presence, she went straight to her uncle and passed her hand
010986 over his head with a sweet womanly caress.
010987 
010988 "You have given orders that Arthur should be liberated, have you
010989 not, dad?" she asked.
010990 
010991 "No, no, my girl, the matter must be probed to the bottom."
010992 
010993 "But I am so sure that he is innocent. You know what woman's
010994 instincts are. I know that he has done no harm and that you will
010995 be sorry for having acted so harshly."
010996 
010997 "Why is he silent, then, if he is innocent?"
010998 
010999 "Who knows? Perhaps because he was so angry that you should
011000 suspect him."
011001 
011002 "How could I help suspecting him, when I actually saw him with
011003 the coronet in his hand?"
011004 
011005 "Oh, but he had only picked it up to look at it. Oh, do, do take
011006 my word for it that he is innocent. Let the matter drop and say
011007 no more. It is so dreadful to think of our dear Arthur in
011008 prison!"
011009 
011010 "I shall never let it drop until the gems are found--never, Mary!
011011 Your affection for Arthur blinds you as to the awful consequences
011012 to me. Far from hushing the thing up, I have brought a gentleman
011013 down from London to inquire more deeply into it."
011014 
011015 "This gentleman?" she asked, facing round to me.
011016 
011017 "No, his friend. He wished us to leave him alone. He is round in
011018 the stable lane now."
011019 
011020 "The stable lane?" She raised her dark eyebrows. "What can he
011021 hope to find there? Ah! this, I suppose, is he. I trust, sir,
011022 that you will succeed in proving, what I feel sure is the truth,
011023 that my cousin Arthur is innocent of this crime."
011024 
011025 "I fully share your opinion, and I trust, with you, that we may
011026 prove it," returned Holmes, going back to the mat to knock the
011027 snow from his shoes. "I believe I have the honour of addressing
011028 Miss Mary Holder. Might I ask you a question or two?"
011029 
011030 "Pray do, sir, if it may help to clear this horrible affair up."
011031 
011032 "You heard nothing yourself last night?"
011033 
011034 "Nothing, until my uncle here began to speak loudly. I heard
011035 that, and I came down."
011036 
011037 "You shut up the windows and doors the night before. Did you
011038 fasten all the windows?"
011039 
011040 "Yes."
011041 
011042 "Were they all fastened this morning?"
011043 
011044 "Yes."
011045 
011046 "You have a maid who has a sweetheart? I think that you remarked
011047 to your uncle last night that she had been out to see him?"
011048 
011049 "Yes, and she was the girl who waited in the drawing-room, and
011050 who may have heard uncle's remarks about the coronet."
011051 
011052 "I see. You infer that she may have gone out to tell her
011053 sweetheart, and that the two may have planned the robbery."
011054 
011055 "But what is the good of all these vague theories," cried the
011056 banker impatiently, "when I have told you that I saw Arthur with
011057 the coronet in his hands?"
011058 
011059 "Wait a little, Mr. Holder. We must come back to that. About this
011060 girl, Miss Holder. You saw her return by the kitchen door, I
011061 presume?"
011062 
011063 "Yes; when I went to see if the door was fastened for the night I

011065 
011066 "Do you know him?"
011067 
011068 "Oh, yes! he is the green-grocer who brings our vegetables round.
011069 His name is Francis Prosper."
011070 
011071 "He stood," said Holmes, "to the left of the door--that is to
011072 say, farther up the path than is necessary to reach the door?"
011073 
011074 "Yes, he did."
011075 
011076 "And he is a man with a wooden leg?"
011077 
011078 Something like fear sprang up in the young lady's expressive
011079 black eyes. "Why, you are like a magician," said she. "How do you
011080 know that?" She smiled, but there was no answering smile in
011081 Holmes' thin, eager face.
011082 
011083 "I should be very glad now to go upstairs," said he. "I shall
011084 probably wish to go over the outside of the house again. Perhaps
011085 I had better take a look at the lower windows before I go up."
011086 
011087 He walked swiftly round from one to the other, pausing only at
