011092 
011093 The banker's dressing-room was a plainly furnished little
011094 chamber, with a grey carpet, a large bureau, and a long mirror.
011095 Holmes went to the bureau first and looked hard at the lock.
011096 
011097 "Which key was used to open it?" he asked.
011098 
011099 "That which my son himself indicated--that of the cupboard of the
011100 lumber-room."
011101 
011102 "Have you it here?"
011103 
011104 "That is it on the dressing-table."
011105 
011106 Sherlock Holmes took it up and opened the bureau.
011107 
011108 "It is a noiseless lock," said he. "It is no wonder that it did
011109 not wake you. This case, I presume, contains the coronet. We must
011110 have a look at it." He opened the case, and taking out the diadem
011111 he laid it upon the table. It was a magnificent specimen of the
011112 jeweller's art, and the thirty-six stones were the finest that I
011113 have ever seen. At one side of the coronet was a cracked edge,
011114 where a corner holding three gems had been torn away.
011115 
011116 "Now, Mr. Holder," said Holmes, "here is the corner which
011117 corresponds to that which has been so unfortunately lost. Might I
011118 beg that you will break it off."
011119 
011120 The banker recoiled in horror. "I should not dream of trying,"
011121 said he.
011122 
011123 "Then I will." Holmes suddenly bent his strength upon it, but
011124 without result. "I feel it give a little," said he; "but, though
011125 I am exceptionally strong in the fingers, it would take me all my
011126 time to break it. An ordinary man could not do it. Now, what do
011127 you think would happen if I did break it, Mr. Holder? There would
011128 be a noise like a pistol shot. Do you tell me that all this
011129 happened within a few yards of your bed and that you heard
011130 nothing of it?"
011131 
011132 "I do not know what to think. It is all dark to me."
011133 
011134 "But perhaps it may grow lighter as we go. What do you think,
011135 Miss Holder?"
011136 
011137 "I confess that I still share my uncle's perplexity."
011138 
011139 "Your son had no shoes or slippers on when you saw him?"
011140 
011141 "He had nothing on save only his trousers and shirt."
011142 
011143 "Thank you. We have certainly been favoured with extraordinary
011144 luck during this inquiry, and it will be entirely our own fault
011145 if we do not succeed in clearing the matter up. With your
011146 permission, Mr. Holder, I shall now continue my investigations
011147 outside."
011148 
011149 He went alone, at his own request, for he explained that any
011150 unnecessary footmarks might make his task more difficult. For an
011151 hour or more he was at work, returning at last with his feet
011152 heavy with snow and his features as inscrutable as ever.
011153 
011154 "I think that I have seen now all that there is to see, Mr.
011155 Holder," said he; "I can serve you best by returning to my
011156 rooms."
011157 
011158 "But the gems, Mr. Holmes. Where are they?"
011159 
011160 "I cannot tell."
011161 
011162 The banker wrung his hands. "I shall never see them again!" he
011163 cried. "And my son? You give me hopes?"
011164 
011165 "My opinion is in no way altered."
011166 
011167 "Then, for God's sake, what was this dark business which was
011168 acted in my house last night?"
011169 
011170 "If you can call upon me at my Baker Street rooms to-morrow
011171 morning between nine and ten I shall be happy to do what I can to
011172 make it clearer. I understand that you give me carte blanche to
011173 act for you, provided only that I get back the gems, and that you
011174 place no limit on the sum I may draw."
011175 
011176 "I would give my fortune to have them back."
011177 
011178 "Very good. I shall look into the matter between this and then.
011179 Good-bye; it is just possible that I may have to come over here
011180 again before evening."
011181 
011182 It was obvious to me that my companion's mind was now made up
011183 about the case, although what his conclusions were was more than
011184 I could even dimly imagine. Several times during our homeward
011185 journey I endeavoured to sound him upon the point, but he always
011186 glided away to some other topic, until at last I gave it over in
011187 despair. It was not yet three when we found ourselves in our
011188 rooms once more. He hurried to his chamber and was down again in
011189 a few minutes dressed as a common loafer. With his collar turned
011190 up, his shiny, seedy coat, his red cravat, and his worn boots, he
011191 was a perfect sample of the class.
011192 
011193 "I think that this should do," said he, glancing into the glass
011194 above the fireplace. "I only wish that you could come with me,
011195 Watson, but I fear that it won't do. I may be on the trail in
011196 this matter, or I may be following a will-o'-the-wisp, but I
011197 shall soon know which it is. I hope that I may be back in a few
011198 hours." He cut a slice of beef from the joint upon the sideboard,
011199 sandwiched it between two rounds of bread, and thrusting this
011200 rude meal into his pocket he started off upon his expedition.
011201 
011202 I had just finished my tea when he returned, evidently in
011203 excellent spirits, swinging an old elastic-sided boot in his
011204 hand. He chucked it down into a corner and helped himself to a
011205 cup of tea.
011206 
011207 "I only looked in as I passed," said he. "I am going right on."
011208 
011209 "Where to?"
011210 
011211 "Oh, to the other side of the West End. It may be some time
011212 before I get back. Don't wait up for me in case I should be
011213 late."
011214 
011215 "How are you getting on?"
011216 
011217 "Oh, so so. Nothing to complain of. I have been out to Streatham
011218 since I saw you last, but I did not call at the house. It is a
011219 very sweet little problem, and I would not have missed it for a
011220 good deal. However, I must not sit gossiping here, but must get
011221 these disreputable clothes off and return to my highly
011222 respectable self."
011223 
011224 I could see by his manner that he had stronger reasons for
011225 satisfaction than his words alone would imply. His eyes twinkled,
011226 and there was even a touch of colour upon his sallow cheeks. He
011227 hastened upstairs, and a few minutes later I heard the slam of
011228 the hall door, which told me that he was off once more upon his
011229 congenial hunt.
011230 
011231 I waited until midnight, but there was no sign of his return, so
011232 I retired to my room. It was no uncommon thing for him to be away
011233 for days and nights on end when he was hot upon a scent, so that
011234 his lateness caused me no surprise. I do not know at what hour he
011235 came in, but when I came down to breakfast in the morning there
011236 he was with a cup of coffee in one hand and the paper in the
011237 other, as fresh and trim as possible.
011238 
011239 "You will excuse my beginning without you, Watson," said he, "but
011240 you remember that our client has rather an early appointment this
011241 morning."
011242 
011243 "Why, it is after nine now," I answered. "I should not be
011244 surprised if that were he. I thought I heard a ring."
011245 
011246 It was, indeed, our friend the financier. I was shocked by the
011247 change which had come over him, for his face which was naturally
011248 of a broad and massive mould, was now pinched and fallen in,
011249 while his hair seemed to me at least a shade whiter. He entered
011250 with a weariness and lethargy which was even more painful than
011251 his violence of the morning before, and he dropped heavily into
011252 the armchair which I pushed forward for him.
011253 
011254 "I do not know what I have done to be so severely tried," said
011255 he. "Only two days ago I was a happy and prosperous man, without
011256 a care in the world. Now I am left to a lonely and dishonoured
011257 age. One sorrow comes close upon the heels of another. My niece,
011258 Mary, has deserted me."
011259 
011260 "Deserted you?"
011261 
011262 "Yes. Her bed this morning had not been slept in, her room was
011263 empty, and a note for me lay upon the hall table. I had said to
011264 her last night, in sorrow and not in anger, that if she had
011265 married my boy all might have been well with him. Perhaps it was
011266 thoughtless of me to say so. It is to that remark that she refers
011267 in this note:
011268 
011269 "'MY DEAREST UNCLE:--I feel that I have brought trouble upon you,
011270 and that if I had acted differently this terrible misfortune
011271 might never have occurred. I cannot, with this thought in my
011272 mind, ever again be happy under your roof, and I feel that I must
011273 leave you forever. Do not worry about my future, for that is
011274 provided for; and, above all, do not search for me, for it will
011275 be fruitless labour and an ill-service to me. In life or in
011276 death, I am ever your loving,--MARY.'
011277 
011278 "What could she mean by that note, Mr. Holmes? Do you think it
011279 points to suicide?"
011280 
011281 "No, no, nothing of the kind. It is perhaps the best possible
011282 solution. I trust, Mr. Holder, that you are nearing the end of
011283 your troubles."
011284 
011285 "Ha! You say so! You have heard something, Mr. Holmes; you have
011286 learned something! Where are the gems?"
011287 
011288 "You would not think 1000 pounds apiece an excessive sum for
011289 them?"
011290 
011291 "I would pay ten."
011292 
011293 "That would be unnecessary. Three thousand will cover the matter.
011294 And there is a little reward, I fancy. Have you your check-book?
011295 Here is a pen. Better make it out for 4000 pounds."
011296 
011297 With a dazed face the banker made out the required check. Holmes
011298 walked over to his desk, took out a little triangular piece of
011299 gold with three gems in it, and threw it down upon the table.
011300 
011301 With a shriek of joy our client clutched it up.
011302 
011303 "You have it!" he gasped. "I am saved! I am saved!"
011304 
011305 The reaction of joy was as passionate as his grief had been, and
011306 he hugged his recovered gems to his bosom.
011307 
011308 "There is one other thing you owe, Mr. Holder," said Sherlock
011309 Holmes rather sternly.
011310 
011311 "Owe!" He caught up a pen. "Name the sum, and I will pay it."
011312 
011313 "No, the debt is not to me. You owe a very humble apology to that
011314 noble lad, your son, who has carried himself in this matter as I
011315 should be proud to see my own son do, should I ever chance to
011316 have one."
011317 
011318 "Then it was not Arthur who took them?"
011319 
011320 "I told you yesterday, and I repeat to-day, that it was not."
011321 
011322 "You are sure of it! Then let us hurry to him at once to let him
011323 know that the truth is known."
011324 
011325 "He knows it already. When I had cleared it all up I had an
011326 interview with him, and finding that he would not tell me the
011327 story, I told it to him, on which he had to confess that I was
011328 right and to add the very few details which were not yet quite
011329 clear to me. Your news of this morning, however, may open his
011330 lips."
011331 
011332 "For heaven's sake, tell me, then, what is this extraordinary
011333 mystery!"
011334 
011335 "I will do so, and I will show you the steps by which I reached
011336 it. And let me say to you, first, that which it is hardest for me
011337 to say and for you to hear: there has been an understanding
011338 between Sir George Burnwell and your niece Mary. They have now
011339 fled together."
011340 
011341 "My Mary? Impossible!"
011342 
011343 "It is unfortunately more than possible; it is certain. Neither
011344 you nor your son knew the true character of this man when you
011345 admitted him into your family circle. He is one of the most
011346 dangerous men in England--a ruined gambler, an absolutely
011347 desperate villain, a man without heart or conscience. Your niece
011348 knew nothing of such men. When he breathed his vows to her, as he
011349 had done to a hundred before her, she flattered herself that she
011350 alone had touched his heart. The devil knows best what he said,
011351 but at least she became his tool and was in the habit of seeing
011352 him nearly every evening."
011353 
011354 "I cannot, and I will not, believe it!" cried the banker with an
011355 ashen face.
011356 
011357 "I will tell you, then, what occurred in your house last night.
011358 Your niece, when you had, as she thought, gone to your room,
011359 slipped down and talked to her lover through the window which
011360 leads into the stable lane. His footmarks had pressed right
011361 through the snow, so long had he stood there. She told him of the
011362 coronet. His wicked lust for gold kindled at the news, and he
011363 bent her to his will. I have no doubt that she loved you, but
011364 there are women in whom the love of a lover extinguishes all
011365 other loves, and I think that she must have been one. She had
011366 hardly listened to his instructions when she saw you coming
011367 downstairs, on which she closed the window rapidly and told you
011368 about one of the servants' escapade with her wooden-legged lover,
011369 which was all perfectly true.
011370 
011371 "Your boy, Arthur, went to bed after his interview with you but
011372 he slept badly on account of his uneasiness about his club debts.
011373 In the middle of the night he heard a soft tread pass his door,
011374 so he rose and, looking out, was surprised to see his cousin
011375 walking very stealthily along the passage until she disappeared
011376 into your dressing-room. Petrified with astonishment, the lad
011377 slipped on some clothes and waited there in the dark to see what
011378 would come of this strange affair. Presently she emerged from the
011379 room again, and in the light of the passage-lamp your son saw
011380 that she carried the precious coronet in her hands. She passed
011381 down the stairs, and he, thrilling with horror, ran along and
011382 slipped behind the curtain near your door, whence he could see
011383 what passed in the hall beneath. He saw her stealthily open the
011384 window, hand out the coronet to someone in the gloom, and then
011385 closing it once more hurry back to her room, passing quite close
011386 to where he stood hid behind the curtain.
011387 
011388 "As long as she was on the scene he could not take any action
011389 without a horrible exposure of the woman whom he loved. But the
011390 instant that she was gone he realised how crushing a misfortune
011391 this would be for you, and how all-important it was to set it
011392 right. He rushed down, just as he was, in his bare feet, opened
011393 the window, sprang out into the snow, and ran down the lane,
011394 where he could see a dark figure in the moonlight. Sir George
011395 Burnwell tried to get away, but Arthur caught him, and there was
011396 a struggle between them, your lad tugging at one side of the
011397 coronet, and his opponent at the other. In the scuffle, your son
011398 struck Sir George and cut him over the eye. Then something
011399 suddenly snapped, and your son, finding that he had the coronet
011400 in his hands, rushed back, closed the window, ascended to your
011401 room, and had just observed that the coronet had been twisted in
011402 the struggle and was endeavouring to straighten it when you
011403 appeared upon the scene."
011404 
011405 "Is it possible?" gasped the banker.
011406 
011407 "You then roused his anger by calling him names at a moment when
011408 he felt that he had deserved your warmest thanks. He could not
011409 explain the true state of affairs without betraying one who
011410 certainly deserved little enough consideration at his hands. He
011411 took the more chivalrous view, however, and preserved her
011412 secret."
011413 
011414 "And that was why she shrieked and fainted when she saw the
011415 coronet," cried Mr. Holder. "Oh, my God! what a blind fool I have
011416 been! And his asking to be allowed to go out for five minutes!
011417 The dear fellow wanted to see if the missing piece were at the
011418 scene of the struggle. How cruelly I have misjudged him!"
011419 
011420 "When I arrived at the house," continued Holmes, "I at once went
011421 very carefully round it to observe if there were any traces in
011422 the snow which might help me. I knew that none had fallen since
011423 the evening before, and also that there had been a strong frost
011424 to preserve impressions. I passed along the tradesmen's path, but
011425 found it all trampled down and indistinguishable. Just beyond it,
011426 however, at the far side of the kitchen door, a woman had stood
011427 and talked with a man, whose round impressions on one side showed
011428 that he had a wooden leg. I could even tell that they had been
011429 disturbed, for the woman had run back swiftly to the door, as was
011430 shown by the deep toe and light heel marks, while Wooden-leg had
011431 waited a little, and then had gone away. I thought at the time
011432 that this might be the maid and her sweetheart, of whom you had
011433 already spoken to me, and inquiry showed it was so. I passed
011434 round the garden without seeing anything more than random tracks,
011435 which I took to be the police; but when I got into the stable
011436 lane a very long and complex story was written in the snow in
011437 front of me.
011438 
011439 "There was a double line of tracks of a booted man, and a second
011440 double line which I saw with delight belonged to a man with naked
011441 feet. I was at once convinced from what you had told me that the
011442 latter was your son. The first had walked both ways, but the
011443 other had run swiftly, and as his tread was marked in places over
011444 the depression of the boot, it was obvious that he had passed
011445 after the other. I followed them up and found they led to the
011446 hall window, where Boots had worn all the snow away while
011447 waiting. Then I walked to the other end, which was a hundred
011448 yards or more down the lane. I saw where Boots had faced round,
011449 where the snow was cut up as though there had been a struggle,
011450 and, finally, where a few drops of blood had fallen, to show me
011451 that I was not mistaken. Boots had then run down the lane, and
011452 another little smudge of blood showed that it was he who had been
011453 hurt. When he came to the highroad at the other end, I found that
011454 the pavement had been cleared, so there was an end to that clue.
011455 
011456 "On entering the house, however, I examined, as you remember, the
011457 sill and framework of the hall window with my lens, and I could
011458 at once see that someone had passed out. I could distinguish the
011459 outline of an instep where the wet foot had been placed in coming
011460 in. I was then beginning to be able to form an opinion as to what
011461 had occurred. A man had waited outside the window; someone had
011462 brought the gems; the deed had been overseen by your son; he had
011463 pursued the thief; had struggled with him; they had each tugged
011464 at the coronet, their united strength causing injuries which
011465 neither alone could have effected. He had returned with the
011466 prize, but had left a fragment in the grasp of his opponent. So
011467 far I was clear. The question now was, who was the man and who
011468 was it brought him the coronet?
011469 
011470 "It is an old maxim of mine that when you have excluded the
011471 impossible, whatever remains, however improbable, must be the
011472 truth. Now, I knew that it was not you who had brought it down,
011473 so there only remained your niece and the maids. But if it were
011474 the maids, why should your son allow himself to be accused in
011475 their place? There could be no possible reason. As he loved his
011476 cousin, however, there was an excellent explanation why he should
011477 retain her secret--the more so as the secret was a disgraceful
011478 one. When I remembered that you had seen her at that window, and
011479 how she had fainted on seeing the coronet again, my conjecture
011480 became a certainty.
011481 
011482 "And who could it be who was her confederate? A lover evidently,
011483 for who else could outweigh the love and gratitude which she must
011484 feel to you? I knew that you went out little, and that your
011485 circle of friends was a very limited one. But among them was Sir
011486 George Burnwell. I had heard of him before as being a man of evil
011487 reputation among women. It must have been he who wore those boots
011488 and retained the missing gems. Even though he knew that Arthur
011489 had discovered him, he might still flatter himself that he was
011490 safe, for the lad could not say a word without compromising his
011491 own family.
011492 
011493 "Well, your own good sense will suggest what measures I took
011494 next. I went in the shape of a loafer to Sir George's house,
011495 managed to pick up an acquaintance with his valet, learned that
011496 his master had cut his head the night before, and, finally, at
011497 the expense of six shillings, made all sure by buying a pair of
011498 his cast-off shoes. With these I journeyed down to Streatham and
011499 saw that they exactly fitted the tracks."
011500 
011501 "I saw an ill-dressed vagabond in the lane yesterday evening,"
011502 said Mr. Holder.
011503 
011504 "Precisely. It was I. I found that I had my man, so I came home
011505 and changed my clothes. It was a delicate part which I had to
011506 play then, for I saw that a prosecution must be avoided to avert
011507 scandal, and I knew that so astute a villain would see that our
011508 hands were tied in the matter. I went and saw him. At first, of
011509 course, he denied everything. But when I gave him every
011510 particular that had occurred, he tried to bluster and took down a
011511 life-preserver from the wall. I knew my man, however, and I
011512 clapped a pistol to his head before he could strike. Then he
011513 became a little more reasonable. I told him that we would give
011514 him a price for the stones he held--1000 pounds apiece. That
011515 brought out the first signs of grief that he had shown. 'Why,
011516 dash it all!' said he, 'I've let them go at six hundred for the
011517 three!' I soon managed to get the address of the receiver who had
011518 them, on promising him that there would be no prosecution. Off I
011519 set to him, and after much chaffering I got our stones at 1000
011520 pounds apiece. Then I looked in upon your son, told him that all
011521 was right, and eventually got to my bed about two o'clock, after
011522 what I may call a really hard day's work."
011523 
011524 "A day which has saved England from a great public scandal," said
011525 the banker, rising. "Sir, I cannot find words to thank you, but
011526 you shall not find me ungrateful for what you have done. Your
011527 skill has indeed exceeded all that I have heard of it. And now I
011528 must fly to my dear boy to apologise to him for the wrong which I
011529 have done him. As to what you tell me of poor Mary, it goes to my
011530 very heart. Not even your skill can inform me where she is now."
011531 
011532 "I think that we may safely say," returned Holmes, "that she is
011533 wherever Sir George Burnwell is. It is equally certain, too, that
011534 whatever her sins are, they will soon receive a more than
011535 sufficient punishment."
011536 
011537 
011538 
011539 XII. THE ADVENTURE OF THE COPPER BEECHES
011540 
011541 "To the man who loves art for its own sake," remarked Sherlock
011542 Holmes, tossing aside the advertisement sheet of the Daily
011543 Telegraph, "it is frequently in its least important and lowliest
011544 manifestations that the keenest pleasure is to be derived. It is
011545 pleasant to me to observe, Watson, that you have so far grasped
011546 this truth that in these little records of our cases which you
011547 have been good enough to draw up, and, I am bound to say,
011548 occasionally to embellish, you have given prominence not so much
011549 to the many causes clbres and sensational trials in which I
011550 have figured but rather to those incidents which may have been
011551 trivial in themselves, but which have given room for those
011552 faculties of deduction and of logical synthesis which I have made
011553 my special province."
011554 
011555 "And yet," said I, smiling, "I cannot quite hold myself absolved
011556 from the charge of sensationalism which has been urged against my
011557 records."
011558 
011559 "You have erred, perhaps," he observed, taking up a glowing
011560 cinder with the tongs and lighting with it the long cherry-wood
011561 pipe which was wont to replace his clay when he was in a
011562 disputatious rather than a meditative mood--"you have erred
011563 perhaps in attempting to put colour and life into each of your
011564 statements instead of confining yourself to the task of placing
011565 upon record that severe reasoning from cause to effect which is
011566 really the only notable feature about the thing."
011567 
011568 "It seems to me that I have done you full justice in the matter,"
011569 I remarked with some coldness, for I was repelled by the egotism
011570 which I had more than once observed to be a strong factor in my
011571 friend's singular character.
011572 
011573 "No, it is not selfishness or conceit," said he, answering, as
011574 was his wont, my thoughts rather than my words. "If I claim full
011575 justice for my art, it is because it is an impersonal thing--a
011576 thing beyond myself. Crime is common. Logic is rare. Therefore it
011577 is upon the logic rather than upon the crime that you should
011578 dwell. You have degraded what should have been a course of
011579 lectures into a series of tales."
011580 
011581 It was a cold morning of the early spring, and we sat after
011582 breakfast on either side of a cheery fire in the old room at
011583 Baker Street. A thick fog rolled down between the lines of
011584 dun-coloured houses, and the opposing windows loomed like dark,
011585 shapeless blurs through the heavy yellow wreaths. Our gas was lit
011586 and shone on the white cloth and glimmer of china and metal, for
011587 the table had not been cleared yet. Sherlock Holmes had been
011588 silent all the morning, dipping continuously into the
011589 advertisement columns of a succession of papers until at last,
011590 having apparently given up his search, he had emerged in no very
011591 sweet temper to lecture me upon my literary shortcomings.
011592 
011593 "At the same time," he remarked after a pause, during which he
011594 had sat puffing at his long pipe and gazing down into the fire,
011595 "you can hardly be open to a charge of sensationalism, for out of
011596 these cases which you have been so kind as to interest yourself
011597 in, a fair proportion do not treat of crime, in its legal sense,
011598 at all. The small matter in which I endeavoured to help the King
011599 of Bohemia, the singular experience of Miss Mary Sutherland, the
011600 problem connected with the man with the twisted lip, and the
011601 incident of the noble bachelor, were all matters which are
011602 outside the pale of the law. But in avoiding the sensational, I
011603 fear that you may have bordered on the trivial."
011604 
011605 "The end may have been so," I answered, "but the methods I hold
011606 to have been novel and of interest."
011607 
011608 "Pshaw, my dear fellow, what do the public, the great unobservant
011609 public, who could hardly tell a weaver by his tooth or a
011610 compositor by his left thumb, care about the finer shades of
011611 analysis and deduction! But, indeed, if you are trivial, I cannot
011612 blame you, for the days of the great cases are past. Man, or at
011613 least criminal man, has lost all enterprise and originality. As
011614 to my own little practice, it seems to be degenerating into an
011615 agency for recovering lost lead pencils and giving advice to
011616 young ladies from boarding-schools. I think that I have touched
011617 bottom at last, however. This note I had this morning marks my
011618 zero-point, I fancy. Read it!" He tossed a crumpled letter across
011619 to me.
011620 
011621 It was dated from Montague Place upon the preceding evening, and
011622 ran thus:
011623 
011624 "DEAR MR. HOLMES:--I am very anxious to consult you as to whether
011625 I should or should not accept a situation which has been offered
011626 to me as governess. I shall call at half-past ten to-morrow if I
011627 do not inconvenience you. Yours faithfully,
011628                                                "VIOLET HUNTER."
011629 
011630 "Do you know the young lady?" I asked.
011631 
011632 "Not I."
011633 
011634 "It is half-past ten now."
011635 
011636 "Yes, and I have no doubt that is her ring."
011637 
011638 "It may turn out to be of more interest than you think. You
011639 remember that the affair of the blue carbuncle, which appeared to
011640 be a mere whim at first, developed into a serious investigation.
011641 It may be so in this case, also."
011642 
011643 "Well, let us hope so. But our doubts will very soon be solved,
011644 for here, unless I am much mistaken, is the person in question."
011645 
011646 As he spoke the door opened and a young lady entered the room.
011647 She was plainly but neatly dressed, with a bright, quick face,
011648 freckled like a plover's egg, and with the brisk manner of a
011649 woman who has had her own way to make in the world.
011650 
011651 "You will excuse my troubling you, I am sure," said she, as my
011652 companion rose to greet her, "but I have had a very strange
011653 experience, and as I have no parents or relations of any sort
011654 from whom I could ask advice, I thought that perhaps you would be
011655 kind enough to tell me what I should do."
011656 
011657 "Pray take a seat, Miss Hunter. I shall be happy to do anything
011658 that I can to serve you."
011659 
011660 I could see that Holmes was favourably impressed by the manner
011661 and speech of his new client. He looked her over in his searching
011662 fashion, and then composed himself, with his lids drooping and
011663 his finger-tips together, to listen to her story.
011664 
011665 "I have been a governess for five years," said she, "in the
011666 family of Colonel Spence Munro, but two months ago the colonel
011667 received an appointment at Halifax, in Nova Scotia, and took his
011668 children over to America with him, so that I found myself without
011669 a situation. I advertised, and I answered advertisements, but
011670 without success. At last the little money which I had saved began
011671 to run short, and I was at my wit's end as to what I should do.
011672 
011673 "There is a well-known agency for governesses in the West End
011674 called Westaway's, and there I used to call about once a week in
011675 order to see whether anything had turned up which might suit me.
011676 Westaway was the name of the founder of the business, but it is
011677 really managed by Miss Stoper. She sits in her own little office,
011678 and the ladies who are seeking employment wait in an anteroom,
011679 and are then shown in one by one, when she consults her ledgers
011680 and sees whether she has anything which would suit them.
011681 
011682 "Well, when I called last week I was shown into the little office
011683 as usual, but I found that Miss Stoper was not alone. A
011684 prodigiously stout man with a very smiling face and a great heavy
011685 chin which rolled down in fold upon fold over his throat sat at
011686 her elbow with a pair of glasses on his nose, looking very
011687 earnestly at the ladies who entered. As I came in he gave quite a
011688 jump in his chair and turned quickly to Miss Stoper.
011689 
011690 "'That will do,' said he; 'I could not ask for anything better.
011691 Capital! capital!' He seemed quite enthusiastic and rubbed his
011692 hands together in the most genial fashion. He was such a
011693 comfortable-looking man that it was quite a pleasure to look at
011694 him.
011695 
011696 "'You are looking for a situation, miss?' he asked.
011697 
011698 "'Yes, sir.'
011699 
011700 "'As governess?'
011701 
011702 "'Yes, sir.'
011703 
011704 "'And what salary do you ask?'
011705 
011706 "'I had 4 pounds a month in my last place with Colonel Spence
011707 Munro.'
011708 
011709 "'Oh, tut, tut! sweating--rank sweating!' he cried, throwing his

011726 "You may imagine, Mr. Holmes, that to me, destitute as I was,

011807 "The manageress had sat all this while busy with her papers

011822 "Well, Mr. Holmes, when I got back to my lodgings and found

011835 here and I will read it to you:
011836 
011837                        "'The Copper Beeches, near Winchester.
011838 "'DEAR MISS HUNTER:--Miss Stoper has very kindly given me your
011839 address, and I write from here to ask you whether you have
011840 reconsidered your decision. My wife is very anxious that you
011841 should come, for she has been much attracted by my description of

011845 wife is fond of a particular shade of electric blue and would
011846 like you to wear such a dress indoors in the morning. You need
011847 not, however, go to the expense of purchasing one, as we have one
011848 belonging to my dear daughter Alice (now in Philadelphia), which
011849 would, I should think, fit you very well. Then, as to sitting
011850 here or there, or amusing yourself in any manner indicated, that
011851 need cause you no inconvenience. As regards your hair, it is no
011852 doubt a pity, especially as I could not help remarking its beauty
011853 during our short interview, but I am afraid that I must remain
011854 firm upon this point, and I only hope that the increased salary

011856 is concerned, are very light. Now do try to come, and I shall
011857 meet you with the dog-cart at Winchester. Let me know your train.

011859 
011860 "That is the letter which I have just received, Mr. Holmes, and
011861 my mind is made up that I will accept it. I thought, however,
011862 that before taking the final step I should like to submit the
011863 whole matter to your consideration."
011864 
011865 "Well, Miss Hunter, if your mind is made up, that settles the
011866 question," said Holmes, smiling.
011867 
011868 "But you would not advise me to refuse?"
011869 
011870 "I confess that it is not the situation which I should like to

011872 
011873 "What is the meaning of it all, Mr. Holmes?"
011874 
011875 "Ah, I have no data. I cannot tell. Perhaps you have yourself
011876 formed some opinion?"
011877 
011878 "Well, there seems to me to be only one possible solution. Mr.
011879 Rucastle seemed to be a very kind, good-natured man. Is it not
011880 possible that his wife is a lunatic, that he desires to keep the
011881 matter quiet for fear she should be taken to an asylum, and that

011884

011888

011890

011895 
011896 "I thought that if I told you the circumstances you would

011911

011918 
011919 "At least," said I as we heard her quick, firm steps descending

011922 
011923 "And she would need to be," said Holmes gravely. "I am much
011924 mistaken if we do not hear from her before many days are past."
011925 
011926 It was not very long before my friend's prediction was fulfilled.
011927 A fortnight went by, during which I frequently found my thoughts
011928 turning in her direction and wondering what strange side-alley of
011929 human experience this lonely woman had strayed into. The unusual
011930 salary, the curious conditions, the light duties, all pointed to
011931 something abnormal, though whether a fad or a plot, or whether
011932 the man were a philanthropist or a villain, it was quite beyond
011933 my powers to determine. As to Holmes, I observed that he sat
011934 frequently for half an hour on end, with knitted brows and an
011935 abstracted air, but he swept the matter away with a wave of his
011936 hand when I mentioned it. "Data! data! data!" he cried
011937 impatiently. "I can't make bricks without clay." And yet he would
011938 always wind up by muttering that no sister of his should ever
011939 have accepted such a situation.
011940 
011941 The telegram which we eventually received came late one night
011942 just as I was thinking of turning in and Holmes was settling down
011943 to one of those all-night chemical researches which he frequently
011944 indulged in, when I would leave him stooping over a retort and a
011945 test-tube at night and find him in the same position when I came
011946 down to breakfast in the morning. He opened the yellow envelope,
011947 and then, glancing at the message, threw it across to me.
011948 
011949 "Just look up the trains in Bradshaw," said he, and turned back
011950 to his chemical studies.
011951 
011952 The summons was a brief and urgent one.
011953 
011954 "Please be at the Black Swan Hotel at Winchester at midday
011955 to-morrow," it said. "Do come! I am at my wit's end.  HUNTER."
011956 
011957 "Will you come with me?" asked Holmes, glancing up.
011958 
011959 "I should wish to."
011960 
011961 "Just look it up, then."
011962 
011963 "There is a train at half-past nine," said I, glancing over my
011964 Bradshaw. "It is due at Winchester at 11:30."
011965 
011966 "That will do very nicely. Then perhaps I had better postpone my
011967 analysis of the acetones, as we may need to be at our best in the
011968 morning."
011969 
011970 By eleven o'clock the next day we were well upon our way to the
011971 old English capital. Holmes had been buried in the morning papers
011972 all the way down, but after we had passed the Hampshire border he
011973 threw them down and began to admire the scenery. It was an ideal
011974 spring day, a light blue sky, flecked with little fleecy white
011975 clouds drifting across from west to east. The sun was shining
011976 very brightly, and yet there was an exhilarating nip in the air,
011977 which set an edge to a man's energy. All over the countryside,
011978 away to the rolling hills around Aldershot, the little red and
011979 grey roofs of the farm-steadings peeped out from amid the light
011980 green of the new foliage.
011981 
011982 "Are they not fresh and beautiful?" I cried with all the
011983 enthusiasm of a man fresh from the fogs of Baker Street.
011984 
011985 But Holmes shook his head gravely.
011986 
011987 "Do you know, Watson," said he, "that it is one of the curses of
011988 a mind with a turn like mine that I must look at everything with
011989 reference to my own special subject. You look at these scattered
011990 houses, and you are impressed by their beauty. I look at them,
011991 and the only thought which comes to me is a feeling of their
011992 isolation and of the impunity with which crime may be committed
011993 there."
011994 
011995 "Good heavens!" I cried. "Who would associate crime with these
011996 dear old homesteads?"
011997 
011998 "They always fill me with a certain horror. It is my belief,
011999 Watson, founded upon my experience, that the lowest and vilest
012000 alleys in London do not present a more dreadful record of sin
012001 than does the smiling and beautiful countryside."
012002 
012003 "You horrify me!"
012004 
012005 "But the reason is very obvious. The pressure of public opinion
012006 can do in the town what the law cannot accomplish. There is no
012007 lane so vile that the scream of a tortured child, or the thud of
012008 a drunkard's blow, does not beget sympathy and indignation among
012009 the neighbours, and then the whole machinery of justice is ever
012010 so close that a word of complaint can set it going, and there is
012011 but a step between the crime and the dock. But look at these
012012 lonely houses, each in its own fields, filled for the most part
012013 with poor ignorant folk who know little of the law. Think of the
012014 deeds of hellish cruelty, the hidden wickedness which may go on,
012015 year in, year out, in such places, and none the wiser. Had this
012016 lady who appeals to us for help gone to live in Winchester, I
012017 should never have had a fear for her. It is the five miles of
012018 country which makes the danger. Still, it is clear that she is
012019 not personally threatened."
012020 
012021 "No. If she can come to Winchester to meet us she can get away."
012022 
012023 "Quite so. She has her freedom."
012024 
012025 "What CAN be the matter, then? Can you suggest no explanation?"
012026 
012027 "I have devised seven separate explanations, each of which would
012028 cover the facts as far as we know them. But which of these is
012029 correct can only be determined by the fresh information which we
012030 shall no doubt find waiting for us. Well, there is the tower of
012031 the cathedral, and we shall soon learn all that Miss Hunter has

012033 
012034 The Black Swan is an inn of repute in the High Street, at no
012035 distance from the station, and there we found the young lady
012036 waiting for us. She had engaged a sitting-room, and our lunch
012037 awaited us upon the table.
012038 
012039 "I am so delighted that you have come," she said earnestly. "It
012040 is so very kind of you both; but indeed I do not know what I
012041 should do. Your advice will be altogether invaluable to me."
012042 
012043 "Pray tell us what has happened to you."
012044 
012045 "I will do so, and I must be quick, for I have promised Mr.
012046 Rucastle to be back before three. I got his leave to come into
012047 town this morning, though he little knew for what purpose."
012048 
012049 "Let us have everything in its due order." Holmes thrust his long
012050 thin legs out towards the fire and composed himself to listen.
012051 
012052 "In the first place, I may say that I have met, on the whole,

012056 
012057 "What can you not understand?"
012058 
012059 "Their reasons for their conduct. But you shall have it all just
012060 as it occurred. When I came down, Mr. Rucastle met me here and
012061 drove me in his dog-cart to the Copper Beeches. It is, as he
012062 said, beautifully situated, but it is not beautiful in itself,

012070 front of the hall door has given its name to the place.
012071 
012072 "I was driven over by my employer, who was as amiable as ever,

012074 There was no truth, Mr. Holmes, in the conjecture which seemed to
012075 us to be probable in your rooms at Baker Street. Mrs. Rucastle is

012080 seven years, that he was a widower, and that his only child by
012081 the first wife was the daughter who has gone to Philadelphia. Mr.

012084 the daughter could not have been less than twenty, I can quite
012085 imagine that her position must have been uncomfortable with her
012086 father's young wife.
012087 
012088 "Mrs. Rucastle seemed to me to be colourless in mind as well as

012090 She was a nonentity. It was easy to see that she was passionately
012091 devoted both to her husband and to her little son. Her light grey
012092 eyes wandered continually from one to the other, noting every
012093 little want and forestalling it if possible. He was kind to her
012094 also in his bluff, boisterous fashion, and on the whole they

012099 her child which weighed upon her mind, for I have never met so
012100 utterly spoiled and so ill-natured a little creature. He is small
012101 for his age, with a head which is quite disproportionately large.
012102 His whole life appears to be spent in an alternation between

012104 pain to any creature weaker than himself seems to be his one idea

012109 
012110 "I am glad of all details," remarked my friend, "whether they
012111 seem to you to be relevant or not."
012112 
012113 "I shall try not to miss anything of importance. The one
012114 unpleasant thing about the house, which struck me at once, was

012116 man and his wife. Toller, for that is his name, is a rough,

012119 quite drunk, and yet Mr. Rucastle seemed to take no notice of it.

012125 
012126 "For two days after my arrival at the Copper Beeches my life was
012127 very quiet; on the third, Mrs. Rucastle came down just after
012128 breakfast and whispered something to her husband.
012129 
012130 "'Oh, yes,' said he, turning to me, 'we are very much obliged to

012137 
012138 "The dress which I found waiting for me was of a peculiar shade
012139 of blue. It was of excellent material, a sort of beige, but it
012140 bore unmistakable signs of having been worn before. It could not

012148 asked to sit, and then Mr. Rucastle, walking up and down on the
012149 other side of the room, began to tell me a series of the funniest
012150 stories that I have ever listened to. You cannot imagine how
012151 comical he was, and I laughed until I was quite weary. Mrs.
012152 Rucastle, however, who has evidently no sense of humour, never so
012153 much as smiled, but sat with her hands in her lap, and a sad,
012154 anxious look upon her face. After an hour or so, Mr. Rucastle
012155 suddenly remarked that it was time to commence the duties of the

012158 
012159 "Two days later this same performance was gone through under

012162 stories of which my employer had an immense rpertoire, and which
012163 he told inimitably. Then he handed me a yellow-backed novel, and

012169 
012170 "You can easily imagine, Mr. Holmes, how curious I became as to

012191 
012192 "'Jephro,' said she, 'there is an impertinent fellow upon the
012193 road there who stares up at Miss Hunter.'
012194 
012195 "'No friend of yours, Miss Hunter?' he asked.
012196 
012197 "'No, I know no one in these parts.'
012198 
012199 "'Dear me! How very impertinent! Kindly turn round and motion to
012200 him to go away.'
012201 
012202 "'Surely it would be better to take no notice.'
012203 
012204 "'No, no, we should have him loitering here always. Kindly turn

012206 
012207 "I did as I was told, and at the same instant Mrs. Rucastle drew

012211 
012212 "Pray continue," said Holmes. "Your narrative promises to be a
012213 most interesting one."
012214 
012215 "You will find it rather disconnected, I fear, and there may
012216 prove to be little relation between the different incidents of
012217 which I speak. On the very first day that I was at the Copper
012218 Beeches, Mr. Rucastle took me to a small outhouse which stands
012219 near the kitchen door. As we approached it I heard the sharp
012220 rattling of a chain, and the sound as of a large animal moving
012221 about.
012222 
012223 "'Look in here!' said Mr. Rucastle, showing me a slit between two
012224 planks. 'Is he not a beauty?'
012225 
012226 "I looked through and was conscious of two glowing eyes, and of a
012227 vague figure huddled up in the darkness.
012228 
012229 "'Don't be frightened,' said my employer, laughing at the start
012230 which I had given. 'It's only Carlo, my mastiff. I call him mine,
012231 but really old Toller, my groom, is the only man who can do
012232 anything with him. We feed him once a day, and not too much then,
012233 so that he is always as keen as mustard. Toller lets him loose
012234 every night, and God help the trespasser whom he lays his fangs
012235 upon. For goodness' sake don't you ever on any pretext set your
012236 foot over the threshold at night, for it's as much as your life
012237 is worth.'
012238 
012239 "The warning was no idle one, for two nights later I happened to
012240 look out of my bedroom window about two o'clock in the morning.
012241 It was a beautiful moonlight night, and the lawn in front of the
012242 house was silvered over and almost as bright as day. I was
012243 standing, rapt in the peaceful beauty of the scene, when I was
012244 aware that something was moving under the shadow of the copper
012245 beeches. As it emerged into the moonshine I saw what it was. It
012246 was a giant dog, as large as a calf, tawny tinted, with hanging
012247 jowl, black muzzle, and huge projecting bones. It walked slowly
012248 across the lawn and vanished into the shadow upon the other side.
012249 That dreadful sentinel sent a chill to my heart which I do not
012250 think that any burglar could have done.
012251 
012252 "And now I have a very strange experience to tell you. I had, as
012253 you know, cut off my hair in London, and I had placed it in a
012254 great coil at the bottom of my trunk. One evening, after the
012255 child was in bed, I began to amuse myself by examining the
012256 furniture of my room and by rearranging my own little things.
012257 There was an old chest of drawers in the room, the two upper ones
012258 empty and open, the lower one locked. I had filled the first two
012259 with my linen, and as I had still much to pack away I was
012260 naturally annoyed at not having the use of the third drawer. It
012261 struck me that it might have been fastened by a mere oversight,
012262 so I took out my bunch of keys and tried to open it. The very
012263 first key fitted to perfection, and I drew the drawer open. There
012264 was only one thing in it, but I am sure that you would never
012265 guess what it was. It was my coil of hair.
012266 
012267 "I took it up and examined it. It was of the same peculiar tint,
012268 and the same thickness. But then the impossibility of the thing
012269 obtruded itself upon me. How could my hair have been locked in
012270 the drawer? With trembling hands I undid my trunk, turned out the
012271 contents, and drew from the bottom my own hair. I laid the two
012272 tresses together, and I assure you that they were identical. Was
012273 it not extraordinary? Puzzle as I would, I could make nothing at
012274 all of what it meant. I returned the strange hair to the drawer,
012275 and I said nothing of the matter to the Rucastles as I felt that
012276 I had put myself in the wrong by opening a drawer which they had
012277 locked.
012278 
012279 "I am naturally observant, as you may have remarked, Mr. Holmes,
012280 and I soon had a pretty good plan of the whole house in my head.
012281 There was one wing, however, which appeared not to be inhabited
012282 at all. A door which faced that which led into the quarters of
012283 the Tollers opened into this suite, but it was invariably locked.
012284 One day, however, as I ascended the stair, I met Mr. Rucastle
012285 coming out through this door, his keys in his hand, and a look on
012286 his face which made him a very different person to the round,
012287 jovial man to whom I was accustomed. His cheeks were red, his
012288 brow was all crinkled with anger, and the veins stood out at his
012289 temples with passion. He locked the door and hurried past me
012290 without a word or a look.
012291 
012292 "This aroused my curiosity, so when I went out for a walk in the
012293 grounds with my charge, I strolled round to the side from which I
012294 could see the windows of this part of the house. There were four
012295 of them in a row, three of which were simply dirty, while the
012296 fourth was shuttered up. They were evidently all deserted. As I
012297 strolled up and down, glancing at them occasionally, Mr. Rucastle
012298 came out to me, looking as merry and jovial as ever.
012299 
012300 "'Ah!' said he, 'you must not think me rude if I passed you
012301 without a word, my dear young lady. I was preoccupied with
012302 business matters.'
012303 
012304 "I assured him that I was not offended. 'By the way,' said I,
012305 'you seem to have quite a suite of spare rooms up there, and one
012306 of them has the shutters up.'
012307 
012308 "He looked surprised and, as it seemed to me, a little startled
012309 at my remark.
012310 
012311 "'Photography is one of my hobbies,' said he. 'I have made my
012312 dark room up there. But, dear me! what an observant young lady we
012313 have come upon. Who would have believed it? Who would have ever
012314 believed it?' He spoke in a jesting tone, but there was no jest
012315 in his eyes as he looked at me. I read suspicion there and
012316 annoyance, but no jest.
012317 
012318 "Well, Mr. Holmes, from the moment that I understood that there
012319 was something about that suite of rooms which I was not to know,
012320 I was all on fire to go over them. It was not mere curiosity,
012321 though I have my share of that. It was more a feeling of duty--a
012322 feeling that some good might come from my penetrating to this
012323 place. They talk of woman's instinct; perhaps it was woman's
012324 instinct which gave me that feeling. At any rate, it was there,
012325 and I was keenly on the lookout for any chance to pass the
012326 forbidden door.
012327 
012328 "It was only yesterday that the chance came. I may tell you that,
012329 besides Mr. Rucastle, both Toller and his wife find something to
012330 do in these deserted rooms, and I once saw him carrying a large
012331 black linen bag with him through the door. Recently he has been
012332 drinking hard, and yesterday evening he was very drunk; and when
012333 I came upstairs there was the key in the door. I have no doubt at
012334 all that he had left it there. Mr. and Mrs. Rucastle were both
012335 downstairs, and the child was with them, so that I had an
012336 admirable opportunity. I turned the key gently in the lock,
012337 opened the door, and slipped through.
012338 
012339 "There was a little passage in front of me, unpapered and
012340 uncarpeted, which turned at a right angle at the farther end.
012341 Round this corner were three doors in a line, the first and third
012342 of which were open. They each led into an empty room, dusty and
012343 cheerless, with two windows in the one and one in the other, so
012344 thick with dirt that the evening light glimmered dimly through
012345 them. The centre door was closed, and across the outside of it
012346 had been fastened one of the broad bars of an iron bed, padlocked
012347 at one end to a ring in the wall, and fastened at the other with
012348 stout cord. The door itself was locked as well, and the key was
012349 not there. This barricaded door corresponded clearly with the
012350 shuttered window outside, and yet I could see by the glimmer from
012351 beneath it that the room was not in darkness. Evidently there was
012352 a skylight which let in light from above. As I stood in the
012353 passage gazing at the sinister door and wondering what secret it
012354 might veil, I suddenly heard the sound of steps within the room
012355 and saw a shadow pass backward and forward against the little
012356 slit of dim light which shone out from under the door. A mad,
012357 unreasoning terror rose up in me at the sight, Mr. Holmes. My
012358 overstrung nerves failed me suddenly, and I turned and ran--ran
012359 as though some dreadful hand were behind me clutching at the
012360 skirt of my dress. I rushed down the passage, through the door,
012361 and straight into the arms of Mr. Rucastle, who was waiting
012362 outside.
012363 
012364 "'So,' said he, smiling, 'it was you, then. I thought that it
012365 must be when I saw the door open.'
012366 
012367 "'Oh, I am so frightened!' I panted.
012368 
012369 "'My dear young lady! my dear young lady!'--you cannot think how
012370 caressing and soothing his manner was--'and what has frightened
012371 you, my dear young lady?'
012372 
012373 "But his voice was just a little too coaxing. He overdid it. I
012374 was keenly on my guard against him.
012375 
012376 "'I was foolish enough to go into the empty wing,' I answered.
012377 'But it is so lonely and eerie in this dim light that I was
012378 frightened and ran out again. Oh, it is so dreadfully still in
012379 there!'
012380 
012381 "'Only that?' said he, looking at me keenly.
012382 
012383 "'Why, what did you think?' I asked.
012384 
012385 "'Why do you think that I lock this door?'
012386 
012387 "'I am sure that I do not know.'
012388 
012389 "'It is to keep people out who have no business there. Do you
012390 see?' He was still smiling in the most amiable manner.
012391 
012392 "'I am sure if I had known--'
012393 
012394 "'Well, then, you know now. And if you ever put your foot over
012395 that threshold again'--here in an instant the smile hardened into
012396 a grin of rage, and he glared down at me with the face of a
012397 demon--'I'll throw you to the mastiff.'
012398 
012399 "I was so terrified that I do not know what I did. I suppose that
012400 I must have rushed past him into my room. I remember nothing
012401 until I found myself lying on my bed trembling all over. Then I
012402 thought of you, Mr. Holmes. I could not live there longer without
012403 some advice. I was frightened of the house, of the man, of the
012404 woman, of the servants, even of the child. They were all horrible
012405 to me. If I could only bring you down all would be well. Of
012406 course I might have fled from the house, but my curiosity was
012407 almost as strong as my fears. My mind was soon made up. I would
012408 send you a wire. I put on my hat and cloak, went down to the
012409 office, which is about half a mile from the house, and then
012410 returned, feeling very much easier. A horrible doubt came into my
012411 mind as I approached the door lest the dog might be loose, but I
012412 remembered that Toller had drunk himself into a state of
012413 insensibility that evening, and I knew that he was the only one
012414 in the household who had any influence with the savage creature,
012415 or who would venture to set him free. I slipped in in safety and
012416 lay awake half the night in my joy at the thought of seeing you.
012417 I had no difficulty in getting leave to come into Winchester this
012418 morning, but I must be back before three o'clock, for Mr. and
012419 Mrs. Rucastle are going on a visit, and will be away all the
012420 evening, so that I must look after the child. Now I have told you
012421 all my adventures, Mr. Holmes, and I should be very glad if you
012422 could tell me what it all means, and, above all, what I should
012423 do."
012424 
012425 Holmes and I had listened spellbound to this extraordinary story.
012426 My friend rose now and paced up and down the room, his hands in
012427 his pockets, and an expression of the most profound gravity upon
012428 his face.
012429 
012430 "Is Toller still drunk?" he asked.
012431 
012432 "Yes. I heard his wife tell Mrs. Rucastle that she could do
012433 nothing with him."
012434 
012435 "That is well. And the Rucastles go out to-night?"
012436 
012437 "Yes."
012438 
012439 "Is there a cellar with a good strong lock?"
012440 
012441 "Yes, the wine-cellar."
012442 
012443 "You seem to me to have acted all through this matter like a very
012444 brave and sensible girl, Miss Hunter. Do you think that you could
012445 perform one more feat? I should not ask it of you if I did not
012446 think you a quite exceptional woman."
012447 
012448 "I will try. What is it?"
012449 
012450 "We shall be at the Copper Beeches by seven o'clock, my friend
012451 and I. The Rucastles will be gone by that time, and Toller will,
012452 we hope, be incapable. There only remains Mrs. Toller, who might
012453 give the alarm. If you could send her into the cellar on some
012454 errand, and then turn the key upon her, you would facilitate
012455 matters immensely."
012456 
012457 "I will do it."
012458 
012459 "Excellent! We shall then look thoroughly into the affair. Of
012460 course there is only one feasible explanation. You have been
012461 brought there to personate someone, and the real person is
012462 imprisoned in this chamber. That is obvious. As to who this
012463 prisoner is, I have no doubt that it is the daughter, Miss Alice
012464 Rucastle, if I remember right, who was said to have gone to
012465 America. You were chosen, doubtless, as resembling her in height,
012466 figure, and the colour of your hair. Hers had been cut off, very
012467 possibly in some illness through which she has passed, and so, of
012468 course, yours had to be sacrificed also. By a curious chance you
012469 came upon her tresses. The man in the road was undoubtedly some
012470 friend of hers--possibly her fianc--and no doubt, as you wore
012471 the girl's dress and were so like her, he was convinced from your
012472 laughter, whenever he saw you, and afterwards from your gesture,
012473 that Miss Rucastle was perfectly happy, and that she no longer
012474 desired his attentions. The dog is let loose at night to prevent
012475 him from endeavouring to communicate with her. So much is fairly
012476 clear. The most serious point in the case is the disposition of
012477 the child."
012478 
012479 "What on earth has that to do with it?" I ejaculated.
012480 
012481 "My dear Watson, you as a medical man are continually gaining
012482 light as to the tendencies of a child by the study of the
012483 parents. Don't you see that the converse is equally valid. I have
012484 frequently gained my first real insight into the character of
012485 parents by studying their children. This child's disposition is
012486 abnormally cruel, merely for cruelty's sake, and whether he
012487 derives this from his smiling father, as I should suspect, or
012488 from his mother, it bodes evil for the poor girl who is in their
012489 power."
012490 
012491 "I am sure that you are right, Mr. Holmes," cried our client. "A
012492 thousand things come back to me which make me certain that you
012493 have hit it. Oh, let us lose not an instant in bringing help to
012494 this poor creature."
012495 
012496 "We must be circumspect, for we are dealing with a very cunning
012497 man. We can do nothing until seven o'clock. At that hour we shall
012498 be with you, and it will not be long before we solve the
012499 mystery."
012500 
012501 We were as good as our word, for it was just seven when we
012502 reached the Copper Beeches, having put up our trap at a wayside
012503 public-house. The group of trees, with their dark leaves shining
012504 like burnished metal in the light of the setting sun, were
012505 sufficient to mark the house even had Miss Hunter not been
012506 standing smiling on the door-step.
012507 
012508 "Have you managed it?" asked Holmes.
012509 
012510 A loud thudding noise came from somewhere downstairs. "That is
012511 Mrs. Toller in the cellar," said she. "Her husband lies snoring
012512 on the kitchen rug. Here are his keys, which are the duplicates
012513 of Mr. Rucastle's."
012514 
012515 "You have done well indeed!" cried Holmes with enthusiasm. "Now
012516 lead the way, and we shall soon see the end of this black
012517 business."
012518 
012519 We passed up the stair, unlocked the door, followed on down a
012520 passage, and found ourselves in front of the barricade which Miss
012521 Hunter had described. Holmes cut the cord and removed the
012522 transverse bar. Then he tried the various keys in the lock, but
012523 without success. No sound came from within, and at the silence
012524 Holmes' face clouded over.
012525 
012526 "I trust that we are not too late," said he. "I think, Miss
012527 Hunter, that we had better go in without you. Now, Watson, put
012528 your shoulder to it, and we shall see whether we cannot make our
012529 way in."
012530 
012531 It was an old rickety door and gave at once before our united
012532 strength. Together we rushed into the room. It was empty. There
012533 was no furniture save a little pallet bed, a small table, and a
012534 basketful of linen. The skylight above was open, and the prisoner
012535 gone.
012536 
012537 "There has been some villainy here," said Holmes; "this beauty
012538 has guessed Miss Hunter's intentions and has carried his victim
012539 off."
012540 
012541 "But how?"
012542 
012543 "Through the skylight. We shall soon see how he managed it." He
012544 swung himself up onto the roof. "Ah, yes," he cried, "here's the
012545 end of a long light ladder against the eaves. That is how he did
012546 it."
012547 
012548 "But it is impossible," said Miss Hunter; "the ladder was not
012549 there when the Rucastles went away."
012550 
012551 "He has come back and done it. I tell you that he is a clever and
012552 dangerous man. I should not be very much surprised if this were
012553 he whose step I hear now upon the stair. I think, Watson, that it
012554 would be as well for you to have your pistol ready."
012555 
012556 The words were hardly out of his mouth before a man appeared at
012557 the door of the room, a very fat and burly man, with a heavy
012558 stick in his hand. Miss Hunter screamed and shrunk against the
012559 wall at the sight of him, but Sherlock Holmes sprang forward and
012560 confronted him.
012561 
012562 "You villain!" said he, "where's your daughter?"
012563 
012564 The fat man cast his eyes round, and then up at the open
012565 skylight.
012566 
012567 "It is for me to ask you that," he shrieked, "you thieves! Spies
012568 and thieves! I have caught you, have I? You are in my power. I'll
012569 serve you!" He turned and clattered down the stairs as hard as he
012570 could go.
012571 
012572 "He's gone for the dog!" cried Miss Hunter.
012573 
012574 "I have my revolver," said I.
012575 
012576 "Better close the front door," cried Holmes, and we all rushed
012577 down the stairs together. We had hardly reached the hall when we
012578 heard the baying of a hound, and then a scream of agony, with a
012579 horrible worrying sound which it was dreadful to listen to. An
012580 elderly man with a red face and shaking limbs came staggering out
012581 at a side door.
012582 
012583 "My God!" he cried. "Someone has loosed the dog. It's not been
012584 fed for two days. Quick, quick, or it'll be too late!"
012585 
012586 Holmes and I rushed out and round the angle of the house, with
012587 Toller hurrying behind us. There was the huge famished brute, its
012588 black muzzle buried in Rucastle's throat, while he writhed and
012589 screamed upon the ground. Running up, I blew its brains out, and
012590 it fell over with its keen white teeth still meeting in the great
012591 creases of his neck. With much labour we separated them and
012592 carried him, living but horribly mangled, into the house. We laid
012593 him upon the drawing-room sofa, and having dispatched the sobered
012594 Toller to bear the news to his wife, I did what I could to
012595 relieve his pain. We were all assembled round him when the door
012596 opened, and a tall, gaunt woman entered the room.
012597 
012598 "Mrs. Toller!" cried Miss Hunter.
012599 
012600 "Yes, miss. Mr. Rucastle let me out when he came back before he
012601 went up to you. Ah, miss, it is a pity you didn't let me know
012602 what you were planning, for I would have told you that your pains
012603 were wasted."
012604 
012605 "Ha!" said Holmes, looking keenly at her. "It is clear that Mrs.
012606 Toller knows more about this matter than anyone else."
012607 
012608 "Yes, sir, I do, and I am ready enough to tell what I know."
012609 
012610 "Then, pray, sit down, and let us hear it for there are several
012611 points on which I must confess that I am still in the dark."
012612 
012613 "I will soon make it clear to you," said she; "and I'd have done
012614 so before now if I could ha' got out from the cellar. If there's
012615 police-court business over this, you'll remember that I was the
012616 one that stood your friend, and that I was Miss Alice's friend
012617 too.
012618 
012619 "She was never happy at home, Miss Alice wasn't, from the time
012620 that her father married again. She was slighted like and had no
012621 say in anything, but it never really became bad for her until
012622 after she met Mr. Fowler at a friend's house. As well as I could
012623 learn, Miss Alice had rights of her own by will, but she was so
012624 quiet and patient, she was, that she never said a word about them
012625 but just left everything in Mr. Rucastle's hands. He knew he was
012626 safe with her; but when there was a chance of a husband coming
012627 forward, who would ask for all that the law would give him, then
012628 her father thought it time to put a stop on it. He wanted her to
012629 sign a paper, so that whether she married or not, he could use
012630 her money. When she wouldn't do it, he kept on worrying her until
012631 she got brain-fever, and for six weeks was at death's door. Then
012632 she got better at last, all worn to a shadow, and with her
012633 beautiful hair cut off; but that didn't make no change in her
012634 young man, and he stuck to her as true as man could be."
012635 
012636 "Ah," said Holmes, "I think that what you have been good enough
012637 to tell us makes the matter fairly clear, and that I can deduce
012638 all that remains. Mr. Rucastle then, I presume, took to this
012639 system of imprisonment?"
012640 
012641 "Yes, sir."
012642 
012643 "And brought Miss Hunter down from London in order to get rid of
012644 the disagreeable persistence of Mr. Fowler."
012645 
012646 "That was it, sir."
012647 
012648 "But Mr. Fowler being a persevering man, as a good seaman should
012649 be, blockaded the house, and having met you succeeded by certain
012650 arguments, metallic or otherwise, in convincing you that your
012651 interests were the same as his."
012652 
012653 "Mr. Fowler was a very kind-spoken, free-handed gentleman," said
012654 Mrs. Toller serenely.
012655 
012656 "And in this way he managed that your good man should have no
012657 want of drink, and that a ladder should be ready at the moment
012658 when your master had gone out."
012659 
012660 "You have it, sir, just as it happened."
012661 
012662 "I am sure we owe you an apology, Mrs. Toller," said Holmes, "for
012663 you have certainly cleared up everything which puzzled us. And
012664 here comes the country surgeon and Mrs. Rucastle, so I think,
012665 Watson, that we had best escort Miss Hunter back to Winchester,
012666 as it seems to me that our locus standi now is rather a
012667 questionable one."
012668 
012669 And thus was solved the mystery of the sinister house with the
012670 copper beeches in front of the door. Mr. Rucastle survived, but
012671 was always a broken man, kept alive solely through the care of
012672 his devoted wife. They still live with their old servants, who
012673 probably know so much of Rucastle's past life that he finds it
012674 difficult to part from them. Mr. Fowler and Miss Rucastle were
012675 married, by special license, in Southampton the day after their
012676 flight, and he is now the holder of a government appointment in
012677 the island of Mauritius. As to Miss Violet Hunter, my friend
012678 Holmes, rather to my disappointment, manifested no further
012679 interest in her when once she had ceased to be the centre of one
012680 of his problems, and she is now the head of a private school at
012681 Walsall, where I believe that she has met with considerable success.
